| Chapter 1 | Functions of the |

| INTRODUCTION | Database Editor |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

1.18. DBE System Generation

The generation of DBE and its associated library of macros was intended to operate as simply as possible. During the initial Site generation, the system parameters such as buffer sizes and desired features are described in english-like source generation statements (for @SSG). If multiple versions of DBE are desired (for example one with and one without debugging code) then each version may be given a unique identifier (referred to as a class-id) for use during the generation process. At any point after that, the generation of a DBE system is as simple as entering one of the following SGS statements to @SSG:

 

GENERATE class-id: ALL MODULES

 

GENERATE class-id: ALL MODULES WITH TEMPORARY CORRECTIONS

 

GENERATE class-id: ALL MODULES WITH PERMANENT CORRECTIONS

 

GENERATE class-id: ALL MODULES WITH CORRECTIONS

The generation skeletons supplied with DBE will access the parameters defined for the given <class-id> and will generate the appropriate version of DBE. At the conclusion of the generation, DBE will generate a listing of the various system macros (supplied with DBE).

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 1 | DBE Operation Concepts |

| INTRODUCTION | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

1.19. DBE operation concepts

DBE operates as an interpretive processor in demand or batch mode. There is little internal difference between the command entered by the user or the command encountered within a macro. Macros are allowed to invoke other macros to virtually any desired depth as long as no macro is attempted to be executed in a recursive manner.

DBE maintains a fixed-length write-protected ibank and a fixed-length dbank table area in addition to a dynamically expandable dbank area (used to hold a schema, subschema or user dimensioned variables). At its smallest, DBE will occupy approximately 25k words. The maximum size DBE can attain depends directly on the size of any schema or subschema DBE is asked to load and the size of user arrays.

All contingency errors are trapped and all non-recoverable errors will cause an edited dump to be sent to the high-speed printer complex under a generation-defined banner id.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 2 | DBE Processor Call |

| DBE OPERATION | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

2. DBE Operation

2.1. Syntax of the DBE Processor Call

The Database Editor is called as follows:

 

@<DBE-file>.DBE[,<options>] [<spec1>][,<spec2>]

 

where <DBE-file> represents the Qual*Filename of the file in which the DBE absolute resides.

2.1.1 Spec Fields

The first spec field (<spec1>) is a filename in standard EXEC-8 format. If present, the @USE name of DBE$PF will be attached to it, thus making this file the user macro library. See the section on macros for more information.

The second spec field (<spec2>), if present, should be a non-zero positive integer. This will be used to specify that hardcopy should be generated to a TIP printer rather than to the on-site high-speed printers. The pid number of the TIP printer selected will be the value of <spec2>. Note that this feature will be available only for versions of DBE that have been configured for TIP. */Options

2.1.2 Options

 

 

 

 

A Accept errors in batch mode. This option (ignored in demand mode) will cause DBE to recover from DBE-detected errors (not contingency errors) should they occur. The normal action for batch jobs in this case is for DBE to be terminated. Macros will still be terminated

 

B Brief mode is wanted. Only output from the following commands will be printed:

 

LIST

OUTPUT

PRINT

WRITE

 

C Simulate console I/O at the terminal. This is useful for debugging macros which do I/O involving the system console. If this option is on, the output to the console will appear at the terminal in the form:

 

****CONSOLE:

<output>

If the operator was to respond, the terminal operator may then enter the desired response.

 

D This option is used to declare the user to be in 'demand' mode. Its effect will be to set the system variable 'MODE' to zero rather than to one. This option may be turned 'OFF' via the DBE 'OFF' command (thus simulating batch mode) even if it was not explicitly turned 'ON'. See the section on 'Processor Operation' in this chapter for more information.

 

E Disable the KEYIN$ handler. This option is only valid on the DBE processor call.

 

F Run at REALTIME priority. The level of realtime as well as the ability to run realtime is controlled via a DBE sysgen parameter.

 

G Do not print DBE processor identification signon or signoff messages.

 

H A hardcopy duplicate of all DBE-produced printout will be sent to the current hardcopy device when this option is on. See the 'HARDCOPY' command for more information.

 

I Not used by DBE - reserved for site definition.

 

J Not used by DBE - reserved for site definition.

 

K Not used by DBE - reserved for site definition.

 

L Not used by DBE - reserved for site definition.

 

M Not used by DBE - reserved for site definition.

 

N No printing (except for error messages) will appear at the terminal. This can be used in conjunction with the 'H' option to simulate a '@BRKPT' situation. Since option letters can be manipulated via the 'ON' and 'OFF' commands, the user can write macros that, in effect, do breakpoints. (See the 'SITE' and 'SEND' macros.) Should an error occur within a macro while the 'N' option is in effect, errors deemed as "recoverable" (see Appendix A) will not have their messages printed. This gives the macro writer the ability to suppress messages that are of a warning nature.

 

O Not used.

 

P Cause PAUSE macro to act as if in batch mode.

 

Q Have DECODE function return a result of zero instead of erroring when an invalid area code is processed.

 

R Reverse the order in which the macro library files are searched. See the chapter on macros for more information.

 

S Suppress the printing of DBE system news at DBE sign-on time. This is useful when calling DBE within @ADD runstreams. See the 'NEWS' macro for more information.

This option cannot be manipulated via the 'ON' and 'OFF' commands.

 

T Trace conversational mode commands as they are input, whether keyed from a terminal or @ADD'ed. Note that commands executed by a macro can only be traced using the 'TRACE' command in DEBUG mode.

 

U Not used.

 

V Not used.

 

W Not used.

 

X Abort DBE if DBE-detected errors occur. This option (ignored by batch runs) allows the demand user to, in effect, become a batch job as far as error-handling is concerned.

 

Y 'AREA' commands will reference training mode areas.

 

Z Used for debugging purposes only. *//

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 2 | DBE Processor Operation |

| DBE OPERATION | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

 

2.2. Processor Operation

The behavior of certain commands and system macros will be altered depending upon the mode of DBE operation (demand versus batch). This altered behavior is basically limited to the DBE-assumed print width of the device used for output. When in demand mode, DBE will assume the device in use to be limited to 72 columns while when in batch mode a limit of 132 will be used. This will influence the following commands:

 

- PRINT

- PRINT# (#=EXCLAMATION POINT)

- OUTPUT

- HISTOGRAM

and the following system macros:

 

- DATA

- DUMPREC

- PGDUMP

- R$SCAN

- SCAN-ONE

- SCAN-ALL

- SIZE-REPORT

- TOC

The following logic controls DBE's determination of whether or not a user is running in demand or batch mode:

 

1. The EXEC-supplied indicator is used to make a preliminary determination of demand/batch status.

 

2. If the user is found to be operating in @BRKPT mode, the mode will be set to 'batch' (regardless of the outcome of #1).

 

3. Finally, if the 'D' option is supplied, the user will be assumed to be in 'demand' mode (regardless of the outcomes of #1 or #2).

At any time during the DBE session the 'D' option may be turned off (via the OFF command) to simulate 'batch' mode or turned on (via the ON command) to simulate 'demand' mode.

The system variable MODE will always contain a value indicating the most-current mode status, zero for demand and one for batch. This variable may be used by user macros needing to know the mode of operation.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 2 | Variables and Tables |

| DBE OPERATION | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

 

2.3. Variables and Tables

Certain DBE commands will, as a side-effect of their operation, cause certain DBE "tables" to be defined. For example, the DBE PAGE command will define a table called "PAGE", which will be the contents of a page from the database you are currently accessing. Tables are generally used by macros although the user may "browse" through them by using the "buffer positioning commands" described later in this manual. Section 1.3 shows some of the available tables.

Consult the DBE programmer's reference manual for more information on tables and variables.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 2 | Arithmetic and Logical |

| DBE OPERATION | Expressions |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

 

 

 

2.4. Arithmetic and Logical Expressions

Most DBE commands will make use of arithmetic or logical expressions. These are formed according to rules similar to most conventional programming languages, but will have some extensions peculiar to DBE. For a detailed discussion on expressions, consult the DBE programmer's reference manual.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 2 | Table and Array |

| DBE OPERATION | Subsets |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

 

 

 

2.5. Subsets (Table or Array)

Many DBE commands allow the use of an array or table subset. This is a technique whereby all or a portion of a DBE table or user array may be referenced as a single entity. The use of subsets is generally applicable mainly to statements within a macro, so a detailed discussion of them will be deferred to the DBE programmer's reference manual.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 2 | Definition of a Command |

| DBE OPERATION | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

 

2.6. Commands

All DBE commands are in the format

 

<command>,<options> <parameters>

Many command names may be abbrievated. Options and parameters (seperated by commas) are optional and are dependent on the particular command selected.

 

There are two special-purpose command forms that may be used within a macro: array/table subset commands and write-buffer commands. Consult the DBE programmer's reference manual for more information.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 2 | Definition of a Function |

| DBE OPERATION | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

 

2.7. Functions

The DBE 'LET' command supports a variety of hardcoded 'functions' which may be invoked to perform certain services. Functions have one or more parameters enclosed within parenthesis following their names and may be used only on the LET command (not within arithmetic expressions as with FORTRAN, etc.). Consult the DBE programmers reference manual for more information.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 2 | Definition of a Macro |

| DBE OPERATION | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

 

2.8. Macros

DBE macros are defined as source elements in the DBE system macro library or in a user file supplied as the first spec field of the DBE processor call or as in-core "programs" defined via the 'MACRO' command.

Documentation on the various system macros and their use will appear in a later chapter of this manual. Information on the creation and maintenance of macros will be found in the DBE Programmer's Reference Manual.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 3 | Introduction |

| DMS / RDMS TABLE ACCESS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

3. Schema/Subschema/Database Oriented Commands

This class of DBE commands is responsible for all accesses to Schema , subschema AND RDMS tables as well as database pages. These commands are all built to automatically do a TIP-connect, 'ER DM$IOW' and TIP-disconnect in order to read information from TIP files.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 3 | 'AREA' Command |

| DMS / RDMS TABLE ACCESS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*/AREA

3.1. AREA Command

3.1.1 Abbreviations

This command may be abbreviated to 'A'.

3.1.2 Syntax

1. AREA[,<options>] <area specification>

2. AREA

3.1.3 Purpose

Locate the Area Reference Table [ART] for the selected area within the Schema Reference Table [SCRT]. If found, assign the area file to the user's run (EXEC areas only) and read in page zero (DARP areas only). All subsequent PAGE, COUNT and DMSCALC (the function, not the macro) requests will refer to this area.

3.1.4 Options

None The 'AREA' command will make available the Area Reference Table and database pages for the area. If an EXEC area, the correct qualifier must already have been defined to DBE (see the section on the 'QUAL' command), and if a TIP area, the file must be TPASG'd. If the area is not available, a message explaining the problem will be printed; however, the table 'ART', the system variables 'ASEQ' and 'ACODE', and possibly other related tables and variables will be accurately updated.

 

N The area name and code will not be printed when the area is made current.

 

P The 'AREA' command will make available the Area Reference Table only. No attempt will be made to access or even verify the existence of the actual area on disc. This is the recommended mode of access to the Area Reference Table when no actual access to the database itself is required.

3.1.5 Format 1

The value of the <area specification> is expected to be one of the following:

 

1. The name of the area to be selected.

 

2. The code of the area to be selected. This code may be an integer number or an expression.

 

3. A "pound-sign" (#) followed by an expression.

If the expression evaluates to a non-zero positive result, the area will be selected by absolute sequence number within the Schema Reference Table. Thus, #1 selects the first, #2 the second, and so forth. Areas will be defined in the schema in ascending order of area code.

If the expression evaluates to zero, any area tables (ART, PAGE, etc.) previously accessible will be made unavailable to the user. This corresponds to the state of an area following a 'SCHEMA' command. This state is useful when it is desired that a macro that utilizes the 'AREA +1' command start with the first area in a schema.

 

4. A "plus-sign" (+) followed by an expression evaluating to a non-zero positive result. This selects an area by relative sequence number within the Schema Reference Table in relation to the current area. Thus, +1 selects the "next" area in the schema. Note, however, that if the resultant relative area number is zero, the error "AREA NOT FOUND" will result (compare to the 'AREA #0' command).

 

5. A "minus-sign" (-) followed by an expression evaluating to a non-zero positive result. This also selects an area by relative sequence number (but in a backwards manner). Thus, -1 selects the "previous" area. Note, however, that if the resultant relative area number is zero, the error "AREA NOT FOUND" will result (compare to the 'AREA #0' command).

 

6. An array/table subset expected to contain a character string which corresponds syntactically to one of the five previous formats.

3.1.6 Discussion

If the area requested is the same as the area which is current, the 'AREA' command will be ignored. An exception to this rule is when the previous area request had either been terminated in error, or the previous area request had been an 'AREA,P' and you are now requesting complete use of the area; under these circumstances the command is honored.

If the 'N' option is not present on the 'AREA' command, when the ART has been located, the DBE-determined filename (or TIP/DMS file code) will be printed. Note that in the case where the area file is determined to be an EXEC area, a qualifier will be needed in addition to the area name (used as the filename). This qualifier is to be supplied by the 'QUAL' command.

If a subschema is current at the time of the 'AREA' command, the 'SART' table corresponding to the area selected will be made current (if it is included in the subschema).

If the DBE 'Y' option is on, the 'AREA' command pertains to the training area requested. If the requested area does not have an associated training area, the command will refer to the production area requested. The DBE system variable 'TRAIN' will be set when the current area is a training area.

3.1.7 Format 2

Format 2 will print the following information about the current area:

 

Area code and name

Area filename

Schema name

Schema filename

3.1.8 Affected Entities

As a result of this command, the following tables will be affected:

 

ACT

ART

CSLOT

P0

PAGE

PH

RSLOT

SART

TREG

and the following system variables will be affected:

 

ACODE

AREAP

ASEQ

DMSDTS

MAXPG

NCSLOT

NRSLOT

SCANTOTALIO^

TRAIN

TABLE : No table will be current if the previous table was PAGE, PH, CSLOT, or RSLOT. Previous table remains current otherwise.

TSIZE : Set to zero if the previous table was PAGE, PH, CSLOT, or RSLOT. Reflects new size if previous table was ACT, ART, P0, SART, or TREG. Unchanged otherwise.

$ : Set to zero if the previous table was ACT, ART, P0, SART, or TREG; PAGE, PH, CSLOT, or RSLOT.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 3 | 'FEATURE' Command |

| DMS / RDMS TABLE ACCESS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */FEATURE

3.2. FEATURE Command

 

3.2.1 Abbreviations

This command may be abbreviated to 'FEA'.

3.2.2 Syntax

1. FEATURE <feature specification>

2. FEATURE

3.2.3 Purpose

Locate a given feature's Reference Table and, if applicable, its Description Table, in the schema and make them available under the table names FRT and GED.

3.2.4 Format 1

The value of the <feature specification> is expected to be one of the following:

 

1. The code of the feature to be selected. This code may be an integer number or an expression.

 

2. A "pound-sign" (#) followed by an expression.

If the expression evaluates to a non-zero positive result, the feature will be selected by absolute sequence number within the Schema Reference Table. Thus, #1 selects the first, #2 the second, and so forth. Features will be defined in the schema in ascending order of feature code.

If the expression evaluates to zero, any feature tables (FRT, GED, etc.) previously accessible will be made unavailable to the user. This corresponds to the state of a feature following a 'SCHEMA' command. This state is useful when it is desired that a macro that utilizes the 'FEATURE +1' command start with the first feature in a schema.

 

3. A "plus-sign" (+) followed by an expression evaluating to a non-zero positive result. This selects an feature by relative sequence number within the Schema Reference Table in relation to the current feature. Thus, +1 selects the "next" feature in the schema. Note, however, that if the resultant relative feature number is zero, the error "FEATURE NOT FOUND" will result (compare to the 'FEATURE #0' command).

 

4. A "minus-sign" (-) followed by an expression evaluating to a non-zero positive result. This also selects a feature by relative sequence number (but in a backwards manner). Thus, -1 selects the "previous" feature. Note, however, that if the resultant relative feature number is zero, the error "FEATURE NOT FOUND" will result (compare to the 'FEATURE #0' command).

 

5. An array/table subset expected to contain a character string which corresponds syntactically to one of the four previous formats.

3.2.5 Discussion

Feature Reference Tables exist for 3 things:

- Database Procedures (including DMSCALC, RANDENTIAL, etc.) used in the schema. These are defined in feature #1.

- Global Encode/Decode Tables (GED's), which are created whenever encoding is specified in the schema. These are defined as features numbered 2 and up. When such a feature is selected by the 'FEATURE' command, the GED table corresponding to the selected FRT is made current under the table name "GED".

- Record Feature Tables (RFT's), which are created whenever a record uses special features. These features are numbered as the record code plus 010000.

3.2.6 Format 2

Format 2 will print the following information about the current feature:

 

Feature code (FCODE)

Feature sequence number (FSEQ)

Schema name

Schema filename

3.2.7 Affected Entities

As a result of this command, the following tables will be affected:

 

FRT

GED

and the following system variables will be affected:

 

FCODE

FSEQ

TABLE : Previous table remains current.

TSIZE : Reflects new size if previous table was FRT or GED.

$ : Set to zero if the previous table was FRT or GED.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 3 | 'PAGE' Command |

| DMS / RDMS TABLE ACCESS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */PAGE

3.3. PAGE Command

 

3.3.1 Abbreviations

This command may be abbreviated to 'PG'.

3.3.2 Syntax

1. PAGE [#]<expression>

2. PAGE +<expression>

3. PAGE -<expression>

4. PAGE <array subset>

5. PAGE,R

6. PAGE

3.3.3 Purpose

Read a database page into a DBE buffer and make it available for inspection by the user via the buffer-oriented commands.

3.3.4 Options

X Allows access to a page even if the page number is outside the range reflected in the area's DAE (Page 0) information.

3.3.5 Discussion

Format 1 will read in the page whose number is the value of the <expression>. The area involved will be the area last referred to on an 'AREA' command. In format 1, the result of the <expression> cannot exceed the maximum page number in the area (see the 'X' option on the 'PAGE' command for an exception.) The optional '#' is allowed to produce compatibility with other table-handling commands and is not actually required; 'PAGE 5' and 'PAGE #5' will produce identical results (both load page five of the current area).

Formats 2 and 3 use the result of <expression> as a relative indication of the desired page. For example, 'PAGE +1' would read the next page from the current one while 'PAGE -2' would read the page located two pages earlier. In both of these formats the value of <expression> added to (or subtracted from) the current page number must result in a legal page number for the current area.

Format 4 allows a character string (within an array subset) to be supplied as a parameter to the command by a macro. The contents of the subset should be a syntactically legal 'PAGE' command parameter.

Format 5 will cause the current page to be re-read from mass-storage.

Format 6 will print the following information about the current page:

 

Page number

Area code and name

Area filename

Schema name

Schema filename

To provide ease-of-use, if a 'PAGE' command is executed in conversational mode (i.e., not from a macro) and no other table is current, the table 'PAGE' will automatically be made current.

3.3.6 Affected Entities

As a result of this command, the following tables will be affected:

 

CSLOT

PAGE

PH

RSLOT

and the following system variables will be affected:

 

NCSLOT

NRSLOT

PGNUM

TABLE (if old table was CSLOT, PAGE, PH, RSLOT)

TSIZE (if old table was CSLOT, PAGE, PH, RSLOT)

$ (if old table was CSLOT, PAGE, PH, RSLOT)

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 3 | 'PATH' Command |

| DMS / RDMS TABLE ACCESS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */PATH

3.4. PATH Command

3.4.1 Abbreviations

This command may not be abbreviated.

3.4.2 Syntax

1. PATH <path-name>

2. PATH <path-seq-num>

3. PATH #<path-seq-num>

4. PATH +expression

5. PATH -expression

6. PATH

3.4.3 Purpose

Locate a given path's Path Index Table and Path Description Table in the subschema and make them available under the table names of PIT and PDT.

3.4.4 Options

D Find next duplicate path entry.

3.4.5 Discussion

The <path-specification> in formats 1 to 5 operate consistent with the 'AREA' command. However, a QLP path is not assigned a path-code in the subschema definition language (symbolic element) but is given its sequence number dynamically during subschema compilation. (This sequence number may be used for path selection via formats 2 through 5). All absolute/relative path selection will select a path by its position in the Path Index Table [PIT]. Please note that the position of a path within the PIT will not necessarily coincide with the physical order of the paths in the subschema source code. The special case of 'PATH #0' (see format 3) will rebase the pointers to both the Path Index Table and the Path Description Table to the header word and thus will make no path current. This is the original state prior to the issuing of a 'PATH' command. This is useful for determining the number of path entries (see H2 of PIT header word zero).

The 'D' option on the 'PATH' command will find the next PIT and PDT entry whose path name equals that of the current path. The search ends when the end of the Path Index Table is reached; a duplicate path name whose sequence number is less than the current path will not be found. If no duplicate is found, the previous path will remain current.

Format 5 will print information about the current path.

3.4.6 Affected Entities

As a result of this command, the following tables will be affected:

 

PDT

PIT

and the following system variables will be affected:

 

PSEQ

TABLE (if old table was PDT or PIT)

TSIZE (if old table was PDT or PIT)

$ (if old table was PDT or PIT)

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 3 | 'QUAL' Command |

| DMS / RDMS TABLE ACCESS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */QUAL

3.5. QUAL Command

3.5.1 Abbreviations

This command may not be abbreviated.

3.5.2 Syntax

1. QUAL <qualifier>

2. QUAL

3.5.3 Purpose

Establishes the qualifier to be used by the 'AREA' command when attempting to access EXEC areas. This is needed only if EXEC areas are being accessed since TIP areas are referred to only by file code.

3.5.4 Options

P Set the qualifier to the project-id of the run.

3.5.5 Discussion

Format 1 sets the qualifier to the given value. The qualifier supplied on this format is not checked for syntactical form; it will not be detected as being an illegally formatted qualifier until an AREA command attempts to do a dynamic assign (via ER CSF$) of the file using the qualifier and filename of the area. At this time the 'AREA' command would error. Take care that there are no erroneous symbols in the qualifier.

Format 2 displays the qualifier currently in effect.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 3 | 'RAP' Command |

| DMS / RDMS TABLE ACCESS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */RAP

3.6. RAP Command

3.6.1 Abbreviations

This command may not be abbreviated.

3.6.2 Syntax

1. RAP [#]<expression>

2. RAP +expression

3. RAP -expression

4. RAP

3.6.3 Purpose

Load the RAP table with one of the Allocation Pages from the current RDMS area.

3.6.4 Discussion

Format 1 will base the allocation page whose number is the value of the <expression>. In format 1, the result of the <expression> cannot exceed the allocation page number for that area. The optional '#' is allowed to produce compatibility with other table-handling commands and is not actually required; 'RAP 2' and 'RAP #2' will produce identical results (both load allocation page two of the current area).

Formats 2 and 3 use the result of <expression> as a relative indication of the desired allocation page. For example, 'RAP +1' would base the next allocation page from the current one while 'RAP -2' would base the allocation page located two pages earlier. In both of these formats the value of <expression> added to (or subtracted from) the current allocation page number must result in a legal allocation page number for the current area.

Format 4 will print the current Allocation Page number and RDMS area name.

3.6.5 Affected Entities

As a result of this command, the following tables will be affected:

 

RAP

and the following system variables will be affected:

 

RAPNUM

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 3 | 'RAREA' Command |

| DMS / RDMS TABLE ACCESS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */RAREA

3.7. RAREA Command

3.7.1 Abbreviations

This command may not be abbreviated.

3.7.2 Syntax

1. RAREA <TIP-CODE>

2. RAREA <QUALIFIER*EXEC-FILE-NAME>

2. RAREA

3.7.3 Purpose

Assigns the RDMS area to the user's run (EXEC areas only) and reads in the File Control Page and Allocation pages.

3.7.4 Discussion

Format 1 selects a UDS/TIP file as the current RDMS area.

Format 2 selects an EXEC file as the current RDMS area. Note that both qualifier and file name are required.

Format 3 will display the current RDMS area (if any) and area type (DATA, DATA/INDEX,INDEX).

3.7.5 Affected Entities

As a result of this command, the following tables will be affected:

 

RP1

RFCP

RAP

RPAGE

RPH

RRSLOT

and the following system variables will be affected:

 

RAFILE

RAPNUM

RBTCNT

RFPAGE

RLSTPG

RMAXPG

RNSLOT

RPGNUM

 

TABLE : No table will be current if the previous table was RPAGE, RPH or RRSLOT. Previous table remains current otherwise.

TSIZE : Set to zero if the previous table was RPAGE, RPH or RRSLOT.

$ : Set to zero if the previous table was RPAGE, RPH, RRSLOT, RP1, RFCP , RAP.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 3 | 'RPAGE' Command |

| DMS / RDMS TABLE ACCESS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */RPAGE

3.8. RPAGE Command

3.8.1 Abbreviations

This command may not be abbreviated.

3.8.2 Syntax

1. RPAGE [#]<expression>

2. RPAGE +<expression>

3. RPAGE -<expression>

4. RPAGE <array subset>

5. RPAGE,R

6. RPAGE

3.8.3 Purpose

Read an RDMS database page into a DBE buffer and make it available for inspection by the user via the buffer-oriented commands.

3.8.4 Options

X Allows access to a page even if the page number is outside the highest allocated.

3.8.5 Discussion

Format 1 will read in the page whose number is the value of the <expression>. The RDMS area involved will be the area last referred to on an 'RAREA' command. In format 1, the result of the <expression> cannot exceed the maximum page number in the area (see the 'X' option on the 'RPAGE' command for an exception.) The optional '#' is allowed to produce compatibility with other table-handling commands and is not actually required; 'RPAGE 5' and 'RPAGE #5' will produce identical results (both load page five of the current RDMS area).

Formats 2 and 3 use the result of <expression> as a relative indication of the desired page. For example, 'RPAGE +1' would read the next page from the current one while 'RPAGE -2' would read the page located two pages earlier. In both of these formats the value of <expression> added to (or subtracted from) the current page number must result in a legal page number for the current area.

Format 4 allows a character string (within an array subset) to be supplied as a parameter to the command by a macro. The contents of the subset should be a syntactically legal 'RPAGE' command parameter.

Format 5 will cause the current page to be re-read from mass-storage.

Format 6 will print the following information about the current page:

 

Page number

RDMS Area name

To provide ease-of-use, if a 'RPAGE' command is executed in conversational mode (i.e., not from a macro) and no other table is current, the table 'RPAGE' will automatically be made current.

3.8.6 Affected Entities

As a result of this command, the following tables will be affected:

 

RPAGE

RPH

RRSLOT

and the following system variables will be affected:

 

RNSLOT

RPGNUM

TABLE (if old table was RPAGE, RPH, RRSLOT)

TSIZE (if old table was RPAGE, RPH, RRSLOT)

$ (if old table was RPAGE, RPH, RRSLOT)

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 3 | 'RECORD' Command |

| DMS / RDMS TABLE ACCESS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */RECORD

3.9. RECORD Command

 

3.9.1 Abbreviations

This command may be abbreviated to 'REC'.

3.9.2 Syntax

1. RECORD <record specification>

2. RECORD

3.9.3 Purpose

Locate a given record's Reference and Description Tables in the schema and make them available under the table names RRT and RDT.

3.9.4 Format 1

The value of the <record specification> is expected to be one of the following:

 

1. The name of the record to be selected.

 

2. The code of the record to be selected. This code may be an integer number or an expression.

 

3. A "pound-sign" (#) followed by an expression.

If the expression evaluates to a non-zero positive result, the record will be selected by absolute sequence number within the Schema Reference Table. Thus, #1 selects the first, #2 the second, and so forth. Records will be defined in the schema in ascending order of record code.

If the expression evaluates to zero, any record tables (RRT, RDT, etc.) previously accessible will be made unavailable to the user. This corresponds to the state of a record following a 'SCHEMA' command. This state is useful when it is desired that a macro that utilizes the 'RECORD +1' command start with the first record in a schema.

 

4. A "plus-sign" (+) followed by an expression evaluating to a non-zero positive result. This selects an record by relative sequence number within the Schema Reference Table in relation to the current record. Thus, +1 selects the "next" record in the schema. Note, however, that if the resultant relative record number is zero, the error "RECORD NOT FOUND" will result (compare to the 'RECORD #0' command).

 

5. A "minus-sign" (-) followed by an expression evaluating to a non-zero positive result. This also selects a record by relative sequence number (but in a backwards manner). Thus, -1 selects the "previous" record. Note, however, that if the resultant relative record number is zero, the error "RECORD NOT FOUND" will result (compare to the 'RECORD #0' command).

 

6. An array/table subset expected to contain a character string which corresponds syntactically to one of the five previous formats.

3.9.5 Discussion

If a subschema is current at the time of the 'RECORD' command, the 'SRRT' table corresponding to the record selected will be made current (if it is included in the subschema).

3.9.6 Format 2

Format 2 will print the following information about the current record:

 

Record code and name

Schema name

Schema filename

3.9.7 Affected Entities

As a result of this command, the following tables will be affected:

 

RDT

RRT

and the following system variables will be affected:

 

RCODE

RSEQ

TABLE (if old table was RDT or RRT)

$ (if old table was RDT or RRT)

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 3 | 'SCHEMA' Command |

| DMS / RDMS TABLE ACCESS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */SCHEMA

3.10. SCHEMA Command

3.10.1 Abbreviations

This command may be abbreviated to 'SCH'.

3.10.2 Syntax

1. SCHEMA <file>.<elt>[/<version>] [<schema-name>]

2. SCHEMA,T <tip-file-code> <elt>[/<version>] [<schema-name>]

3. SCHEMA,L <file>.<elt>[/<version>] [<schema-name>]

4. SCHEMA

3.10.3 Purpose

Loads an absolute schema element into an internal DBE buffer and makes it available for inspection or for use by the other commands in this section.

3.10.4 Format 1

This format is used when the absolute schema is to be loaded from an EXEC-8 file. <File> is a standard EXEC-8 file name in the format Qual*File(F-cycle)/Read-key/Write-key.

<Elt> is a standard element name (minus elt-cycle).

<Version> is a standard version name.

<Schema-name> is the name specified in the SCHEMA NAME IS clause of the symbolic schema element of the schema to be loaded.

The <file>.<elt>/<version> specifies the location of the schema while the <schema-name> specifies its name (from the DMR's point of view). If the <schema-name> should be the same as <elt> (as will be the case most of the time), then it need not be supplied.

3.10.5 Format 2

This format is used when the absolute schema is to be loaded from a TIP file. <Tip-file-code> is any expression evaluating to a non-negative and non-zero result.

If the desired schema contains a LOCK FOR COPY, the user will be asked to supply it. If the user fails to exactly match the lock, access to the schema will be denied.

Note: If the user access bit 'Ignore Locks' is set than the user will not be asked to supply the Copy Lock.

3.10.6 Format 3

Format 3 will load a schema absolute from an EXEC-8 file as in format 1 above. After loading, if the schema is defined as a Tip Schema, it will then be reloaded from the Tip file identified in the schema absolute.

3.10.7 Format 4

Format 4 will print the following information about the current schema:

 

Schema name

Schema filename

The user should be aware that DBE can be generated in one of two ways as far as schema access is concerned. The first calls for the entire schema to be available in-core following successful execution of this command. The second calls for only the "FDT" and "SCRT" portion of a schema to be loaded. This method can significantly reduce the memory usage of DBE (as well as allow larger schemas to be accessed) by not loading in the various record and set description tables until needed; the 'RECORD' and 'SET' commands will load the appropriate description tables, when necessary. The user should notice only the following two differences between the two types of access modes:

 

1. When the full schema is being read, the 'FDT', 'SRT', 'RDT' and 'SDT' tables will be unavailable on the 'REWRITE' command. The table 'SCHEMA' will exist and will be available.

 

2. When only the FDT/SCRT portions of the schema are being read, the table 'SCHEMA' will not exist and the 'FDT', 'SCRT', 'RDT' and 'SDT' tables will be allowed on the 'REWRITE' command.

3.10.8 Affected Entities

As a result of this command, the following tables will be affected:

 

All tables except 'IOBUF'.

and the following system variables will be affected:

 

ACODE

ASEQ

MAXPG

NCSLOT

NRSLOT

PGNUM

PSEQ

RCODE

RSEQ

SCHLEV

SCODE

SSEQ

TABLE (unless old table was 'IOBUF')

TSIZE (unless old table was 'IOBUF')

$ (unless old table was 'IOBUF')

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 3 | 'SET' Command |

| DMS / RDMS TABLE ACCESS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */SET

3.11. SET Command

3.11.1 Abbreviations

This command cannot be abbreviated.

3.11.2 Syntax

1. SET <set specification>

2. SET

3.11.3 Purpose

Locate a given set's Reference and Description Tables in the schema and make them available under the table names 'SRT' and 'SDT'.

3.11.4 Format 1

The value of the <set specification> is expected to be one of the following:

 

1. The name of the set to be selected.

 

2. The code of the set to be selected. This code may be an integer number or an expression.

 

3. A "pound-sign" (#) followed by an expression.

If the expression evaluates to a non-zero positive result, the set will be selected by absolute sequence number within the Schema Reference Table. Thus, #1 selects the first, #2 the second, and so forth. Sets will be defined in the schema in ascending order of set code.

If the expression evaluates to zero, any set tables (SRT, SDT, etc.) previously accessible will be made unavailable to the user. This corresponds to the state of a set following a 'SCHEMA' command. This state is useful when it is desired that a macro that utilizes the 'SET +1' command start with the first set in a schema.

 

4. A "plus-sign" (+) followed by an expression evaluating to a non-zero positive result. This selects an set by relative sequence number within the Schema Reference Table in relation to the current set. Thus, +1 selects the "next" set in the schema. Note, however, that if the resultant relative set number is zero, the error "SET NOT FOUND" will result (compare to the 'SET #0' command).

 

5. A "minus-sign" (-) followed by an expression evaluating to a non-zero positive result. This also selects a set by relative sequence number (but in a backwards manner). Thus, -1 selects the "previous" set. Note, however, that if the resultant relative set number is zero, the error "SET NOT FOUND" will result (compare to the 'SET #0' command).

 

6. An array/table subset expected to contain a character string which corresponds syntactically to one of the five previous formats.

3.11.5 Discussion

If a subschema is current at the time of the 'SET' command, the 'SSRT' table corresponding to the set selected will be made current (if it is included in the subschema).

3.11.6 Format 2

Format 2 will print the following information about the current set:

 

Set code and name

Schema name

Schema filename

3.11.7 Affected Entities

As a result of this command, the following tables will be affected:

 

SDT

SRT

and the following system variables will be affected:

 

SCODE

SSEQ

TABLE (if old table was SDT or SRT)

TSIZE (if old table was SDT or SRT)

$ (if old table was SDT or SRT)

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 3 | 'SSAREA' Command |

| DMS / RDMS TABLE ACCESS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */SSAREA

3.12. SSAREA Command

3.12.1 Abbreviations

This command may not be abbreviated.

3.12.2 Syntax

1. SSAREA[,<options>] <area specification>

2. SSAREA

3.12.3 Purpose

Locate the Subschema Area Reference Table [SART] for the selected area within the Subschema Reference Table [SST]. If found, assign the area file to the user's run (EXEC areas only) and read in page zero (DARP areas only). All subsequent PAGE, COUNT and DMSCALC (the function, not the macro) requests will refer to this area.

3.12.4 Options

None The 'SSAREA' command will make available the Subschema Area Reference Table (SART) and database pages for the area. If an EXEC area, the correct qualifier must already have been defined to DBE (see the section on the 'QUAL' command), and if a TIP area, the file must be TPASG'd. If the area is not available, a message explaining the problem will be printed; however, the tables 'ART' and 'SART', the system variables 'ASEQ', 'SSASEQ', 'ACODE' and 'SSACODE', and possibly other related tables and variables will be accurately updated.

 

N The area name and code will not be printed when the area is made current.

 

P The 'SSAREA' command will make available the area's reference tables ("ART" and "SART") only. No attempt will be made to access or even verify the existence of the actual area on disc. This is the recommended mode of access to the Area Reference Table when no actual access to the database itself is required.

3.12.5 Format 1

The value of the <area specification> is expected to be one of the following:

 

1. The name of the area to be selected.

 

2. The code of the area to be selected. This code may be an integer number or an expression.

 

3. A "pound-sign" (#) followed by an expression.

If the expression evaluates to a non-zero positive result, the area will be selected by absolute sequence number within the Subschema Reference Table. Note that since a subschema area's absolute number is defined to be it's relative position in the Subschema Reference Table, this form is identical to number 2 above.

If the expression evaluates to zero, any area tables (ART, SART, etc.) previously accessible will be made unavailable to the user. This corresponds to the state of an area following a 'SCHEMA' command. This state is useful when it is desired that a macro that utilizes the 'SSAREA +1' command start with the first area in a schema.

4. A "plus-sign" (+) followed by an expression evaluating to a non-zero positive result. This selects an area by relative sequence number within the Subschema Reference Table in relation to the current area. Thus, +1 selects the "next" area in the subschema. Note, however, that if the resultant relative area number is zero, the error "AREA NOT FOUND" will result (compare to the 'SSAREA #0' command).

 

5. A "minus-sign" (-) followed by an expression evaluating to a non-zero positive result. This also selects an area by relative sequence number (but in a backwards manner). Thus, -1 selects the "previous" area in the subschema. Note, however, that if the resultant relative area number is zero, the error "AREA NOT FOUND" will result (compare to the 'SSAREA #0' command).

 

6. An array/table subset expected to contain a character string which corresponds syntactically to one of the five previous forms.

3.12.6 Discussion

If the area requested is the same as the area which is current, the 'SSAREA' command will be ignored. An exception to this rule is when the previous area request had either been terminated in error, or the previous area request had been an 'SSAREA,P' and you are now requesting complete use of the area; under these circumstances the command is honored.

If the 'N' option is not present on the 'SSAREA' command, when the ART has been located, the DBE-determined filename (or TIP/DMS file code) will be printed. Note that in the case where the area file is determined to be an EXEC area, a qualifier will be needed in addition to the area name (used as the filename). This qualifier is to be supplied by the 'QUAL' command.

If a subschema is current at the time of the 'SSAREA' command, the 'SART' table corresponding to the area selected will be made current (if it is included in the subschema). When an 'SSAREA' command is requested, the (schema) Area Reference Table (ART) corresponding to the record selected will be made current.

If the DBE 'Y' option is on, the 'SSAREA' command pertains to the training area requested. If the requested area does not have an associated training area, the command will refer to the production area requested. The DBE system variable 'TRAIN' will be set when the current area is a training area.

3.12.7 Format 2

Format 2 will print the following information about the current area:

 

Area code and name

Area filename

Schema name

Schema filename

3.12.8 Affected Entities

As a result of this command, the following tables will be affected:

 

ART

CSLOT

P0

PAGE

PH

RSLOT

SART

TREG

and the following system variables will be affected:

 

ACODE

ASEQ

MAXPG

NCSLOT

NRSLOT

TABLE : No table will be current if the previous table was PAGE, PH, P0, CSLOT, or RSLOT. Previous table remains current otherwise.

TSIZE : Set to zero if the previous table was PAGE, PH, P0, CSLOT, or RSLOT. Unchanged otherwise.

$ : Set to zero if the previous table was ART, SART, P0, PH, PAGE, CSLOT, or RSLOT.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 3 | 'SSRECORD' Command |

| DMS / RDMS TABLE ACCESS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */SSRECORD

3.13. SSRECORD Command

3.13.3 Purpose

Note that since a subschema record's absolute number is defined to be it's relative position in the Subschema Reference Table, this form is identical to number 2 above.

Thus, -1 selects the "previous" record in the subschema. Note, however, that if the resultant relative record number is zero, the error "RECORD NOT FOUND" will result (compare to the 'SSRECORD #0' command).

 

6. An array/table subset expected to contain a character string which corresponds syntactically to one of the five previous forms.

3.13.5 Discussion

3.13.6 Format 2

Record code and name

Schema name

Schema filename

3.15. SUBSCH Command

3.15.1 Abbreviations

This command may be abbreviated to 'SS'.

3.15.2 Syntax

1. SUBSCH [<file>.]<elt>[/<version>] [<subsch-name>]

2. SUBSCH,T <tip-file-code> <elt>[/<version>] [<subsch-name>]

3. SUBSCH

3.15.3 Purpose

Loads an absolute subschema element into an internal DBE buffer and makes it available for inspection or for use by the other DBE commands.

3.15.4 Format 1

This format is used when the absolute subschema is to be loaded from an EXEC-8 file. <File> is a standard EXEC-8 file name in the format Qual*File (F-Cycle)/Read-key/Write-key. If <file> is omitted, the schema file will be used. <Elt> is a standard EXEC-8 element name (minus elt-cycle)

<Version> is a standard version name.

<Subschema-name> is the name specified in the SUBSCHEMA NAME IS clause of the symbolic subschema element of the sub- schema to be loaded.

3.15.5 Format 2

This format is used when the absolute subschema is to be loaded from a TIP file. <Tip-file-code> is any expression evaluating to a non-negative and non-zero result.

3.15.6 Format 3

Format 3 will print the following information about the current subschema:

 

Subschema name

Subschema filename (or TIP/DMS code)

Schema name

Schema filename (or TIP/DMS code)

The following tables will be available to the DBE user upon the issuing of the 'SUBSCH' command:

 

SFD - Subschema File Description Table. Contains pertinent file information about the subschema (name, file, TIP code, associated schema, etc) and points to the SST and SHT.

 

SST - Subschema Reference Table. Contains additional characteristics about the subschema and gives the lengths and addresses of the Subschema Area, Record and Set Reference Tables.

 

SSCD - Subschema Description Table Contains additional subschema characteristics as well as Subschema File Name information.

 

DNT - Data Name Table Contains information pointing to data names and data name lengths.

 

DDT - Data Name Description Table Contains Data Name mappings from Schema to Subschema.

 

INI - Item Name Table Contains information pointing to item names and item lengths.

 

SART - Subschema Area Reference Table

 

SRRT - Subschema Record Reference Table

 

SRDT - Subschema Record Description Table

 

SSRT - Subschema Set Reference Table

 

SSDT - Subschema Set Description Table The following tables are available if the subschema is type QLP:

 

SHT - Subschema Header Table. This table points to all other QLP subschema tables and contains information specific to QLP. (See 'SHT' macro.)

 

PIT - Path Index Table. Provides the necessary information for locating a path that meets the requirements of a query. The path mask is utilized during path selection and the corresponding PDT, as pointed to by the PIT, is retrieved. At least one entry exists for every QLP path described in the QLP subschema.

 

PDT - Path Description Table. Provides information on a path such that path validation can be completed. Path selection determines from this table what records need to be traversed. For each record-to-record traversal which must be performed on a given path, a "path step" entry exists. If a path consists of only one record, no path entries will be created and the word offset to the first path step (PDT003) will equal zero. The only situation for which a PDT will not exist for a path defined in the subschema is when the root record has a location mode defined in the PIT as direct, calc, or index sequential and the root record is the only record defined on the path.

 

SIT - Set Information Table. Provides information about sets defined in the QLP subschema. One SIT exists for each set and is pointed to by the SCT entry for that set.

 

RIT - Record Information Table. Provides QLP with needed information about a record so that QLP can traverse that record on a selected path and know what keys are required for access. One RIT exists for each record in the QLP subschema and is pointed to by the RCDT entry for that record.

 

ACT - Area Code Table. Provides QLP with file assignment information at the time of invoke and is used for area code to area name translations. One ACT exists consisting of an entry for each area defined in the QLP subschema.

 

RCDT - Record Code Table. Serves three purposes:

1. To translate a record code to a record name.

2. To obtain the location of a record's corresponding RIT.

3. To obtain the location of a record's ICT.

One RCDT exists consisting of an entry for each record type defined in the QLP subschema.

 

SCT - Set Code Table. Used to translate a set code to a set name and to obtain the location of a set's SIT. Only one SCT exists consisting of an entry for each set defined in the QLP subschema.

 

DCT - Data Base Data Name Table. Provides information on data base data names defined in the QLP subschema. The data base data name codes are used to obtain the name location in the DNS area and characteristics of a given DBDN. One DCT exists for each DBDN defined in the QLP subschema.

 

ICT - Item Code Table. Provides the information necessary to translate item codes to item names (which are used in diagnostics or to serve as keys in the Name Hash Table to get the description of an item). It is also used to translate item codes to sub-items, both for list by item and for key fields passed to the DMR. One ICT exists for each data item of each record type defined in the QLP subschema.

 

QED - Name Hash Table or Data Item Dictionary Table (DIDT). Specifically defines the characteristics of each data item defined in the QLP subschema. One QED exists for each data item.

 

DNS - Data Name Storage Area. Provides the initial values of data base data names defined in the QLP subschema. These initial values are passed to the DMR for data base access.

 

NHT - Name Hash Table

 

DSW - D$WORK Area

3.15.7 Affected Entities

As a result of this command, the following tables will be affected:

 

ACT

DCT

DNS

ICT

PDT

PIT

QED

RCDT

RIT

SCT

SFD

SHT

SIT

SST

SUBSCH

and the following system variables will be affected:

 

PSEQ

TABLE (if the old table was in the above list)

TSIZE (if the old table was in the above list)

$ (if the old table was in the above list)

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 3 | 'TIPIO' Command |

| DMS / RDMS TABLE ACCESS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */TIPIO

3.16. TIPIO Command

3.16.1 Abbreviations

This command may not be abbreviated.

3.16.2 Syntax

1. TIPIO CLEAR

2. TIPIO PRIMARY

3. TIPIO SECONDARY

4. TIPIO

3.16.3 Purpose

Allows the DBE user to direct subsequent I/O to a particular leg of a duplex TIP file.

3.16.4 Format 1

This format is used to clear the TIPIO flag. When the flag is clear, TIP I/O is directed to either leg of the duplex file.

3.16.5 Format 2

This format directs TIP I/O to the primary leg (leg 1) of a duplex file.

3.16.6 Format 3

This format directs TIP I/O to the secondary leg (leg 2) of a duplex file.

3.16.7 Format 4

This format will print the current status of the TIPIO flag.

3.16.8 Discussion

Should I/O be directed to the secondary leg, but the file is not duplexed, an error message will be returned:

 

<102> THIS TIP FILE IS NOT DUPLEXED

Also, if I/O is directed to a particular leg and that leg is TPFREE'D, an error message will be returned:

 

<101> THIS LEG OF THE TIP FILE IS TPFREE'D

The user should also be aware that execution of the SCHEMA command will automatically clear the TIPIO flag. *//

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 4 | Introduction |

| BUFFER ORIENTED COMMANDS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

4. Buffer Oriented Commands

The commands in this section are used to inspect the contents of a table or array that is presently defined to DBE.

Each time the user is solicited for input (while in conversational mode) a string of the form:

 

tttttt[ooo]:

or

aaaaaa(ooo):

will be printed. The 'tttttt' is the name of the table that is currently the default. The 'ooo' is an octal number indicating the current buffer pointer location within the current table ('tttttt'). The 'aaaaaa' is the name of the array that is currently the default, while the 'ooo' within the () is the current word within the array. Only one of these prompts will appear (if any) and which one depends on whether you have been looking at a table or an array. Hereafter in the discussions in this chapter, all references to tables being examined may be assumed to apply equally to arrays, unless otherwise stated. Remember, however, that the first word of an array is always one (1), whereas that for a table is zero (0).

Should no table currently be established as the default, then the string would appear merely as '*:'.

These commands work on the principle of moving an imaginary pointer through a buffer. This is a principle similar to that used by @ED. The buffer is either that for the default table, or for one explicitly referred to on the particular command. After a table has been referred on a command, it then becomes the default table for future buffer commands.

Many of the commands in this chapter allow options that specify the type of print representation that is to be used. For a summary of these options (and formats) consult Table 4-1.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 4 | Moving the pointer through |

| BUFFER ORIENTED COMMANDS | a table |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

4.1. (Buffer Pointer Positioning)

 

 

4.1.1 Abbreviations

Not applicable.

4.1.2 Syntax

1. <Expression>[,<option>] [<table>]

2. +<Expression>[,<option>] [<table>]

3. -<Expression>[,<option>] [<table>]

4.1.3 Purpose

To position the buffer pointer to a specified position within either the given table or the default table.

4.1.4 Options

See Table 4-1 or the "FMT" command.

4.1.5 Discussion

Format 1 is used when the user wishes to position the buffer pointer within a table to an absolute word number. See Figure 1-1 for a list of the tables that may be used. The buffer pointer will be set to the word whose location within the desired table is the result of <expression>. The presence of the optional table name will position to a word within that table, while the absence of the table name will position to that word of the current table (the one mentioned on the command prompt).

Formats 2 and 3 move the buffer pointer forward or backward the number of words specified by the value of <expression>. The destination word number computed by taking the current buffer location and adding to it (or subtracting from it) the value of <expression> should be within the range of word numbers for that table.

The effect of this command will be to print the following:

 

tttttt[ooo]: vvvvvvvvvvvv

or

aaaaaa(ooo): vvvvvvvvvvvv

where 'tttttt' is the table name (or 'aaaaaa' is the array name), 'ooo' is the buffer pointer location within the table/array and 'vvvvvvvvvvvv' is the value of that word printed in the desired print format (see the 'FMT' command). If brief-mode is on (the 'B' option on the processor call) then this print will not be done. Regardless of the setting of the 'B' option, the default table will be set to the table that was specified, and the buffer pointer will be set to the location referenced within that table.

If the requested word number is out-of-range for the specified table, then the message

 

EOF: xxx

will be displayed, where <xxx> is the highest word number in the table. In this case, the buffer pointer will be reset to the origin of the table (word 0 for a table, word 1 for an array).

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 4 | 'FMT' Command |

| BUFFER ORIENTED COMMANDS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*/FMT

4.2. FMT Command

4.2.1 Abbreviations

This command cannot be abbreviated.

4.2.2 Syntax

FMT,<option>

4.2.3 Purpose

Sets the default print format to the desired user-specified setting.

4.2.4 Options

See Table 4-1.

4.2.5 Discussion

All of the commands in this section (with the exception of this one) cause at least one word of a table to be printed (unless the 'B' option is on). This command sets the default format code for these prints.

The other commands in this section can override this default print format by specifying an option on the command. As an example:

 

101,F SCRT

PRINT,A 10,200

LAST,D

The legal format codes are listed in Table 4-1.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 4 | Print Command Format Codes |

| BUFFER ORIENTED COMMANDS | Table 4-1 |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

 

 

 

 

Format-Code Meaning

=========== =======

A Print a continuous string of characters showing the

ASCII representation of the words being printed.

Leading and trailing quotes will delimit the beginning

and end of the string. Control characters (octal

037 and below) will appear as '?'.

 

B Print the words in binary.

 

D Print the words in decimal.

 

F Like 'A', but for Fieldata.

 

H Print the words in hexadecimal.

 

O Print the words in octal.

 

Q Like 'A', but each word will be delimited by quotes.

 

S Like 'F', but each word will be delimited by quotes.

The following table illustrates the maximum number of words per line for each print code for demand and batch usage:

 

Code Demand Batch

 

A 15 28

B 1 3

D 4 8

F 10 19

H 6 12

O 4 8

Q 9 16

S 6 12

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 4 | 'LAST' Command |

| BUFFER ORIENTED COMMANDS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */LAST

4.3. LAST Command

4.3.1 Abbreviations

This command may not be abbreviated.

4.3.2 Syntax

LAST[,<option>] [<table>]

4.3.3 Purpose

Position the buffer pointer at the last word of either the specified table or the current table. That word will also be printed (if the 'B' option is not set).

4.3.4 Options

See Table 4-1 or the "FMT" command.

4.3.5 Discussion

The buffer pointer will be positioned to the last word of the given table (if a table name is supplied) or to the last word of the current table (if no table name is supplied). If the 'B' option is off, the word positioned to will be printed in the requested format (if an option is supplied) or in the default format (if no option is supplied). Note that the 'LAST' command is a special case of the 'LAST' system variable. Both command and variable have identical results, except when a table or array name is specified on the command, in which case the pointer will be positioned to the last word in the specified table/array (as opposed to the previous value of the 'LAST' variable).

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 4 | 'OUTPUT' Command |

| BUFFER ORIENTED COMMANDS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */OUTPUT

4.4. OUTPUT Command

4.4.1 Abbreviations

This command may be abbreviated to 'OUT' or 'O'.

4.4.2 Syntax

OUTPUT[,<option>] [<expression>] [<table>]

4.4.3 Purpose

Output the next one or more words of either the specified table or the current table.

4.4.4 Options

See table 4-1 or the "FMT" command.

4.4.5 Discussion

<Expression> must evaluate to a non-negative, non-zero result. The value of <expression> will be the number of words to print (default value will be 1). Printing will begin with the next word of the current table, for a total of <expression> words. The print format will be that requested (if an option was supplied) or the default format (if no option was supplied).

If the value of <expression> is so large as to cause the buffer pointer to go beyond the end of the table, the outputting will cease and the buffer pointer will be positioned at the origin of the table (word 0 for a table; word 1 for an array). If the DBE processor 'D' option is set (implying DEMAND mode), the data will be displayed in 80-column format. If the option is clear (implying BATCH mode), output will be in 132-column format.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 4 | 'PRINT' Command |

| BUFFER ORIENTED COMMANDS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */PRINT

4.5. PRINT Command

4.5.1 Abbreviations

This command may be abbreviated to 'P'.

4.5.2 Syntax

1. PRINT[,<option>] <expression-1>,<expression-2> [<table>]

2. PRINT[,<option>] [<expression>] [<table>]

4.5.3 Purpose

Print words from either the specified table or the current table.

4.5.4 Options

See Table 4-1 or the "FMT" command.

4.5.5 Discussion

<Expression>, <expression-1>, and <expression-2> are all expressions with non-negative values where the value of <expresion-1> is not greater than that of <expression-2>.

Format 1 prints words from the specified table (if a table was specified) or the current table (if no table was specified). Words <expression-1> through <expression-2> (inclusive) will be printed.

Format 2 prints <expression> words from the current table starting at the current word. If <expression> is absent, a value of one will be assumed.

The words will be printed using the requested format (if an option was supplied) or using the default format (if no option was given).

Any print request that causes the buffer pointer to go past the end of the table being printed will be terminated at the end of the table, and will leave the buffer pointer positioned at the origin of the table (word 0 of a table, word 1 of an array); otherwise the buffer pointer will be left at the last word printed. If the DBE processor 'D' option is set (implying DEMAND mode), the data will be displayed in 80-column format. If the option is clear (implying BATCH mode), output will be in 132-column format.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 4 | 'P!' Command |

| BUFFER ORIENTED COMMANDS | Printing an entire table |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*//

4.6. PRINT# (Print-Exclamation)

***** NOTE *****

Some printers do not support the 'exclamation point' character....A '#' has been substituted in this document.

4.6.1 Abbreviations

This command may be abbreviated to 'P#' (where # is an exclamation point).

4.6.2 Syntax

PRINT#[,<option> [<table>] (Remember, # = exclamation point)

4.6.3 Purpose

Print a table in its entirety.

4.6.4 Options

See Table 4-1 or the "FMT" command.

4.6.5 Discussion

The entire table specified (if one was specified) or the entire current table (if none was specified) will be printed from its origin (word 0 for a table, word 1 for an array) onward regardless of where the buffer pointer is presently positioned.

After the printing is complete, the buffer pointer will be positioned at the table origin.

Printing will be according to the requested format (if an option was supplied) or will be in the default format (if no option was given). If the DBE processor 'D' option is set (implying DEMAND mode), the data will be displayed in 80-column format. If the option is clear (implying BATCH mode), output will be in 132-column format.

5.1.4 Discussion

This command is similar to the BYE/EXIT command except that it issues an 'ER EABT$' to error-terminate the DBE processor.

or

| Chapter 5 | 'EVALUATE' Command |

| MISCELLANEOUS COMMANDS | |

*// */EVALUATE

5.4. EVALUATE Command

5.4.1 Abbreviations

This command may be abbreviated to 'EVAL' or 'E'.

5.4.2 Syntax

EVALUATE,[<option>] [<expression>]

5.4.3 Purpose

This command provides a 'desk-calculator' capability to DBE.

5.4.4 Options

The options are print formats. Consult Table 4-1 for a list of legal print formats.

5.4.5 Discussion

The given expression will be evaluated and the result will be printed according to the specified format code (if one is supplied as an option) or the default print (if none is supplied). If no <expression> is supplied, the result from the last 'EVALUATE' command will be used. If there has been no previous 'EVALUATE' command executed, a value of zero will be assumed.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 5 | 'HARDCOPY' Command |

| MISCELLANEOUS COMMANDS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */HARDCOPY

5.5. HARDCOPY

5.5.1 Abbreviations

This command may not be abbreviated.

5.5.2 Syntax

1. HARDCOPY [<copies>] [,<device>] [,<banner>]

2. HARDCOPY,T <pid> [,<did>]

5.5.3 Purpose

Display or alter the current copy-count, hardcopy device specification or @SYM banner.

5.5.4 Discussion

Format 1 is used to either designate hardcopy output to a high-speed printer (including the number of copies to be printed and banner) or, when no parameters are given, print the current hardcopy specifications.

<Copies>, if supplied, must be an expression evaluating to a number between 0 and 63.

<Device>, if supplied, must be the name of the desired onsite device. No check will be made that this is a legal device.

<Banner> , if supplied, must be the banner/user-id desired to print on the output cover page.

For example, to specify that the hardcopy output designation should be the high-speed printer 'PR1' , 7 copies should be printed, and the banner should be DA0220, specify:

 

HARDCOPY 7,PR1,DA0220

Format 2 is legal only for versions of DBE that have been configured for TIP support. This format allows an expression to be specified as the pid number to which a copy of all terminal input and output will be sent should the processor 'H' option be activated. No check will be made that the pid number supplied is valid or that it is actually a printer and not a CRT. Format 2 allows an expression to be specified as the 'did' of a terminal-attached TIP printer. If no 'did' is specified, the default of octal 0163 (hex 73) will be used. Neither format will cause hardcopy mode to activate but rather specifies where hardcopy output will go should hardcopy mode ever become activated. To activate hardcopy mode, the 'H' option must be turned on (see the 'ON' command).

Once hardcopy mode is actually in effect you may change HARDCOPY parameters within certain restricted areas:

 

1. If you are in standard hardcopy mode (high-speed printer) you may alter the copy count, printer id and banner but you may not switch to TIP hardcopy mode without first turning off hardcopy mode (via the 'OFF H' command) to @SYM the accumulated output.

 

2. If you are in TIP hardcopy mode you may alter the pid number to which you are sending the output but you may not switch to standard hardcopy mode without first turning off hardcopy mode (via the 'OFF H' command).

When in TIP hardcopy mode, DBE will internally buffer output until that buffer becomes filled, at which time it will be formatted and sent to the selected pid. After a buffer is sent it will be erased and filled with new output. Because of this you will not immediately see output when you enter TIP hardcopy mode - the output will be delayed until the buffer fills and you will then see about 1500 characters worth of output. Each time you switch pids the buffer contents will be sent prior to actually effecting the pid switch. If you execute a 'OFF H' or 'BYE' command, the remaining buffer contents (if any) will be sent.

| MISCELLANEOUS COMMANDS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */WAIT

5.9. WAIT

 

WAIT[,options] [delay-value] ----

5.9.1 Options

None Legal only if no "delay-value" is given

H Treat the "delay-value" as an hhmm value

M Treat the "delay-value" as minutes

S Treat the "delay-value" as seconds This statement allows the Database Editor to be "put to sleep" for a period of time. That period of time may be "forever, or until an @@X" (WAIT with no options), until a specified time (WAIT,H), for a certain number of seconds (WAIT,S) or a certain number of minutes (WAIT,M).

The following illustrate how WAIT is used.

5.9.2 Wait Forever

WAIT ----

This will cause DBE to be permanently suspended. The only event that can re-awaken DBE is an @@X contingency. remain 10

5.9.3 Wait Until a Specified Time

WAIT,H hhmm ---- -

The expression "hhmm" is treated as a 24-hour format time. DBE will remain suspended until that time.

5.9.4 Wait One or More Seconds

WAIT,S number-of-seconds ---- -

Note that the wait must be an integral number of seconds.

5.9.5 Wait One or More Minutes

WAIT,M number-of-minutes ---- -

Note that the wait must be an integral number of minutes.
