| Chapter 6 | 'REWRITE' Command |

| TABLE PATCHING | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */Rewrite

6. The 'REWRITE' Command

 

If security features have been configured with DBE, this command will be available only to those users having the 'UPDATE' privilege or 'SELECTED-REWRITE' feature.

6.1. Abbreviations

This command may not be abbreviated.

6.2. Syntax

REWRITE <table>

6.3. Purpose

Writes the entire table back to mass-storage in the exact location from whence it came.

6.4. Discussion

The specified <table> may be one of the following:

 

FDT

* PAGE

* P0

* RAP

RDT

* RFCP

* RPAGE

* RP1

SCHEMA

SCRT

SDT

SFD

SUBSCH

Tables marked with an "*" can only be rewritten by users who have the "UPDATE" privilege set.

FDT, SCRT, RDT, and SDT may not be specified unless the version of DBE being used has FULL-SCHEMA-READS disabled (see the 'SCHEMA' command). If the FULL-SCHEMA-READ feature is enabled, the table SCHEMA will be allowed and FDT/SDT will not. If the FULL-SCHEMA-READ feature is disabled, the SCHEMA table will not be allowed (since it will not exist) and FDT/SDT will.

In the event that the current table was a schema table of some sort (FDT, SCRT, ART or SCHEMA) no attempt will be made to verify that the absolute schema element has not changed locations in the file. The user should be completely certain that no one else is using the file at the time the rewrite is attempted.

In the event that the current table is a database table (P0, PH or PAGE) no attempt will be made to determine if the area involved is 'down'ed. Should it not be down, the patches applied may be overwritten should the DMR have been accessing the page at the time. The user should be sure to 'down' the area (via the DMU) prior to attempting a patch/rewrite sequence involving pages from that area.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | Macro Concepts |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

7. Macros

*//

7.1. Macro Concepts

7.1.1 The Concept of a Macro

A macro is a collection of DBE statements that, collectively, are treated as a single statement. The macro is, in effect, a program consisting of DBE commands.

7.1.2 Macros and Conversational Mode

 

The normal interactive operation mode of DBE is referred to as 'conversational mode'. When a macro is running however, we say that DBE is running in 'macro mode'.

7.1.3 Creation of Macros

Macros come in two varieties - local and global. The local kind

 

are defined via the 'MACRO' command in an interactive manner. Their definitions remain known to DBE only for the duration of the DBE session in which they were created (or until they are deleted via the DELETE command).

Global macros are known from one DBE session to the next. This is due to the fact that their text is stored on file as a source element in a program file. Such macros may reside in either of the two following files:

 

 

1. The DBE system macro library as specified in the DBE sysgen. This file is referred to as the system file since macros defined in it are available to all users (system-wide). This is the file to which the @USE name DBE$SYSLIB will be attached while DBE is running.

 

2. A SITE LIBRARY file. This file should contain macros used by all users at a given site but are not transportable accross sites. Some examples are macros which generate ECL to call the DMU, IRU, or DD processors. This file will have an @USE name of DBE$SITELIB attached.

 

3. A user-specified library file. This file (the one specified in spec 1 of the DBE processor call) is referred to as the 'library file' or 'user library'. This the file to which the @USE name DBE$PF will be attached while DBE is running.

The user keeps his own macros in his personal 'library file'. Thus, these macros are (generally) local to the particular user.

 

4. A user-specified alternate library file. This file can be specified by the ALT-LIB macro and will have an internal @USE name of DBE$PF2.

 

Macro names may consist of 1 to 12 characters from the set of 'A'-'Z', '0'-'9', '$' and '-'. In addition, local macros may include other characters (except ' ' and '@') but use of such characters is not recommended.

7.1.4 Macro Execution

One way in which macros are executed is by using their name as a DBE command. Any parameters that the macro might be expecting are to be supplied on the same line as the macro call in the format discussed under the 'PARAMETER' command. The second way is by coding the complete macro call (options and any parameters included) to the right of an equals sign (=) on a 'LET' command. Using this second technique the macro may (but is not obligated to) return a value to the field to the left of the equals sign in a manner similar to that used by the various DBE functions. Thus, the user may use macros to enhance the DBE command set and the DBE function repetoire.

In order for the macro to be executed, its text must be loaded into an internal fixed-length buffer referred to as the 'Macro Area'. All macros,

whether local or global, whether found in the system-file or user-library, whether executed as commands or functions, must be loaded into this buffer in order to be run. There may be any number of macros in the macro area at any given time, limited only by the size of the macro area. The size of the macro area is a DBE configuration parameter. The user may determine the maximum macro area size via the 'LIST' command.

The presence of a macro already loaded into the macro area will prevent the loading of another of the same name from either of the two files until the macro in-core is 'DELETE'd.

When a macro is to be loaded for execution, the system library will be searched before the user library. If a name match is found in the system library, that will be the version of the macro loaded, even if one with the same name exists in the user library. Specifying the 'R' option on the DBE processor call (or turning it on while within DBE) will reverse this order.

For more information on macros, specifically the handling of run-time errors, see the documentation for the 'ERROR', 'ERRPR', and 'RETURN' commands in the DBE Programmer's Reference Manual.

7.1.5 Macro Area Maintenance

The macro area is a fixed-size block of reserved memory within the DBE processor. This memory is dedicated to the storage of macros during and after their execution. When a sufficient number of macros have been defined and/or loaded from a file (the system file or user-specified library), the macro area will be full; any attempt to load or define an additional macro when this area is full will cause a "macro area overflow" condition.

This "macro area overflow" condition will be resolved in one of two fashions, depending upon the circumstances. If you were attempting to load a macro from a file (system file or user library) and that request was in response to a user input from the terminal (as opposed to one macro calling another), DBE will remove from the macro area all macros that originated from one of the two files. If this "compaction" does not yield enough free space to hold the macro or if the conditions mentioned above were not met, then an error message will be printed and the macro load attempt will be aborted. In this second case you will have no choice but to manually erase macros from the macro area (using the 'DELETE' command) until sufficient space has been made available.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

The ALLSLOTS macro will produce a DUMPREC listing for all records on the current page. The records will be printed in the order in which their record slots occur on the page (upward from the bottom). Contrast with the ALLRECS macro.

7.2.2.1 Syntax

ALLSLOTS

7.2.2.2 Discussion

None.

7.2.2.3 Sample Output

Identical to ALLRECS, except the records will be printed in the order in which their record slot pointers occur at the bottom of the page (from the bottom up).

7.2.4 AREA-ALL

The AREA-ALL macro is used to call a specified macro for each area in the current schema matching an optional mask.

P Pause between areas.

7.2.4.3 Discussion

None.

7.2.5 AREA-DDL

This macro will print all of the same information presented by the ART macro (see the ART macro) but prints it using DDL syntax. This means that the description of an area exactly as described to DDL will be printed.

7.2.5.1 Syntax

AREA-DDL[,<options>] [<area specification>]

7.2.5.2 Options

A All areas in the schema will be described.

P Invokes the 'P' option for each 'AREA' command performed. The area(s) requested will not be physically accessed; all information will be taken only from the schema tables.

7.2.5.3 Discussion

The <area specification> (if any) is the same as any legal area selector for the 'AREA' command. Absence of an <area specification> will cause reference to the current area.

7.2.5.4 Sample Output

See Figure 1-3.

7.2.7 AREA-INIT

This macro will create an SDF file containing a runstream to initialize selected areas via the DMU.

7.2.7.1 Syntax

AREA-INIT,[<options>] [<mask>][,<start-page>]

7.2.7.2 Options

7.2.7.3 Discussion

The SDF file created is "*INIT." with an @USE name of "INIT.".

| Chapter 7 | 'AREAS' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */AREAS

7.2.8 AREAS

 

This macro is used to produce a listing of all (or some) areas in the currently loaded schema. The following information will be printed for each area:

 

1. Area-name

2. Area-code

3. Mode (SARP/DARP)

4. Access (EXEC/TIP)

5. Type (Data/Index/Pointer)

In addition, the area will be checked for each of the following items, with an appropriate message printed if an item applies:

 

1. Facility status (EXEC areas)

2. TIP assignment (TIP areas)

3. Initialized/uninitialized

4. Page header inconsistency

7.2.8.1 Syntax

AREAS[,options] [<mask>]

7.2.8.2 Options

S Display areas sorted by area name instead of TIP code.

T Display TIP DUPLEX/SIMPLEX information.

7.2.8.3 Discussion

Note that in the case of EXEC areas, the current default qualifier (see the 'QUAL' command) will be used to determine the complete area file name. If this is incorrect, unexpected 'FAC REJECT' messages may result.

DBE will only check the first page of an area (page zero if DARP) for being consistent and initialized.

Absence of the optional <mask> parameter will cause all areas to be listed as shown previously. Presence of the <mask> parameter will cause only those areas whose names match the pattern specified by the mask to be listed. Patterns are specified by supplying an area name pattern using an asterisk (*) where any character(s) are allowed to match. For example, to match area names beginning with the letter "A" and followed by any other characters, a mask of "A*" would be used (note that "A*" and "A**" are treated identically - one asterisk is sufficient). To match area names ending in "Q", a mask of "*Q" would be used. To match area names beginning with "A" and ending with "Q", a mask of "A*Q" would be used. To match area names having an "A" anywhere in their name, a mask of "*A*" would be used. The preceeding examples show only a small part of the masking capabilities available.

If run in demand mode, the display will pause after each screen of data is displayed. This can be overriden by use of the "PAUSE OFF/ON P" commands.

7.2.8.4 Sample Output

See Figure 1-3.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'ATT' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */ATT

7.2.10 ATT

This macro is used to "browse" through an IRU created audit trail , either on tape or disk.

7.2.10.1 Syntax

ATT[,options] [<function>],[<parameter>]

7.2.10.2 Options

C Continuous mode - similar to an "OFF D" command.

 

D Call the ATT-DUMP macro to dump each audit record.

 

Q Show QUEUE Item table additions and removals.

 

R Re-run a previous search function.

 

S Display block header statistics on console every 1000 blocks.

7.2.10.3 Discussion

This macro enables you to browse audit trails on a record by record basis.

The available functions are:

 

INIT Initializes all tables for a new audit trail. If the audit trail is on tape, it must be previously assigned with an @USE name of "ATT". If the audit trail is on disk, it must have an @USE name of "ATT".

This must be the first function performed.

 

COUNT Specifies the number of blocks to be processed on a subsequent call if the "C" option is specified or the macro is running in batch ("OFF D") mode.

 

SEARCH Allows dumping of only audits relating to specified runids or area codes / file names. These search arguments are saved to a temporary file so that if the macro is called with the "R" option and the "SEARCH" function, the same search criteria will be used.

 

RECORD Allows dumping only of selected record types. A list of valid record types can be obtained by answering "?" at the prompt. As with the SEARCH function, this function can be re-started via the "R" option.

 

STEP Allows dumping only of selected Integrated Step Ids. As with the SEARCH function, this function can be re-started via the "R" option.

 

BLOCK Positions the audit trail to the specified Block. If the BLOCK is not passed as a parameter, the user will be prompted to enter one.

 

TBSN Positions the audit trail to the specified Trail Block Sequence Number (TBSN). If the TBSN is not passed as a parameter, the user will be prompted to enter one.

 

TIME Positions the audit trail to the first block at or after the specified date/time. The date/time can not be passed as a parameter but will always be obtained from a prompt to the user.

 

DUMP Passes parameters after the DUMP keyword as options to the ATT-DUMP macro. For example, "ATT DUMP,OA" would generate an "ATT-DUMP,OA" macro call.

7.2.10.4 Sample Output

*:> ATT INIT *:> ATT COUNT,2 *:> ATT,C

*// */ATT-UPDATES

7.2.13 ATT-UPDATES

This displays a histogram detailing the number of AFTER LOOKS taken per step for a given Audit Trail.

7.2.13.1 Syntax

ATT-UPDATES[<,options>] [<mask>][<,number-of-steps>]

B Display Block Numbers

L Display Run-Id, Step-# And Number Of Updates

Q Display Queue Item Counts As They Are Added/Removed From Table

Z Display Each Audit Recod Type, Subtype and Length

7.2.13.2 Discussion

If <mask> is supplied, only those generated run-ids which mask the <mask> will be reported on.

If <number-of-steps> is omitted, the entire Audit Trail will be processed. This macro will not expand compacted looks from the tape.

Before running this macro, the ATT macro must have been previously run with a parameter of "INIT" to intialize the ATTBUF table.

An SDF file is created with an @USE name of PFILE. This file contains the run-ids,step-ids, and number of updates for each runid that matches the specified <mask>.

| Chapter 7 | 'CALC-REPORT' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */CALC-REPORT

7.2.18 CALC-REPORT

This macro scans all the calc chains in an area, then allows the user to display the page/chains that are a certain length.

7.2.18.1 Syntax

CALC-REPORT [<interval>][,<hi-page>]

7.2.18.2 Discussion

The <interval> parameter on the macro call line allows the macro to take a sampling of the area's pages. If an interval is specified, the macro will analyse a page, then skip <interval> pages until the next page to be analysed. If an interval is not specified, each page in the area will be read. The <hi-page> parameter specifies the highest page number to be read during the analysis phase. If the highest page number is not specified, the highest prime page number will be determined from the ART (SARP areas), or from page zero (DARP areas). If the 'L' option was specified on the macro call, the user will be asked if a detailed page display is desired. If the response is 'Y', or if the 'L' option was not specified, the user is asked for the minimum and maximum calc chain counts that are desired. Entering a null input (no chain count) will terminate the macro. The page and chain numbers of all chains with a length between the minimum and maximum will be displayed. After printing the list of all the pages satisfying the criteria selected, the user will have the opportunity to enter a new set of minimum/maximum specifications. This process will continue until the user enters a null input.

The detailed page/chain listing will list pages/chains and their length in a format such that if page 200, calc chain 2 was of length 30, it would appear as:

200/2/30

7.2.18.3 Sample Output

*:>CALC-REPORT

 

 

ENTER A NULL INPUT TO HALT

ENTER MINIMUM CHAIN LENGTH: >10

ENTER MAXIMUM CHAIN LENGTH: >20

 

 

 

FORMAT BELOW IS <PAGE-#>/<CHAIN-#>/<CHAIN-LENGTH>

 

 

267/0/11 314/0/14 324/0/12 384/0/11

394/0/12 400/0/12 403/0/11 404/0/10

462/0/10 479/0/10

 

 

ENTER MINIMUM CHAIN LENGTH: >

*:>CALC-REPORT,L

PAGE: 1, CHAIN: 0, LENGTH: 0

PAGE: 2, CHAIN: 0, LENGTH: 0

PAGE: 3, CHAIN: 0, LENGTH: 1

PAGE: 4, CHAIN: 0, LENGTH: 0

PAGE: 5, CHAIN: 0, LENGTH: 0

... <One line is generated for each page/chain in the area>

 

DO YOU WISH A DETAILED PAGE DISPLAY (Y/N)? > y

 

... <Print continues as above>

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'CALCASE' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */CALCASE

7.2.19 CALCASE

This macro allows the user to locate a calc record within the database controlled by the current schema provided its location mode is via the CALCASE calc procedure.

7.2.19.1 Syntax

CALCASE[,<option>] [<area>],[<RECORD>],[<KEY VALUE>]

7.2.19.2 Options

None The <key value> will be used as the key for the CALCASE process. If none is supplied, the user will be prompted for one (demand) or an error message will result (batch). The mode of the record will be used to dictate whether the key should be converted to ASCII or not.

 

B The <key value>, if any, will be ignored. A key of spaces (Fieldata or ASCII, as appropriate) will be used.

 

Z The <key value>, if any, will be ignored. A key of binary zeros will be used.

7.2.19.3 Discussion

<Area> is a specification of the area in which the record would be stored. This specification may be any that is legal on the 'AREA' command. If absent, the current area will be used.

<Record> is a specification of the record type you are looking for. This specification may be any that is legal on the 'RECORD' command. If absent, the current record will be used.

The <key value> should not be expressed within quotes unless the quotes are to be actual characters within the key.

After determining the page and chain number, this macro will fetch the appropriate page and begin searching the correct calc chain until it either finds the record of the correct type having the given <key value> or reaches the end of the calc chain (the point where it cycles back to the chain header word); this second condition would cause a "***RECORD NOT FOUND***" message to be printed.

As synonyms are found during the calc chain scan, the user will be told of the actual key values and record names of those synonym records.

7.2.19.4 Sample Output

See the example for DMSCALC in Figure 1-7.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'CALCBOUNDS' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */CALCBOUNDS

7.2.20 CALCBOUNDS

The CALCBOUNDS macro is used to load the CLCBND table for use with the RANDENTIAL function.

7.2.20.1 Syntax

CALCBOUNDS <lower-page-bound>,<upper-page-bound>

7.2.20.2 Discussion

The lower-page-bound is store in CLCBND[0] and the upper-page-bound is stored in CLCBND[1].

No verification is made to ensure that the page boundaries are valid.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'CALCSLOT' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */CALCSLOT

7.2.21 CALCSLOT

The CALCSLOT macro allows the user to specify a calc chain number on the current page to be used to locate a record. The record found will then be printed via the 'DUMPREC' macro.

7.2.21.1 Syntax

CALCSLOT <calc-chain-number>

7.2.21.2 Discussion

<calc-chain-number> is an integer in the range of 0-n, where "n" is one less than the number of calc chains defined for the area.

7.2.21.3 Sample Output

A DUMPREC listing of the desired record will be produced.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'CALCSLOTS' Macro |

| MACROS | |

The CALCSLOTS macro will print a formatted dump of the calc chain headers both in the page header and at the end-of-page for the currently loaded page.

7.2.22.1 Syntax

CALCSLOTS

7.2.22.2 Discussion

None.

7.2.23 CHECKSUM

The CHECKSUM macro is used to perform UDS checksum calculation on the currently based database page.

7.2.23.1 Syntax

CHECKSUM[,<options>]

7.2.23.2 Options

none Set "B" and "G" options.

 

B Display if checksum is bad.

 

C Update checksum IN CORE COPY ONLY if bad.

 

G Display if checksum is good

7.2.23.3 Discussion

None.

7.2.23.4 Sample Output

*:>CHECKSUM **BAD CHECKSUM IN AREA 788 / PAGE 0 - 000000000000 SHOULD BE 451457251551

*:>CHECKSUM,C

*:>CHECKSUM GOOD CHECKSUM IN AREA 788 / PAGE 0

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'CHECKSUM-ALL' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */CHECKSUM-ALL

7.2.24 CHECKSUM-ALL

The CHECKSUM-ALL macro calls the CHECKSUM-ONE macro for each area in a schema.

7.2.24.1 Syntax

CHECKSUM-ALL[,<options>] [<area-mask>]

7.2.24.2 Discussion

None.

7.2.24.3 Sample Output

A 'CHECKSUM-ONE' (with the given options) will be performed for all areas selected.

Presence of the optional <mask> parameter will cause only those areas whose names match the <mask> will be reported. Absence of the <mask> parameter will cause all areas to be reported.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'CHECKSUM-ONE' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */CHECKSUM-ONE

7.2.25 CHECKSUM-ONE

The CHECKSUM-ONE macro is used to verify checksums on all or some pages in the current area.

7.2.25.1 Syntax

CHECKSUM-ONE[,<options>] [<start-page>,<end-page>]

7.2.25.2 Options

none Set "B" and "G" options.

 

B Display if checksum is bad.

 

C Update checksum in core AND rewrite page to disk if bad.

 

G Display if checksum is good

 

M Multiple execution mode - exit and re-enter DBE processor every

500 pages processed to avoid max Log entries error.

7.2.25.3 Discussion

None.

7.2.25.4 Sample Output

*:>CHECKSUM-ONE 0,1 GOOD CHECKSUM IN AREA 788 / PAGE 0 **BAD CHECKSUM IN AREA 788 / PAGE 1 - 000000000000 SHOULD BE 072044666253

GOOD PAGES: 1 BAD PAGES: 1 REWRITES: 0

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'CHECKSUM-SET' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */CHECKSUM-SET

7.2.26 CHECKSUM-SET

The CHECKSUM-SET macro is used to create DD/UREP commands to change checksum settings for all areas in the based schema.

7.2.26.1 Syntax

CHECKSUM-SET[,<options>] <setting>[,<dd-options>]

7.2.26.2 Options

A @ADD the created file.

 

L Display generated output as it is written to the file.

7.2.26.3 Discussion

An SDF file is created with an @USE name of "CHKSET". This file will contain an SSG runstream to modify checksum settings. This allows easy updating of the file to change areas/checksum options.

Valid <setting> values are "YES", "NO" and "WRITE".

If <dd-options> are specified, they are used as options to the DD/UREP processor call. If omitted, default options of "ES" will be used.

7.2.26.4 Sample Output

*:>CHECKSUM-SET,L YES

@SSG,LM SKEL *IF [INFO$,1,5,1]=DEMAND #FREE [SCHEMA,1,1,1]*CHECKSUM-SET. #CAT,P [SCHEMA,1,1,1]*CHECKSUM-SET(+1).,///1000 #USE CHECKSUM-SET.,[SCHEMA,1,1,1]*CHECKSUM-SET. #BRKPT PRINT$/CHECKSUM-SET *ENDIF #UDS$$SVN*UREP$ABS.DD,ES ,,APPSVN . . *INCREMENT A FROM 1 TO [AREA] UPDATE STORAGE-AREA [AREA,A,1,1] FOR SCHEMA [SCHEMA,1,1,1]. REPLACE CHECKSUM WITH CHECKSUM [CHECKSUM,1,1,1]. PROCESS STORAGE-AREA [AREA,A,1,1] FOR SCHEMA [SCHEMA,1,1,1] UPDATE. *LOOP EXIT. *IF [INFO$,1,5,1]=DEMAND #BRKPT PRINT$ #ED,R CHECKSUM-SET. F END DDS *ENDIF @EOF SGS AREA LOGICAL-AREA AREA FILE-AREA AREA IO-AREA AREA FILE-HIST AREA LOGICAL-HIST AREA ATT-AREA-1 AREA ATT-AREA-2 SCHEMA FILMGT-SCH CHECKSUM YES @EOF @EOF

| Chapter 7 | 'DATA' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */DATA

7.2.28 DATA

This macro may be used to print the data area of a record on the current page.

7.2.28.1 Syntax

DATA[,<option>] [<record-location>]

7.2.28.2 Options

None The mode of the record being printed will determine the characterset (ASCII/Fieldata) used.

 

A Regardless of the record mode, ASCII will be used.

 

F Regardless of the record mode, Fieldata will be used.

7.2.28.3 Discussion

The <record-location> is the address of the start of a record on the current page. If specified, the data portion of the record at that location will be printed, and the current buffer pointer will be set to the start of that record. If the <record-location> is omitted, the current table pointer is assumed to be at the start of a record.

7.2.28.4 Sample Output

See Figure 1-7.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'DD-CALL' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */DD-CALL

7.2.29 DD-CALL

This macro is used to generate a call to the correct DD/UREP processor for the currently based UDS application group.

7.2.29.1 Syntax

DD-CALL[,<options>] <return-array>

7.2.29.2 Options

All options passed to this macro are used as options on the DD/UREP processor call line.

7.2.29.3 Discussion

The <return-array> will contain the processor call line for the DD/UREP processor for the current UDS application group. The current application group name will be passed to the DD call as field 3 to ensure that the correct application group is selected.

The <return-array> must be dimensioned as at least 8 words to ensure that the processor call line will not be truncated.

7.2.29.4 Sample Output

*:>U$APP 5

 

*:>DIMENSION A(8)

 

*:>DD-CALL,BSE <A>

 

*:>WDDUMP,F <A>

 

FIELDATA---------------------------------------------------------------- 000000 @UDS$$FIV*UREP$ABS.DD ,,APPFIV . .

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'DBK' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */DBK

7.2.30 DBK

The DBK macro allows the user to encode or decode database keys and pointers.

7.2.30.1 Syntax

1. DBK [<area>],<page>,<record/slot>

2. DBK <database key>

7.2.30.2 Discussion

Format 1 will encode (build) a database key while format 2 will decode a database key. Both formats are illustrated in the sample output. If no <area> specification is given, the current area will be assumed.

The <area> specification in format 1 may be any of the specifications legal for the 'AREA' command. The database key/pointer in format 2 is assumed to be an octal number, regardless of whether it is preceeded with a zero or not.

7.2.30.3 Sample Output

>DBK 593,1,3 DATABASE KEY/POINTER = 450400100003

>DBK 0450400100003 AREA: UTP-PROBLEMS (593) PAGE: 1 RECORD/SLOT: 3

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'DIAGRAM' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */DIAGRAM

7.2.31 DIAGRAM

The DIAGRAM macro produces a "picture" of the records and set relationships of the currently-loaded schema.

7.2.31.1 Syntax

DIAGRAM[,L] [<bar-char>]

7.2.31.2 Options

None A bubble diagram will be generated. The listing will be generated at 8 lines-per-inch with no margins. You may have to piece the listing together to produce the complete picture.

L In addition to the bubble listing, a level listing will be generated. This is the first part of the listing shown for the DIAGRAM macro in Figure 1-3.

7.2.31.3 Discussion

The discussion for Figure 1-3 describes the macro sufficiently. If the <bar-char> is not specified, the letter "I" will be used as a vertical bar. Any character (such as an explanation mark) may be specified if your printer supports that character.

The listing will be annotated with page numbers. By aligning pages side-by-side (ascending page numbers from left to right) you will be able to get the complete diagram. Try it on a schema whose structure you are familiar with.

7.2.31.4 Sample Output

See Figure 1-3.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'DIRECT' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */DIRECT

7.2.32 DIRECT

This macro enables the user to locate a record given its database key or pointer. The record may be direct, via set or calc.

7.2.32.1 Syntax

1. DIRECT[,<option>] [<area>],<page>,<record/slot>

2. DIRECT[,<option>] <database key/pointer>

7.2.32.2 Options

None The third field is a record number (format 1) or the parameter is a database key (format 2).

 

P The third field is a slot number (format 1) or the parameter is a database pointer (format 2).

7.2.32.3 Discussion

Format 1 allows you to supply the separate components of a database key/pointer whereas format 2 requires the actual octal database key/pointer itself.

The <area> specification in format 1 is optional and, if absent, will allow the DIRECT macro to default to the current area. If present, it may be any of the area specifications legal on the 'AREA' command. The database key/pointer in format 2 is assumed to be an octal number, regardless of whether it is preceeded with a zero or not.

7.2.32.4 Sample Output

See Figure 1-7.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'DISCEDIT' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */DISCEDIT

7.2.33 DISCEDIT

This macro allows the user to perform editing operations on a disc file (TIP/DMS or EXEC) similar to those of such file-patch utilities as @FANG or @FED.

7.2.33.1 Syntax

1. DISCEDIT <filename>

2. DISCEDIT,T <TIP/DMS file number>

7.2.33.2 Discussion

Format 1 will initiate editing of an EXEC file while format two will do the same for a TIP/DMS file.

Note that this macro incorporates all system macros beginning with the characters "DISC$". Those macros are not to be used by the user directly nor are they to be used by user-written macros.

The following are the commands recognized by this macro (in alphabetical order):

Command Syntax Command Use ------- ------ ------- ---

<Word number> Go to the given word and print it in the current default print format.

 

+<Nwords> Move forward the given number of words, returning to the first buffer word if the value of <nwords> would cause you to go past the last word.

 

-[<Nwords>] Move backward the given number of words (the default value for <nwords> is 1), stopping at the first word if <nwords> is too large.

 

BLOCK <number> Define the size of blocks to be read or written (words). The value will be rounded up to a sector (28 words) boundary. This command will erase the buffer contents.

 

EXIT Quit and return to DBE conversational mode.

 

FORMAT,AOF Any combination of "A", "O" and "F" may be supplied to be set as the default print format.

 

GET <block> Get the given block number from the file. Note that the current block size (see the 'BLOCK' command) will be used to determine the actual disc sector address along with the <block> number.

 

N Move to the next buffer word, returning to the first word if an attempt is made to pass the end of the buffer.

 

NAME Print the name of the file being edited.

 

NARROW Restrict printing to an 80-column (CRT screen) width.

 

ORIGIN <0/1> Specify whether the first word of the buffer and the first block of the file are to be called "0" or "1".

 

P#,AOF Note that the # is an exclamation point. Print the entire buffer in octal and/or Fieldata and/or ASCII (or the default format if no options are specified). Following the print you will remain positioned at the word you were at when you did the print.

 

P,AOF <nwords> Print <nwords> words in the desired format(s) beginning with the current word. You will remain positioned at the last word printed. If no print format is given, the default format will be used.

 

P,AOF <first>,<last> Print words <first> through <last> of the buffer. You will remain positioned at the last word printed.

 

PATCH <value>[,<jdesig>] Patch the specified part of the word (a standard DBE j-designator name) with the specified value.

 

PUT [<block>] Write the current buffer to the specified block. If no block is given, the block last referenced by 'GET' will be assumed.

 

SEND Resume printing at the terminal (see 'SITE').

 

SITE [<pid>] Exactly like the 'SITE' macro.

 

TOC,AROSD <elt/vers>,<subtype> Just like the 'TOC' macro, but the file being edited will be assumed.

 

WIDE Use a wide (132 column) print format.

7.2.33.3 Sample Output

See Figure 1-15.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'DMSCALC' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */DMSCALC

7.2.34 DMSCALC

This macro allows the user to locate a calc record within the database controlled by the current schema provided its location mode is via the DMSCALC procedure.

7.2.34.1 Syntax

DMSCALC[,<option>] [<area>],[<record>],[<key value>]

7.2.34.2 Options

None The <key value> will be used as the key for the DMSCALC process. If none is supplied, the user will be prompted for one (demand) or an error message will result (batch). The mode of the record will be used to dictate whether the key should be converted to ASCII or not.

 

B The <key value>, if any, will be ignored. A key of spaces (Fieldata or ASCII, as appropriate) will be used.

 

Z The <key value>, if any, will be ignored. A key of binary zeros will be used.

7.2.34.3 Discussion

<Area> is a specification of the area in which the record would be stored. This specification may be any that is legal on the 'AREA' command. If absent, the current area will be used.

<Record> is a specification of the record type you are looking for. This specification may be any that is legal on the 'RECORD' command. If absent, the current record will be used.

The <key value> should not be expressed within quotes unless the quotes are to be actual characters within the key.

After determining the page and chain number, this macro will fetch the appropriate page and begin searching the correct calc chain until it either finds the record of the correct type having the given <key value> or reaches the end of the calc chain (the point where it cycles back to the chain header word); this second condition would cause a "***RECORD NOT FOUND***" message to be printed.

As synonyms are found during the calc chain scan, the user will be told of the actual key values and record names of those synonym records.

If the location mode is via the user written CALCASE procedure, the CALCASE macro will automatically be called to find the record.

7.2.34.4 Sample Output

See Figure 1-7.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'DMU-INVOKE' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */DMU-INVOKE

7.2.35 DMU-INVOKE

This macro will create an SDF file containing a DMU processor call and INVOKE statement for the currently based schema.

7.2.35.1 Syntax

DMU-INVOKE [<alias-name>]

7.2.35.2 Options

L List output as it is written to SDF file.

7.2.35.3 Discussion

<Alias-name> can be specified to force a specific UDS application group to be used to invoke the DMU subschema for the current schema. This is required when invoking the DMU subschema for the SCHEMATA schema.

The SDF file created will be "DMU-INVOKE$." with an @USE name of "DMU$C".

If access keys exist for DMU, INVOKE and/or IMPART, these will be taken from the DMU subschema and added to the INVOKE syntax.

It is not neccessary to base the DMU subschema prior to calling this macro. The macro will determine the correct subschema regardless of which , if any , subschema is based.

7.2.35.4 Sample Output

*:>SCHEMATA 3

 

*:>DMU-INVOKE,L

@UDS$$SRC*DMRMT$.DMU,L ,,UDSSRC INVOKE SUBSCHEMA SCHEMATADMU FILE UDS$$SRC*DDL$

SCHEMA SCHEMATA KEY FOR INVOKE IS 'DDS$DMU'.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'DOWN-AREAS' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */DOWN-AREAS

7.2.36 DOWN-AREAS

This macro will create an SDF file containing a DMU or IRU processor call to down selected areas.

7.2.36.1 Syntax

DOWN-AREAS[,<options>] [<mask>][,<alias-name>]

7.2.36.2 Options

A Append output to previously created down file.

I Down Immediate.

L List output as it is written to SDF file.

S Down schema file.

U Down for Update.

X Use "Q" option on IRU call / "X" option on DMU call.

7.2.36.3 Discussion

If <mask> is supplied, only areas matching the <mask> specification will be downed. If <mask> is omitted, all areas in the schema will be downed.

<Alias-name> can be specified to force a specific UDS application group to be used for the IRU/DMU. This is required when downing areas for the SCHEMATA schema.

The SDF file created will be "DOWN$." with an @USE name of "DFILE".

7.2.36.4 Sample Output

*:>FILMGT-SCH

 

*:>DOWN-AREAS,ILX

@UDS$$SVN*IRU.IRU,EIQUX . . DOWN IMMEDIATE FILE 595#LOGICAL-AREA FILE 596#FILE-AREA FILE 597#IO-AREA FILE 598#FILE-HIST FILE 599#LOGICAL-HIST FILE 2339#ATT-AREA-1 FILE 2348#ATT-AREA-2 ;

ACT APPL APPSVN ; END ; @EOF

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'DPATCH' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */DPATCH

7.2.37 DPATCH

The DPATCH macro is an alternative to the PATCH macro when a database is to be patched (modified) using DBE. This macro enables the user to use the powerful DBE capabilities to determine the necessary patch(s) and then automatically generate patch directives for the DMS/1100 data management utility (DMU). In this manner, any alterations to the database will be performed by the DMR using its audit-trail capability.

7.2.37.1 Syntax

1. DPATCH,F <filename>[.<element>[/<version>]]

2. DPATCH [<expression>]

3. DPATCH,E

7.2.37.2 Discussion

Format 1 should be used prior to the others to define an OS/1100 file.elt/version into which the generated DMU patch directives may be written. Failure to do this will cause the DPATCH macro to assume TPF$.PATCHELT (this will be done the first time you try to patch).

Format 2 is used to actually generate a DMU 'PATCH' image. The user must position to the desired word of the desired page and use this format to alter that word's contents. The contents of the word will be altered to the value of <expression> - not now, but later when the DMU is invoked. All DBE will actually do is write the appropriate DMU 'PATCH' directive to the patch file (format 1) for later use by the DMU. A copy of the PATCH directive image will be printed at the terminal. If no <expression> is supplied, the user will be prompted for one.

Format 3 is used to signal the end of patching and close the patch element. This will be done automatically when you leave DBE if you forget. The responsibility of calling the DMU, invoking the appropriate subschema and @ADDing the patch file/element created here will be yours.

7.2.37.3 Sample Output

See Figure 1-10.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'DT-STAMP' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */DT-STAMP

7.2.38 DT-STAMP

This macro decodes a DMS/1100 12-digit octal date/time stamp into its equivalent date (MM/DD/YY) and time (HH:MM:SS).

7.2.38.1 Syntax

DT-STAMP <date-time-stamp>

7.2.38.2 Discussion

None.

7.2.38.3 Sample Output

>DT-STAMP 0123451543210 DATE-TIME STAMP: 123451543210 DECODES TO: 02/19/73 22:35:18

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'DUMPATT' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */DUMPATT

7.2.39 DUMPATT

This macro allows summary information about blocks on an audit trail tape to be dumped.

This macro works only with audit-trail tapes produced by DMS/1100 level 8R2 or prior.

7.2.39.1 Syntax

DUMPATT[,C] [<block-count>]

7.2.39.2 Discussion

The optional <block-count> is an expression indicating the number of blocks to dump (the default is one). The 'C' option (which overrides <block-count>, if given) will cause continuous dumping to an end-of-file.

The macro requires that the audit-trail tape be 'OPEN'ed with a fileid of "ATT".

7.2.39.3 Sample Output

See Figure 1-11.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'DUMPREC' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */DUMPREC

7.2.40 DUMPREC

This macro will produce a listing of the pointers of a record on the database. No data elements (other than calc and sort keys, if any) will be printed. See the 'DATA' and 'REC-DDL' macros for methods with which the data area of a record may be printed.

7.2.40.1 Syntax

DUMPREC[<,options>] [<rhw-address>]

where <rhw-address> is the word address on the current page where the record header word for the desired record may be found. If this is not specified the assumption will be made that the current table is a database page and that the current word of that page is the desired record header word (if that assumption is incorrect strange results - probably DBE error messages - will result).

7.2.40.2 Options

D Decode the database key.

 

H Display database key and record header information only.

7.2.40.3 Discussion

The record header word address is the value contained in the page displacement portion of record pointers at the foot of each page (see the SLOTS macro).

Note that the pointers are all decoded, showing the sets and types of pointers for those sets that they relate to. Each pointer will have a "link reference number" associated with it (see the LINK macro) within square brackets, i.e. [02]. This is merely the relative pointer number for the record (1st, 2nd, 3rd, etc.) and may be used by the LINK macro to link to the next record (or prior record, etc.) of any set indicated in the output.

7.2.40.4 Sample Output

Figures 1-6 and 1-7 show many macros using the DUMPREC macro to print records on a data page.

The following illustrates the output for indexed pointer and pointer array records:

>DUMPREC

INDEXED P/A SET TYPE: 1054 (MMISPR-PTR), DBP=100000100001, DBK=100000100001.

AT WORDS 012-020, LENGTH: 7. MEMBER DBP'S: 1

RECORD FLAGS: 010 (IN USE)

 

I/S LINK: [1] 000000000000

OWNER DBP: [2] 077401200010 = AREA 127, PAGE 10, PGSLOT 8.

IPA KEY='006463304'

 

[3] 101052000030

>DUMPREC

P/A SET TYPE: 1052 (MMISPR-RATE-RATE), DBP=102400100002, DBK=102400100002.

AT WORDS 015-030, LENGTH: 12. MEMBER DBP'S: 11

RECORD FLAGS: 010 (IN USE)

 

[1] 101013040013 [2] 101013320125 [3] 101014140033

[4] 101014140060 [5] 101014160031 [6] 101021260056

[7] 101021400103 [8] 101032700071 [9] 101033640065

[10] 101045060074 [11] 101057300024

7.2.41 EDMAC

The EDMAC macro can be used as a quick way to edit macros being developed. By supplying a macro name as a parameter, edmac will perform an @ED,U on that element in the current user library file (See the LIB macro).

7.2.41.1 Syntax

7.2.41.2 Discussion

None.

| Chapter 7 | 'ELAPSED-TIME' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */ELAPSED-TIME

7.2.42 ELAPSED-TIME

This macro is used to display the elapsed time, in milliseconds, between the current time and a previously saved time.

7.2.42.1 Syntax

ELAPSED-TIME <start-time>

7.2.42.2 Discussion

The <start-time> must be a 1 word variable previously loaded from the system variable "MSTIME".

The value of the system variable "RESULT" will be the elapsed time in milliseconds.

7.2.42.3 Output

*:>LET Z=MSTIME

 

*:>ELAPSED-TIME Z

 

ELAPSED MILLISECONDS: 4738

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'EXPLAIN' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */EXPLAIN

7.2.43 EXPLAIN

This macro allows the user to get explanations of DBE errors and DBE macros.

7.2.43.1 Syntax

EXPLAIN [<expression>]

7.2.43.2 Discussion

The <expression> supplied must evaluate to a non-negative value. It will be treated as the error number to be explained. If no <expression> is supplied, the error number of the most-recently received DBE error will be assumed.

The message defined for the given error number will be printed along with a paragraph or two describing the error and possibly suggesting one or more ways in which the problem causing the error could be avoided.

The actual text of the error explanations is stored as a series of SDF elements (one element per error) in the DBE help library file (DBE$HELPLIB). The elements will be named:

 

E$#/EXPLANATION

where the "#" represents the error number.

The actual text of the macro explanations is stored as a series of SDF elements (one element per macro) in the DBE help library file (DBE$HELPLIB). The elements will be named:

 

T$######/EXPLANATION

where the ###### represents the macro name.

7.2.43.3 Sample Output

See Figure 1-14.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'FACERR' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

7.2.44 FACERR

The FACERR macro will decode an Exec Facility status (similar to @FAC processor.

7.2.44.1 Syntax

7.2.44.2 Discussion

If the fac-status-code is not supplied (in octal) then the most recent facility status returned to DBE will be decoded.

7.2.44.3 Sample Output

*:>SCH DA0*ABS-FMGGEV.FMGDEV-SCH <2> FAC REJECT: 400010000000 ON @ASG OF SCHEMA/SUBSCHEMA FILE

*:>FACERR 400010000000 \^\^REQUEST NOT ACCEPTED \^\^FILE DOES NOT EXIST

7.2.46 FETCH

The FETCH macro is used to retrieve a record in the current area in a "Fetch First / Fetch Next" fashion.

7.2.46.1 Syntax

FETCH[,<options>] [<record-name>]

7.2.46.2 Options

A Match any record type.

 

C Continous fetch

 

D Call DATA macro for each record fetched.

 

F Start fetching from page 1.

 

H Dump database key and record header info.

 

N Fetch next record of same type as current.

 

K Dump key if location mode is Calc or Index/Sequential.

 

S Dump set pointers by calling DUMPREC macro.

7.2.46.3 Discussion

None.

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */FITEM

7.2.49 FITEM

The FITEM macro displays FITEM$ information about a file.

7.2.49.1 Syntax

FITEM <file-name>

7.2.49.2 Discussion

Either an internal filename (@USE-name) or an external filename (with or without a qualifier) may be specified as the <file-name> parameter. If the file is not assigned to the calling job when the macro is called, the macro will assign the file, and will free it at macro termination. This macro may be used to describe word- or sector-addressable mass-storage, or tape files. Other file types (e.g., communications channels) are not supported.

7.2.49.3 Sample Output

>fitem filex.

 

FITEM$ INFORMATION FOR DISK FILE 'FILEX'

PREPARED ON 03/30/87 AT 10:26:47

| Chapter 7 | 'IFETCH' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */IFETCH

7.2.54 IFETCH

The IFETCH macro is used to "Fetch" a record with location mode of index sequential in a manner similar to the DMSCALC macro.

7.2.54.1 Syntax

IFETCH [<area>],[<key-value>]

7.2.54.2 Options

D Call DATA macro to dump data portion of record.

 

M Display "Map" of records physically walked on pages.

7.2.54.3 Discussion

If only one parameter is passed, it will be assumed to be the I/S key and the current area will be used. As only one I/S record type is allowed in an area, the record name is not a parameter as in DMSCALC.

Note that the IFETCH macro operates as if the RANGE KEY option were specified in the schema description - if the record with the exact key specified does not exist, the record with the next higher (in sort sequence) key will be returned.

7.2.54.4 Sample Output

*:>IFETCH 000005

RECORD POINTS TO PAGE 5

RECORD TYPE: 1030 (EMPLOYEE-TIME), DBP=277300005001, DBK=277300005001

AT WORDS 012-01611, LENGTH: 896. RECORD FLAGS: 010 (IN USE)

 

--INDEX SEQUENTIAL POINTERS -------------> [1] NEXT: 000000000000

 

I/S KEY='000005'

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| MACROS | |

*// */ILINK

7.2.55 ILINK

The ILINK macro is used to "walk" Index-Sequential records in an area. This is similar to the DML command "Fetch next within --- record" syntax.

7.2.55.1 Syntax

ILINK[,<options>] [<repeat-count>]

7.2.55.2 Options

C Continue fetching records until the repeat-count is reached or end of area is reached.

 

D Call DATA to display data portion of record.

 

F Find first I/S record in the current area.

 

M Display "Map" of records walked on pages.

 

N Do NOT call DUMPREC macro.

 

P Check current page only

7.2.55.3 Discussion

None.

7.2.55.4 Sample Output

*:>ILINK,F RECORD TYPE: 1030 (EMPLOYEE-TIME), DBP=277300005001, DBK=277300005001

AT WORDS 012-01611, LENGTH: 896. RECORD FLAGS: 010 (IN USE)

 

--INDEX SEQUENTIAL POINTERS -------------> [1] NEXT: 000000000000

 

I/S KEY='000005'

*:>ILINK RECORD TYPE: 1030 (EMPLOYEE-TIME), DBP=277300008001, DBK=277300008001

AT WORDS 012-01611, LENGTH: 896. RECORD FLAGS: 010 (IN USE)

 

--INDEX SEQUENTIAL POINTERS -------------> [1] NEXT: 000000000000

7.2.56 ILI-TO-ONE

The ILI-TO-ONE Macro is used to patch the Illogical Last Insert Point for the current area back to Page 1.

| Chapter 7 | 'ILLPR-CLEAR' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */ILLPR-CLEAR

7.2.57 ILLPR-CLEAR

The ILLLPR-CLEAR macro is used to create an SDF file containing DMU commands to clear the Initial Load in progress flag set when a run which opens an area for initial load error terminates.

7.2.57.1 Syntax

ILLPR-CLEAR[,<options>]

7.2.57.2 Options

L List output as it is written to SDF file.

7.2.57.3 Discussion

If a run opens an area for initial load and error terminates, the area is left in a state where it can only be opened for initial load - retrieval or update modes are not allowed. This macro creates syntax to initialize the area starting at the last prime page, which will cause the flag to be cleared. The area can then be restored and subsequent open commands will work.

The area which needs the Initial Load flag cleared must be based before calling this macro.

The SDF file created is "ILLPR-CLEAR$" with an @USE name of "ILLPRC".

7.2.57.4 Output

*:>FILMGT-SCH

 

*:>AREA ATT-AREA-1

 

*:>ILLPR-CLEAR,L

@UDS$$SVN*DMRMT$.DMU,L ,,APPSVN INVOKE SUBSCHEMA DMU-FILMGT TIP FILE 408

SCHEMA FILMGT-SCH. INITIALIZE AREA ATT-AREA-2 BEGIN AT PAGE 2011. @EOF

RUNSTREAM IS IN "ILLPR-CLEAR$." WITH @USE NAME OF "ILLPRC."

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */LIB

7.2.60 LIB (LIBRARY)

 

The LIB macro allows the user to alter the user macro library specification that was supplied as <spec1> of the DBE processor call.

7.2.60.1 Syntax

LIB [<user-macro-file-name>]

7.2.60.2 Discussion

This macro operates by attaching the @USE name of DBE$PF to the file supplied on the macro call.

If no <file-name> is specified, the current user library file-name will be displayed.

7.2.60.3 Sample Output

*:>LIB MY*FILE. THE USER LIBRARY IS NOW MY*FILE(1).

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'LINK' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */LINK

7.2.61 LINK

Once you have used the DUMPREC macro to list the pointers for a record, you may link to the next record in any chain represented by those pointers using this macro.

7.2.61.1 Syntax

LINK[,<options> <pointer-#>[,<repeat-count>]

7.2.61.2 Options

None The link will be done the number of times specified by the <repeat-count> parameter, producing a full listing for each record found.

 

C The link will be done continuously, for record-after-record in the chain being traversed, until LINK returns to the original record.

 

D When each link is performed, the 'DATA' macro will be called to display the data portion of the record.

 

N No printing will occur during the linking process, except for printing the number of records spanned upon completion (only for the 'C' option or when a <repeat-count> is specified). Contrast with the 'S' option.

 

S When each link is performed, the listing will include only a two-line statement of how the pointer being used at the moment decodes (no DUMPREC listing will be produced). The number of records spanned will be printed upon completion (only for the 'C' option or when a <repeat-count> is specified). Contrast with the 'N' option.

7.2.61.3 Discussion

The <pointer-#> parameter is required, and is an expression evaluating to the pointer number to be used within the record whose record header word you are currently positioned to (the 'DMSCALC', 'DIRECT' and 'FIND' macros will leave you positioned at the appropriate record header word). When a listing of the record is produced via the DUMPREC macro, each pointer will be labeled with its pointer number to facilitate use of this macro.

The optional <repeat-count> parameter is an expression evaluating to the number of times you wish to link (i.e., the number of records to span on the chain). The 'C' option, if specified, will override this parameter. The desired number of records will be spanned (and printed as per the presence/absence of the 'N' and 'S' options) and, when done, the macro will terminate. If no <repeat-count> is given and the 'C' option is not specified, you will be prompted for a command following the link. Simply entering a null input (hitting transmit/return) will cause the link to begin anew from the current record doing an additional link. Entering any DBE command/macro call will terminate 'LINK' and execute the command.

7.2.61.4 Sample Output

See Figure 1-7.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

7.2.65 NEXTREC

This macro may be used to give a DUMPREC listing of the record which is physically next on the current page.

7.2.65.1 Syntax

NEXTREC

7.2.65.2 Discussion

Prior to calling the 'NEXTREC' macro, the current table pointer must be positioned to a record header word on a database page. This macro will move the page pointer to the record header word for the record which is physically next on the page and call the 'DUMPREC' macro for that record.

7.2.65.3 Sample Output

The output will be a DUMPREC listing of the next record on the page (if any).

7.2.67 OPTALK

This macro enables the DBE user to hold a two-way conversation with the onsite console operator.

7.2.67.1 Syntax

OPTALK

7.2.67.2 Discussion

None.

7.2.67.3 Sample Output

The following dialog would take place at the user terminal (note that anything that appears after a '>' was typed by the user):

 

> optalk

MESSAGE?> has tape 022323 been delivered yet?

CONSOLE REPLY: NO IT HASNT...

MESSAGE?> ok...when it arrives, it needs a ring

CONSOLE REPLY: OK

MESSAGE?>

*:>

The user entered a null input after the last "MESSAGE?", thus terminating the macro (and the conversation).

Meanwhile, the dialogue would appear as follows at the operator's console:

 

0-HAS TAPE 022323 BEEN DELIVERED YET?

0 NO IT HASN'T...

0-OK...WHEN IT ARRIVES, IT NEEDS A RING

0 OK

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'OVERFLOW' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */OVERFLOW

7.2.68 OVERFLOW

This macro determines what prime pages in a DARP area have overflow pages chained to them, and exactly how many overflow pages each prime page has. A histogram is then produced showing the prime pages broken up into the following groups:

 

- Those having 1 overflow page

- Those having 2 overflow pages

- Those having 3 overflow pages

- Those having 4 overflow pages

- Those having 5 overflow pages

- Those having 6 overflow pages

- Those having 7 overflow pages

- Those having 8 overflow pages

- Those having 9 overflow pages

- Those having 10 overflow pages

- Those having from 11 to 99 overflow pages

- Those having more than 99 overflow pages

7.2.68.1 Syntax

OVERFLOW [<min>][,<max>]

7.2.68.2 Discussion

The macro will, in addition to producing the histogram, provide for listing the page numbers of those prime pages having overflow (and how many overflow pages they have). The minimum and/or maximum number of overflow pages that a prime page must have in order to be included in this second listing will be requested by the macro. Note that in batch mode this second listing will automatically be generated for all possible overflow chain lengths.

The two parameters are the minimum/maximum chain lengths for the second listing (of prime page numbers and overflow chain lengths). The defaults for these parameters are 1 for <min> and infinity for <max> (thus printing all). The parameters are ignored by demand jobs, since they will be able conversationally to get the second listing (or prevent it).

The area, schema name, date and time are clearly shown in the output.

The total number of prime and overflow pages are given with their sum (total number of pages in the area) beneath them. The percentage figure after the overflow page count shows what percentage of the total number of pages in the area are overflow pages.

The total number of prime pages that have overflow are printed on the third line of the output. In addition, this count's percentage of the total number of prime pages is given, also on the third line.

The rows of stars going across the page indicate prime pages. They may be scaled so that each star represents a single prime page, or due to the number of pages to be represented on the histogram they may denote more than one page. The scale at the bottom may be used to get an approximate count for any row, and the number in the 'COUNT' column may be used to get the exact count. The percentage figure in the 'PCT' column shows, for that row of stars, what percentage that row represents of the total number of prime pages getting plotted.

After the histogram will come the listing of those prime pages that have overflow along with how many overflow pages each one has. This will be generated automatically for the batch user according to the selection criteria given by the two parameters to the macro. The demand user will, conversationally, be able to produce the same listing. The remainder of this discussion pertains only to the demand user.

The user will be asked if a detailed page display is desired. If the response is 'YES', the user is asked for the minimum and maximum overflow chain counts that are desired. Entering a null input (no chain count) will terminate the macro. The meanings of these two inputs are similar to the parameters that may be given by a batch user. After printing the list of all the pages satisfying the criteria selected, the user will have the opportunity to enter a new set of minimum/maximum specifications. This process will continue until the user enters a null input.

The detailed page listing will list prime pages and their counts of overflow pages in a format such that if prime page 200 had 16 overflow pages, it would appear as:

200/16

7.2.68.3 Sample Output

See Figure 1-8.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'OVERFLOW-ALL' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */OVERFLOW-ALL

7.2.69 OVERFLOW-ALL

This macro does an 'OVERFLOW' for all or some DARP areas in the current schema. For the batch user the prime page chain length detail listing will always assume 1-infinity for the chain lengths (thus printing all).

The demand user will be given the opportunity to get detailed page listings for each area.

7.2.69.1 Syntax

OVERFLOW-ALL [<mask>]

7.2.69.2 Discussion

If the optional <mask> parameter is supplied, only those DARP areas whose names match the mask defined by <mask> will be reported. The absence of <mask> will cause all DARP areas to be reported.

7.2.69.3 Sample Output

An "OVERFLOW" listing will be generated for each area selected.

| Chapter 7 | 'PAGE-COPY' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */PAGE-COPY

7.2.71 PAGE-COPY

This macro copies database pages updated after a specified date/time to and from an SDF file.

7.2.71.1 Syntax

PAGE-COPY [,<options>]

7.2.71.2 Options

A Abort DBE if an error occurs.

L List Pages being copied.

S Save pages to SDF file.

R Restore pages from SDF file.

7.2.71.3 Discussion

The S or R opotion is required. If omitted, the macro will error terminate.

The update date/time used for comparison when using the "S" option to save pages to the SDF file must be called "<schema>*DATEFILE." and will have an @USE name of "DATFIL." attached. This file must be a permanently catalogued file as the macro will first @FREE the file before assigning it.

The "Page Save" SDF file must be called "<schema>*UPDTFILE." and will have an @USE name of "UPDFIL." attached. This file must be a permanently catalogued file as the macro will first @FREE the file before assigning it.

After copying out all pages ("S" option specified), the DATFIL will be updated with the date/time from the start of the macro. This will be in the format YYMMDDHHMMSS.

While no special privileges are required to save pages with the "S" option, the user must have "Update" privilege in order to copy pages back to the database via the "R" option.

7.2.71.4 Sample Output

*:>PRT,S CNSDEV-SCH*DATEFILE.

CNSDEV-SCH*DATEFILE(1).

1: 930913162455 2: YYMMDDHHMMSS

 

*:>PAGE-COPY,S

SAVING PAGES UPDATED AFTER 93/09/13 16:24:55 FOR SCHEMA CNSDEV-SCH

 

113 OF 114 ( 99%) PAGES SAVED FOR AREA CNS-CONTROL (1374)

10 OF 539 ( 2%) PAGES SAVED FOR AREA CNS-PARA (1391)

0 OF 24 ( 0%) PAGES SAVED FOR AREA CNS-TABLE (1392)

0 OF 47 ( 0%) PAGES SAVED FOR AREA CNS-TEXT-E (1393)

0 OF 11 ( 0%) PAGES SAVED FOR AREA CNS-TEXT-E-I (1394)

0 OF 56 ( 0%) PAGES SAVED FOR AREA CNS-TEXT-S (2351)

0 OF 11 ( 0%) PAGES SAVED FOR AREA CNS-TEXT-S-I (2352)

| Chapter 7 | 'PAGE-USAGE' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */PAGE-USAGE

7.2.72 PAGE-USAGE

This macro produces a histogram illustrating the manner in which pages are being used in the current area. The histogram will show the percentage of space on pages that is still available for use. These percentages will be broken down into the following categories:

 

- 0-9% available (full)

- 10-19% available

- 20-29% available

- 30-39% available

- 40-49% available

- 50-59% available

- 60-69% available

- 70-79% available

- 80-89% available

- 90-99% available

- 100% available (empty)

- Unallocated [optional]

The final category (unallocated) will show the number of overflow pages remaining to be allocated for a DARP area. This is an indicator of how full an area is in terms of allocated pages. Logically speaking these 'unallocated' pages are empty.

7.2.72.1 Syntax

PAGE-USAGE[,<options>] [<min>][,<max>]

7.2.72.2 Options

L Combination of 'O', 'P', and 'T' options.

O Analyze overflow pages only.

P Analyze prime pages only.

T Print totals by page type.

7.2.72.3 Discussion

Only pages <min> through <max> will be scanned. The defaults are 1 for <min> and 'last page in area' for <max>.

The header immediately above the histogram indicates what pages were selected due to the parameter(s) supplied.

Each horizontal row of stars indicates how many of the selected pages had a percentage of available (unused) space on them that fell into the range indicated to the left of the row.

Actual counts and percentages of total pages selected are given to the right of each row of stars.

For SARP areas, "prime" means all pages up to the first "AT END" overflow page.

7.2.72.4 Sample Output

See Figure 1-8.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'PAGE-USAGE-ALL' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */PAGE-USAGE-ALL

PAGE-USAGE-ALL[,<options>] [<mask>]

7.2.73.2 Options

O Analyze overflow pages only.

7.2.73.3 Discussion

A 'PAGE-USAGE' (with the given <options>, <min>, and <max>) will be performed for all areas selected. Presence of the optional <mask> parameter will cause only those areas whose names match the <mask> to be reported. Absence of the <mask> parameter will cause all areas to be reported.

7.2.73.4 Sample Output

None.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'PATCH' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */PATCH

7.2.74 PATCH

This macro is used to patch any DBE table/array in core, replacing the value of all or a portion of the current table word with a new value.

7.2.74.1 Syntax

PATCH <expression>[,<jdesignator>]

7.2.74.2 Discussion

The current word of the current table will be modified. If no <jdesignator> is given, the entire word will get the value of <expression>. If a <jdesignator> is given, then only that portion of the current word will get the value of <expression>.

If a table is specified, only the in-core value of that table is modified. The 'REWRITE' command must be used to actually write a 'PATCH'ed table back to disc. Note that <j-designator> of 'W' means bit 4 as opposed to the whole word. If an entire word is to be patched, the user must omit the <j-designator> parameter.

7.2.74.3 Sample Output

This macro produces no output.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'PATCH-FREE-O' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */PATCH-FREE-O

7.2.75 PATCH-FREE-O

This macro is used to create DMU page patch commands (via the DPATCH macro) to set the prime page associated with each overflow page on the free page chain to 0.

7.2.75.1 Syntax

PATCH-FREE-O[,<options>]

7.2.75.2 Options

None Open the patch file if closed, leave open if already open. Leave patch file open at macro completion.

 

C Close the patch file at macro completion.

 

O Close and re-open the patch file if already open.

7.2.75.3 Discussion

When a DMU page compaction is executed, overflow pages which are completely empty are returned to the unused overflow chain. The prime page number associated with the overflow page (PH[6]:H1) is NOT reset to 0. This causes the DBE overflow page related macros (SCAN-ONE, OVERFLOW, etc.) to incorrectly associate the overlow page with the original prime page. This macro will allow those macros to produce correct results.

If DMS code is changed to zero out the prime page number, this macro will no longer be needed.

7.2.75.4 Sample Output

See the DPATCH macro for examples.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'PATHLIST' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */PATHLIST

7.2.76 PATHLIST

This macro will list for each path defined in the current subschema pertinent information found in the Path Index Table (PIT) and Path Description Table (PDT).

7.2.76.1 Syntax

PATHLIST

7.2.76.2 Discussion

The output is grouped so that multiple path table entries for any path appear together. The characteristics of these entries are detailed horizontally in the table:

 

- PSEQ NUM: Path sequence number.

- PDT: Indicator as to whether or not a PDT entry exists.

- PRIV FLAG: Indicator for private access to path.

- ROOT RECORD NAME: Name of root record for path.

- ROOT LOC MODE: Location mode of root record.

- # PATH STEPS: Number of path steps (or sets) involved in path.

| Chapter 7 | 'PATHSTEPS' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */PATHSTEPS

7.2.77 PATHSTEPS

This macro will list each step defined in a path. The path to be analyzed must have been obtained thru a previous 'PATH' command.

7.2.77.1 Syntax

PATHSTEPS

7.2.77.2 Discussion

The output of this macro includes the output resulting from a null 'PATH' command along with a description of each step of the path. The first record name given is the origination record. The set through which the path is defined can be found next. Certain set characteristics will be listed beside the set name if they exist. They are:

- DQUAL: Data qualification required.

- NORETR: No data retrieval allowed.

- SETOWN: Set is owned by the destination record.

- MULTI: Set is a multimember set.

- MANUAL: Set is defined as a manual set rather than automatic. The third line of output contains the record name of the destination record. If more than one path step is defined, each will appear in the above format.

7.2.77.3 Sample Output

*:>PATH 37

*:>PATHSTEPS

****************** <PATHSTEPS> ********************

PATH: P-RQ-IT PATH SEQ NUMBER: 37

SUBSCHEMA: S-QLP-FAMIS FILE: SYS*UNIDMS.

SCHEMA: STEST-SCHEMA FILE: SYS*UNIDMS.

 

: PATH : RECORD: REQ-DUMMY THRU

: STEP : SET: REQDUMMY-FORMS TO

: # 1 : RECORD: FORMS-REC

 

: PATH : RECORD: FORMS-REC THRU

: STEP : SET: FORMS-ITEM TO

: # 2 : RECORD: ITEM-REC

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'PGDUMP' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */PGDUMP

7.2.81 PGDUMP

This macro will produce a formatted listing of an entire database page. The contents of the listing will resemble a combination of the DMU 'PRINT' and 'DUMP' functions.

7.2.81.1 Syntax

PGDUMP [<page specification>]

7.2.81.2 Discussion

The <page specification> is the same as for the 'PAGE' command. If the <page specification> field is absent, the macro will dump the current page.

The actual data contents of records dumped will be dumped both in octal and character representations. The characterset used depends on the record mode as defined in the schema.

This macro may be used only to dump pages from data areas.

7.2.81.3 Sample Output

See Figure 1-5.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'PGSLOT' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */PGSLOT

7.2.82 PGSLOT

This macro allows the user to specify a page slot number on the current page to be used to locate a record. The record found will then be printed using the DUMPREC macro.

7.2.82.1 Syntax

PGSLOT <expression>

7.2.82.2 Discussion

The value of <expression> must be non-negative and not greater than the number of records slots on the current page plus the number of calc chains configured at the bottom of the page.

The macro will make a determination whether the slot referred to is a calc chain header or a record slot. If a calc chain header, it will be decoded and the appropriate record slot determined. The record will then be printed using the DUMPREC macro.

7.2.82.3 Sample Output

The output will be a standard DUMPREC listing.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'PH' Macro |

7.2.83.3 Discussion

7.2.85 PRIME-PATCH

This macro allows easy changing of the Prime Pages, Calc Chains, "Every .. Pages", "Interval..." and "Overflow At End" clauses in the ART for the current area.

7.2.85.1 Syntax

PRIME-PATCH [<prime-pages>],[<calc-chains>],[<every>],[<interval>],[<at-end>]

7.2.85.2 Discussion

Each of the fields that this macro can be used to change are optional input. One or more of the fields may be changed with each macro call.

This macro updates the ART in DBE memory only. A "REWRITE SCRT" command is necessary to update the schema file.

7.2.85.3 Sample Output

An AREA-DDL will be executed to display the new values.

7.2.87 PRT

This macro enables you to print source elements, SDF data files or even print files at the terminal. This is of great value when used in conjunction with TIP hardcopy mode - enabling you to get source listings printed on TIP printers.

PRT[,<options>] <filename>.[<element>[/<version>]]

7.2.87.2 Options

 

None Only text from the file/element will be printed (contrast with the 'S' option).

 

N Do not display file/element information.

 

P Pause after every page.

 

S Text lines will be prefixed with sequence numbers (ala FURPUR '@PRT,S'). Contrast with no options.

7.2.87.3 Discussion

None.

| Chapter 7 | 'R$CHECKSUM' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */R$CHECKSUM

7.2.91 R$CHECKSUM

The R$CHECKSUM macro is used to perform UDS checksum calculation on the currently based database page, File Control Page or currently based allocation page.

7.2.91.1 Syntax

CHECKSUM[,<options>] <checksum-type>

7.2.91.2 Options

none Set "B" and "G" options.

 

B Display if checksum is bad.

 

C Update checksum IN CORE COPY ONLY if bad.

 

G Display if checksum is good

7.2.91.3 Discussion

<checksum-type> can be RPAGE , RFCP or RAP. If omitted, it will default to RPAGE.

7.2.91.4 Sample Output

*:>R$CHECKSUM **BAD CHECKSUM ON PAGE 6 - 000000000000 SHOULD BE 451457251551

*:>R$CHECKSUM,C

*:>R$CHECKSUM GOOD CHECKSUM ON PAGE 6

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'R$CHECKSUM-ONE' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */R$CHECKSUM-ONE

7.2.92 R$CHECKSUM-ONE

The R$CHECKSUM-ONE macro is used to verify checksums on all or some pages in the current area.

7.2.92.1 Syntax

R$CHECKSUM-ONE[,<options>] [<start-page>,<end-page>]

7.2.92.2 Options

none Set "B" and "G" options.

 

B Display if checksum is bad.

 

C Update checksum in core AND rewrite page to disk if bad.

 

G Display if checksum is good

 

M Multiple execution mode - exit and re-enter DBE processor every

500 pages processed to avoid max Log entries error.

7.2.92.3 Discussion

If the <start-page> is less than or equal to the first data/index page, the File Control Page and Allocation Pages will also be checksummed.

7.2.92.4 Sample Output

See the R$CHECKSUM macro.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'R$COUNT' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */R$COUNT

7.2.93 R$COUNT

The R$COUNT macro will display record counts for an RDMS area broken down by Btree.

7.2.93.1 Syntax

R$COUNT <btree-number>

7.2.93.2 Discussion

If btree-number is omitted, all active Btree lists will be reported on.

Note that pages are "walked" by determining the first data page for a Btree and then following the horizontal page links. This results in one I/O for each page scanned. For this reason the R$SCAN macro should be used whenever possible to reduce I/O overhead and processing time.

This macro will only work with RDMS DATA or DATA/INDEX areas.

7.2.93.3 Sample Output

 

*:R$COUNT

 

****************************************************************

* GROSS RECORD COUNTS FOR RDMS AREA: AUDIT-AD*FILES *

* PAGE SIZE: 1792 TOTAL PAGES: 34 *

* FILE CONTROL PAGES: 1 - 1 REPORT LIMITS: 2-34 *

* DATE: 06/06/91 TIMES: 15:48:31 - 15:48:35 *

****************************************************************

* BTREE OCCURRENCE RECORD SIZES *

* NUMBER COUNT MIN MAX *

* ======== =========== ============ *

* 1 361 12 - 16 *

* 2 361 9 - 13 *

* 3 361 8 - 10 *

* 4 635 18 - 19 *

* 5 635 7 - 9 *

* ----------- *

* TOTAL: 2353 *

****************************************************************

| Chapter 7 | 'R$DATA' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */R$DATA

7.2.94 R$DATA

This macro may be used to print the data area of an RDMS record on the current RDMS page.

7.2.94.1 Syntax

R$DATA [<record-location>]

7.2.94.2 Discussion

The record data will be dumped in both octal and ASCII formats.

The <record-location>] is the address of the start of a record on the current RDMS page. If specified, the data portion of the record at that location will be printed, and the current buffer pointer will be set to the start of that record. If the <record-location> is omitted, the current table pointer is assumed to be at the start of a record.

7.2.94.3 Sample Output

See the example for DATA in Figure 1-7.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

7.2.95 R$DUMPREC

This macro will produce a formatted ASCII/Octal listing of a record on the current RDMS page.

7.2.95.1 Syntax

R$DUMPREC [<record-location>]

7.2.95.2 Discussion

The record data will be dumped in both octal and ASCII formats.

The <record-location>] is the address of the start of a record on the current RDMS page. If specified, the record at that location will be printed, and the current buffer pointer will be set to the start of that record. If the <record-location> is omitted, the current table pointer is assumed to be at the start of a record.

7.2.95.3 Sample Output

See Figure 1-12.
