| Chapter 7 | 'R$FETCH' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */R$FETCH

7.2.96 R$FETCH

This macro will "FETCH" an RDMS record using specified keys in the current RDMS area.

7.2.96.1 Syntax

R$FETCH[<,options>] [key1,key2,.....,key10]

7.2.96.2 Options

B Keys are in binary and should not be converted to ASCII.

 

I The first key specified is a Btree Index number. After determining the Btree number, key2 will become key1, key3 will become key2, etc.

7.2.96.3 Discussion

The R$DUMPREC will be called after the record is found.

A maximum of 10 keys can be specified on the macro call. If no keys are supplied, the user will be prompted to enter them. A blank response will terminate the key entering.

7.2.96.4 Sample Output

The output will be a R$DUMPREC listing for the first record encountered with equal or higher keys.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'R$NEXTREC' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */R$NEXTREC

7.2.97 R$NEXTREC

This macro may be used to give a R$DUMPREC listing of the record which is physically next on the current page.

7.2.97.1 Syntax

R$NEXTREC

7.2.97.2 Discussion

Prior to calling the 'R$NEXTREC' macro, the current table pointer must be positioned to a record header word on an RDMS database page. This macro will move the RPAGE pointer to the record header word for the record which is physically next on the page and call the R$DUMPREC macro.

If the current RDMS record is the last on the current page, R$NEXTREC will dump the first record on the next logical RDMS data page (obtained from the horizontal link in the page header).

7.2.97.3 Sample Output

The output will be a R$DUMPREC listing for the next record on the page (if any).

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'R$PGDUMP' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */R$PGDUMP

7.2.98 R$PGDUMP

This macro will produce a formatted listing of an entire RDMS database page. The contents of the listing will resemble a combination of the DMS DMU 'PRINT' and 'DUMP' functions.

7.2.98.1 Syntax

R$PGDUMP[<,options>] [<page specification>]

7.2.98.2 Options

D Format Deleted records instead of octal only dump

 

U Dump unused space on the page

7.2.98.3 Discussion

The <page specification> is the same as for the 'RPAGE' command. If the <page specification> field is absent, the macro will dump the current page.

The actual data contents of records dumped will be dumped both in octal and ASCII formats.

7.2.98.4 Sample Output

See Figure 1-11.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */R$RECSLOT

7.2.99 R$RECSLOT

This macro allows the user to specify a record slot number on the current RDMS page to be used to locate a record. The record found will then be printed using the 'R$DUMPREC' macro.

7.2.99.1 Syntax

R$RECSLOT <expression>

7.2.99.2 Discussion

The value of <expression> must be greater than zero and nopt greater than the number of active record slots on the current RDMS page. Once the macro determines the record header word address on the page using the value of <expression> as the record slot number, the 'R$DUMPREC' macro will be used to print it.

7.2.99.3 Sample Output

An R$DUMPREC listing of the desired record will be produced.

| Chapter 7 | 'R$SCAN' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */R$SCAN

7.2.100 R$SCAN

The R$SCAN macro will produce record counts and page usage reports for the current RDMS area.

7.2.100.1 Syntax

R$SCAN[,<options>] [<start-page>],[<end-page>]

7.2.100.2 Options

None Use option R

 

D Produce Data Page Usage report

 

I Produce Index Page Usage report

 

L Options R , T , D , I

 

R Produce Record Counts

 

T Produce Total Page Usage report

 

V Validate checksum for all pages and RAPs, RFCP

7.2.100.3 Discussion

The R$SCAN uses the RSCAN function to perform multi-track double buffered I/O to obtain its statistics unless the <start-page> field is used which causes I/O on an individual page basis (with a significant increase in overhead).

If the <start-page> and/or <end-page> fields are specified, only pages within those ranges will be reported on.

NOTE: If more than one RDMS table is defined in the area being scanned, this macro will NOT break down the total record counts by table. Use the R$COUNT macro instead.

7.2.100.4 Sample Output

See Figure 1-13.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| MACROS | |

*// */R$SCAN-ALL

7.2.101 R$SCAN-ALL

The R$SCAN-ALL macro will call the macro 'R$SCAN' for each RDMS area associated with a RDMS Schema (group) name.

7.2.101.1 Syntax

R$SCAN-ALL <rdms-group-name>,[<file-mask>],[<qual-mask>]

7.2.101.2 Options

All options are passed to the R$SCAN macro.

7.2.101.3 Discussion

The R$SCAN macro will be called for each RDMS areas for the specified <rdms-qroup-name>, optionally masked by <file-mask> and <qualifier-mask>.

Use of this macro depends on the U$FDT-COPY being run each time FDTs are changed in the UDS FDT$ file.

7.2.101.4 Sample Output

An R$SCAN listings will be produced for each RDMS area matching the selection criteria.

| Chapter 7 | 'RANDENTIAL' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */RANDENTIAL

7.2.103 RANDENTIAL

This macro allows the user to locate a calc record within the database controlled by the current schema provided its location mode is via the RANDENTIAL calc procedure.

7.2.103.1 Syntax

RANDENTIAL[,<option>] [<area>],[<record>],[<key value1>],...[<key value n>]

7.2.103.2 Options

None The <key value> parameters will be used as the key(s) for the RANDENTIAL process. If none is supplied, the user will be prompted for one (demand) or an error message will result (batch). The mode of the record will be used to dictate whether the key should be converted to ASCII or not.

 

B Prompt for lower and upper bounds if required.

7.2.103.3 Discussion

<Area> is a specification of the area in which the record would be stored. This specification may be any that is legal on the 'AREA' command. If absent, the current area will be used.

<Record> is a specification of the record type you are looking for. This specification may be any that is legal on the 'RECORD' command. If absent, the current record will be used.

The <key value> parameters should not be expressed within quotes unless the quotes are to be actual characters within the key.

After determining the page and chain number, this macro will fetch the appropriate page and begin searching the correct calc chain until it either finds the record of the correct type having the given <key value> or reaches the end of the calc chain (the point where it cycles back to the chain header word); this second condition would cause a "***RECORD NOT FOUND***" message to be printed.

As synonyms are found during the calc chain scan, the user will be told of the actual key values and record names of those synonym records.

7.2.103.4 Sample Output

See the DMSCALC example in Figure 1-7.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'RE' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */RE

7.2.107 RE (RESTORE-ENV)

 

The 'RE' macro restores the DBE environment to the point at which the last 'SE' ('SAVE-ENV') macro was called.

7.2.107.1 Syntax

RE

7.2.107.2 Discussion

When the 'SE' macro is called, DBE saves the current environment as a series of statements in a temporary file DBE$SAVE$ENV. When the 'RE' macro is called, the DBE$SAVE$ENV file is @ADD'ed, effectively restoring the user to the point at which the environment was saved. This macro restores only table-related entities, i.e., items such as processor options, DEBUG mode settings, etc. will not be restored.

7.2.107.3 Sample Output

@DBE DBE 6R1 1100/90 L39 (DBE) (870311 1506:00) 870330 1137:32

*:> SCHEMA,T 100 DBE-SCHEMA *:> SUBSCH DBE-SUBQLP *:> AREA 101 *:> PAGE 1 *:> 012 PAGE[012] 023410000030

PAGE[012]:> SE SCHEMA,T 100 DBE-SCHEMA SUBSCH,T 100 DBE-SUBQLP AREA,N 101 PAGE 1 10 PAGE

PAGE[012]:> BYE END DBE

@DBE DBE 6R1 1100/90 L39 (DBE) (870311 1506:00) 870330 1138:32

*:> RE PAGE[012] 023410000030

PAGE[012]:> PAGE PAGE: 1 AREA: 101 (DBE-AREA-1) FILE: TIP/DMS FILE 101 SUBSCHEMA: DBE-SUBQLP FILE: TIP/DMS FILE 100 SCHEMA: DBE-SCHEMA FILE: TIP/DMS FILE 100

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'REC-COUNT' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */REC-COUNT

7.2.108 REC-COUNT

This macro will count all records in the current area and return an edited listing of those counts.

7.2.108.1 Syntax

REC-COUNT[,options] [<start>][,<stop>]

 

H Histogram record counts

 

I Do not display errors encountered

7.2.108.2 Discussion

<Start> and <stop> are the starting and stopping page numbers indicating what pages should be scanned. The default for <start> is one and the default for <stop> is the highest allocated page in the area.

The 'TOTAL PAGES' shown in the report is the count of the total number of pages in the area, while the 'REPORT LIMITS' is an indication of what pages were selected for counting (based on the macro parameter(s)).

The 'TIMES' shown in the report are the time the counting process started and the time the counting process stopped. This may be used to determine how quickly I/O is being done to that area.

The remainder of the fields should be self-explanatory.

7.2.108.3 Value Returned

If this macro is called as a function, the result will be an array containing the occurrence counts for the area, one word per record type in the schema. The receiving field should be at least as large as the number of records described in the schema (see the format of the Schema Reference Table in the DBE Programmer's Reference Manual).

7.2.108.4 Sample Output

See Figure 1-8.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'REC-COUNT-ALL' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */REC-COUNT-ALL

7.2.109 REC-COUNT-ALL

This macro does a 'REC-COUNT' for all or some areas in the currently loaded schema. No <start> or <stop> parameters are accepted; the counts will be done for all pages.

7.2.109.1 Syntax

REC-COUNT-ALL[,<options>] [<mask>]

7.2.109.2 Options

None Standard 'REC-COUNT' listings will be generated for each eligible area.

 

H The 'H' option will be passed to the 'REC-COUNT' macro each time it is called. This will cause record code vs occurrence count histograms to be generated for each area.

 

T At the conclusion of the 'REC-COUNT' listings, a grand-total of all records found will be printed. If the 'H' option was also supplied histograms will be generated as well.

7.2.109.3 Discussion

Presence of the optional <mask> parameter will cause the count report to be performed only on those areas whose names match the <mask> provided. If the <mask> is absent, all data areas will be counted.

7.2.109.4 Sample Output

A 'REC-COUNT' listing will be generated for all selected areas.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'REC-DDL' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */REC-DDL

7.2.110 REC-DDL

This macro can be used to display the symbolic (schema-style) record description for a record. It can also be used to display the value of each field in a specific record occurrence using a schema-style format.

7.2.110.1 Syntax

1. REC-DDL[,<options>] [<record-specification>]

2. REC-DDL,V[E] [<record-address>]

7.2.110.2 Options

None Display the symbolic description of the record specified, including each item in the record.

A Display information for all records in the schema.

B Display data concerning the position of each item in the record. The starting word, starting bit, and item length will be shown on a line following the item name, beginning with an asterisk in column 7.

E Display "value" information (see 'V' option) for elementary items only.

S Display the record header only. No item information is displayed.

V Using the actual record occurrence specified by <record-address> on the current page, display the value of each item in the record. Each value will be given on a line by itself, beginning with an asterisk in column 7.

W Do not print record "within" clauses.

7.2.110.3 Discussion

The item names displayed by the 'REC-DDL' macro are not kept in any form in the absolute schema. These names are kept, however, in any subschema that includes the selected items. If a subschema that includes the item requested is current at the time 'REC-DDL' is called, the names displayed will be correct. If no subschema is current, or the items needed were not included in the current subschema, item names will be displayed as 'ITEM-x', where "x" is the item number in the schema. The 'V' option uses the <record-address> specified, or the current page offset if none was specified, to derive the record's values. Item values are shown in the format defined in the schema, e.g., numeric items (whether "DISPLAY" or "COMP") are shown with the proper number of digits, and non-numeric item values are shown within quotes. Variable-length records (OCCURS DEPENDING ON) are expanded in DBE core according to the number of occurrences in the object record. Each item in an OCCURS item will display "VALUE(x)=", where "x" is the occurrence number of that item.

7.2.110.4 Sample Output

>REC-DDL DBE-RECORD

 

RECORD NAME IS DBE-RECORD-1

RECORD CODE IS 101

LOCATION MODE IS CALC DMSCALC

IN DBE-AREA-NAME

USING DBE-SOC-SEC

DUPLICATES ARE NOT ALLOWED

WITHIN DBE-AREA-1

RECORD MODE IS ASCII COBOL

03 D1-SOC-SEC PIC 9(9) USAGE COMP

03 D1-BIRTHDATE USAGE DISP

05 D1-BIRTH-YY PIC 99 USAGE DISP

05 D1-BIRTH-MM PIC 99 USAGE DISP

05 D1-BIRTH-DD PIC 99 USAGE DISP

03 FILLER PIC XX USAGE DISP

>REC-DDL,V 012

 

RECORD NAME IS DBE-RECORD-2

RECORD CODE IS 102

LOCATION MODE IS INDEX SEQUENTIAL

USING ASCENDING RANGE KEY

D2-NUMBER1

D2-NUMBER2

INDEX AREA IS DBE-AREA-2X

LINKS ARE NEXT

DUPLICATES ARE NOT ALLOWED

WITHIN DBE-AREA-2

RECORD MODE IS ASCII COBOL

03 D2-NUMBER1 PIC 9(4) USAGE DISP

* VALUE 1111

03 D2-NUMBER2 PIC 99 USAGE DISP

* VALUE 22

03 D2-NAME PIC X(10) USAGE DISP

* VALUE 'TEST NAME '

* VALUE 2

03 D2-DATA USAGE DISP

OCCURS 1 TO 6 TIMES DEPENDING ON D2-OCCURS

* VALUE(1): '094R'

* VALUE(2): '014S'

| Chapter 7 | 'RECSLOT' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */RECSLOT

7.2.112 RECSLOT

This macro allows the user to specify a record slot number on the current page to be used to locate a record. The record found will then be printed using the 'DUMPREC' macro.

7.2.112.1 Syntax

RECSLOT <expression>

7.2.112.2 Discussion

The value of <expression> must be greater than zero and not greater than the number of record slots on the current page. Once the macro determines the record header word address on the page, using the value of <expression> as the record slot number, the 'DUMPREC' macro will be used to print it.

7.2.112.3 Sample Output

A DUMPREC listing of the desired record will be produced.

| Chapter 7 | 'SAVE' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */SAVE

7.2.118 SAVE

This macro writes a copy of a macro to a specified file.

7.2.118.1 Syntax

SAVE <macro-name>,<file-name>

7.2.118.2 Options

None The generated element will have the first command in column 10. The remaining lines will be indented as necessary.

 

C The generated element will have the first command in column 2. No indentation will be performed. This option creates a macro which uses the least amount of disk and DBE memory space, but is the least readable.

 

N The generated element will have the first command in column 10. No indentation will be performed.

7.2.118.3 Discussion

<Macro-name> must be the name of a macro currently loaded into DBE core. If the macro has not yet been loaded, a simple way to force a load is to first do a

 

LIST <macro-name> 1,1

command.

The <file-name> specified must terminate with a period.

The macro requested will be saved in the file specified as an element named <macro-name>. No method is available to save the macro using an alternate element-name.

7.2.118.4 Sample Output

> SAVE REC-DDL,X.

SAVED TO: DBE*X(1).REC-DDL

SAVE COMPLETE. LINES: 896

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */SCAN-ALL

7.2.119 SCAN-ALL

The SCAN-ALL macro does a 'SCAN-ONE' for all or some areas in the currently loaded schema.

7.2.119.1 Syntax

SCAN-ALL[,<opts>] <area-mask>

7.2.119.2 Options

S Process areas sorted by area name instead opf the default area code.

7.2.119.3 Discussion

All options supported by SCAN-ONE are acceptable to SCAN-ALL and will be passed to SCAN-ONE with the exception of the "S" option.

7.2.119.4 Sample Output

A 'SCAN-ONE' listing will be generated for all selected areas.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'SCAN-ONE' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */SCAN-ONE

7.2.120 SCAN-ONE

The SCAN-ONE macro will produce the following reports for the current area :

 

Size-report

Rec-count

Page usage / overflowed pages

Page-usage

Overflow

7.2.120.1 Syntax

SCAN-ONE[,<options>] <min-chains>,<max-chains>

7.2.120.2 Options

C Overflow report

 

F Produce second record count file in SGS format

 

H Histogram Record Counts

 

I Ignore error messages

 

L Options U,H,Q,T,P,O,C

 

M Display timing messages / SUP usage

 

O Overflow page usage histogram

 

P Prime page usage histogram

 

Q Page usage / overflow statistics

 

R Do NOT produce record counts (record counts are always produced unless this option is present)

 

T Total page usage histogram

 

U Size-report information

 

None Record Counts & Total page usage histogram

7.2.120.3 Discussion

The SCAN-ONE macro utilizes the SCAN function which performs double-buffered multi-track I/O. As such, it is a very efficient wasy to gather database statistics on an area basis.

Because of this, the following macros actually call the SCAN-ONE / SCAN-ALL macros to produce reports:

 

REC-COUNT / REC-COUNT-ALL

PAGE-USAGE / PAGE-USAGE-ALL

OVERFLOW / OVERFLOW-ALL

If errors are detected, macro "SCAN$ERRMSG" will be attempted. This macro is NOT supplied, but can be written and installed by the user to take an appropriate action such as console error messages or other notification. If the macro is not found, no error will result.

7.2.120.4 Sample Output

See Figure 1-8.

7.2.120.5 Files Produced

The SCAN-ONE macro creates file DBE$*<orunid>-COUNT with @USE name of OUTFIL containing the following:

For each record type found in the area a record is written in the format:

 

Cobol Definition

 

PIC X(20) Literal '25RGROSS '

PIC 9(6) Current date as YYMMDD

PIC X(12) Area Name

PIC Z(4) Area Code

PIC Z(4) Record Code

PIC X(30) Record Name

PIC Z(4) Record Size (Data+Pointers+Header+Slot)

PIC Z(10) Record Count

PIC Z(4) Record Size (Data only)

PIC Z(2) Location Mode

One record for Prime and Overflow Utilization in the format:

 

Cobol Definition

 

PIC X(8) Literal '96LLOAD '

PIC X(12) Schema Name

PIC 9(6) Current date as YYMMDD

PIC Z(4) Area Code

PIC 9(6) Current date as YYMMDD

PIC Z(6) Number of Prime Pages

PIC Z(6) Number of Allocated Overflow Pages

PIC 9(5) COMP

OCCURS 24 TIMES Prime/Overflow Utilization as described in the

discussion on the 'SCAN' command

 

One record for Overflow Chaining in the format:

 

Cobol Definition

 

PIC X(8) Literal '98LLOAD '

PIC X(12) Schema Name

PIC 9(6) Current date as YYMMDD

PIC Z(4) Area Code

PIC 9(6) Current date as YYMMDD

PIC Z(6) Number of Prime Pages

PIC Z(6) Number of Allocated Overflow Pages

PIC 9(5) COMP

OCCURS 10 TIMES Number of Prime pages with 1,2,3,4,5,6,7,8,9,>9

overflow attached.

PIC 99V99 COMP Average I/O

PIC 99V99 COMP Adjusted Average I/O

| Chapter 7 | 'SE' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */SE

7.2.125 SE (SAVE-ENV)

 

The 'SE' macro saves the current DBE environment so that it may be restored later during the demand session via the 'RE' macro.

7.2.125.1 Syntax

SE

7.2.125.2 Discussion

When the 'SE' macro is called, DBE saves the current environment as a series of statements in a temporary file DBE$SAVE$ENV. When the 'RE' macro is called, the DBE$SAVE$ENV file is @ADD'ed, effectively restoring the user to the point at which the environment was saved. This macro restores only table-related entities, i.e., items such as processor options, DEBUG mode settings, etc. will not be restored.

7.2.125.3 Sample Output

@DBE DBE 6R1 1100/90 L39 (DBE) (870311 1506:00) 870330 1137:32

*:> SCHEMA,T 100 DBE-SCHEMA *:> SUBSCH DBE-SUBQLP *:> AREA 101 *:> PAGE 1 *:> 012 PAGE[012] 023410000030

PAGE[012]:> SE SCHEMA,T 100 DBE-SCHEMA SUBSCH,T 100 DBE-SUBQLP AREA,N 101 PAGE 1 10 PAGE

PAGE[012]:> BYE END DBE

@DBE DBE 6R1 1100/90 L39 (DBE) (870311 1506:00) 870330 1138:32

*:> RE PAGE[012] 023410000030

PAGE[012]:> PAGE PAGE: 1 AREA: 101 (DBE-AREA-1) FILE: TIP/DMS FILE 101 SUBSCHEMA: DBE-SUBQLP FILE: TIP/DMS FILE 100 SCHEMA: DBE-SCHEMA FILE: TIP/DMS FILE 100

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'SEND' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */SEND

7.2.126 SEND

This macro has the effect of the following three DBE commands:

 

OFF Hardcopy

OFF NoTerminalPrint

ON Demand

Assuming that hardcopy mode was previously in effect and that it was the standard hardcopy mode (producing a print file to be '@SYM'd to a high-speed printer) this will '@SYM' the hardcopy file to the printer and restore printing to the terminal (see the SITE macro). If hardcopy mode was previously in effect but was to a TIP printer, any output remaining in the print buffer will be sent to the printer, output to the terminal will be resumed and hardcopy mode will be terminated.

7.2.126.1 Syntax

SEND

7.2.126.2 Discussion

The first line of output (if any) is the result of the 'OFF H' command. Note that any time previous to executing the 'SEND' macro the user may use the 'HARDCOPY' command to alter the copy count or device-id (assuming standard hardcopy mode) or the TIP printer id (assuming TIP hardcopy mode).

7.2.126.3 Sample Output

>SEND

OUTPUT TO TERMINAL IS NOW RESUMED

***** Note *****

Line 1 of the above output would not appear if

TIP hardcopy mode were in effect.

If no subschema is current, or the items needed were not included in the current subschema, item names will be displayed as 'ITEM-x', where "x" is the item number in the schema. I-----------------------------I

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'SHT' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */SHT

7.2.130 SHT

This macro prints a formatted dump of the Subschema Header Table for the current subschema. The subschema must be type QLP for this table to exist.

7.2.130.1 Syntax

SHT

7.2.130.2 Discussion

The majority of the SHT fields are self-explanatory. All of the subschema tables utilized by QLP are pointed to by the SHT. Their size is given in words (H1) and their address is given in sectors relative to the start of the subschema (H2). This address is not to be confused with an absolute address in DBE core. However, once this address is converted to words, it can be used as an index for the subschema table. Example:

 

SUBSCH[3612] would reference the PDT header word where sector address 129 * 28 words/sector = 3612.

For a description of these tables, refer to the 'SUBSCH' command. remain 27

7.2.130.3 Sample Output

*:>SHT

| Chapter 7 | 'SITE' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */SITE

7.2.131 SITE

This macro has the effect of the following DBE commands:

 

[ HARDCOPY,T <pid-number> ]

ON Hardcopy

ON NoTerminalPrint

OFF Demand

This will cause all future DBE output to go to the hardcopy device and not to the terminal.

7.2.131.1 Syntax

SITE [<expression>]

7.2.131.2 Discussion

<Expression>, if present, will cause the 'HARDCOPY' command shown above to be executed using the value of <expression> as the pid specification. Error messages will still appear at the terminal.

If a hardcopy file was already in use, it will be closed and sent to printer (resulting in the 'OFF H' message) prior to opening a new one.

7.2.131.3 Sample Output

*:>SITE 517

OUTPUT NOW REDIRECTED TO PID 517

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'SIZE-REPORT' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */SIZE-REPORT

7.2.132 SIZE-REPORT

This macro enables the user to get area sizing information printed for any or all areas in the currently-loaded schema.

7.2.132.1 Syntax

SIZE-REPORT[,<options>] [<limit>][,<mask>]

7.2.132.2 Options

None All areas (or those selected by the <mask> parameter) will be listed and no TIP information will be printed.

 

F Only report on areas which fall below the minimum overflow percentage

threshold.

 

Q Do not count/report free page chain information. This will

significantly speed up reporting for areas with large free page chains.

 

S Report on areas sorted by Area Name instead of the default Area Tip Code order.

 

T All areas printed will also have their "record" sizes and "record" numbers (as defined for TIP areas) printed. These numbers can then be compared against the page size and page count values. This information will only be printed for TIP areas.

7.2.132.3 Discussion

<Limit>, if specified, is an arithmetic expression evaluating within the range 0-100; if absent, a value of 10 will be assumed. This is used to specify the limit for overflow growth percentage (the right-most column of the report) below which an area will be flagged as having a dangerously low overflow growth potential remaining.

<Mask>, if specified, is a standard name mask to be applied against the area names to control which areas are to be printed. If absent, "*" (meaning all areas) will be assumed.

7.2.132.4 Sample Output

See Figure 1-9.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'SS-AREAS' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */SS-AREAS

7.2.136 SS-AREAS

This macro is used to produce a listing of all (or some) areas in the currently loaded subschema. The following information will be printed for each area:

 

1. Area-name

2. Area-code

3. Mode (SARP/DARP)

4. Access (EXEC/TIP)

5. Type (Data/Index/Pointer)

In addition, the area will be checked for each of the following items, with an appropriate message printed if an item applies:

 

1. Facility status (EXEC areas)

2. TIP assignment (TIP areas)

3. Initialized/uninitialized

4. Page header inconsistency

7.2.136.1 Syntax

SS-AREAS [<mask>]

7.2.136.2 Discussion

Note that in the case of EXEC areas, the current default qualifier (see the 'QUAL' command) will be used to determine the complete area file name. If this is incorrect, unexpected 'FAC REJECT' messages may result.

DBE will only check the first page of an area (page zero if DARP) for being consistent and initialized.

See the 'AREAS' macro in this chapter for a complete discussion of the masking feature.

7.2.136.3 Sample Output

*:>SS-AREAS

ALL AREAS FOR SUBSCHEMA: DBE-SUBQLP

SCHEMA: DBE-SCHEMA

1: 101: DBE-AREA-1 SARP TIP DATA 2: 102: DBE-AREA-2 DARP EXEC INDEX

*// */SYM

7.2.142 SYM

This macro allows users to @SYM print files to a TIP printer.

7.2.142.1 Syntax

SYM <filename>.,[<# lines per page>],<TIP printer pid>

7.2.142.2 Discussion

Carriage-control will be performed (except for 0-spacing, which will be treated as 1-spacing).

<# Lines per page> is the maximum number of lines that may be printed per page before an automatic form-feed is generated. This number will default to 55 if omitted.

7.2.142.3 Sample Output

This macro produces only the print file listing at the TIP printer.

| Chapter 7 | 'TOC' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */TOC

7.2.147 TOC

This macro may be used to generate a table-of-contents listing for an EXEC or TIP/DMS program file.

7.2.147.1 Syntax

1. TOC[,<options>] <file.>[<elt>[/<vers>][,<subtype>][,<sgs-name>][,<fname>]

2. TOC[,<options>] <expression>[,<elt>[/<vers>][,<subtype>] [,<sgs-name>][,<fname>]

7.2.147.2 Options

None A table-of-contents listing of the EXEC file supplied as the first parameter will be generated. No deleted elements will be printed and all types (ABS, SYM, REL, OMN) will be eligible.

 

A Restrict the list of elements printed to type "ABS". This may be combined with the 'SRO' options.

 

D Deleted elements are to be considered eligible for listing.

 

F Create a file containing SGS cards.

 

O Restrict the type of elements printed to 'OMN'. This may be combined with the 'ARS' options.

 

R Restrict the type of elements printed to 'REL'. This may be combined with the 'AOS' options.

 

S Restrict the type of elements printed to 'SYM'. This may be combined with the 'AOR' options.

 

T The TIP/DMS file whose number is given by <expression> is to be listed.

7.2.147.3 Discussion

Note that the absence of the 'T' option implies format 1 while its presence implies format 2.

The <elt> and <vers> parameters are masks that may be used to indicate the types of names of elements and versions that are to be listed. Their use is summarized as follows:

 

<Elt> <Vers> <Means>

========== =========== =======

Absent Absent No name/version restrictions to the elements printed

Present Absent Any elements whose names match the <elt> mask, regardless of <vers> will be eligible. An exception is the case of "<elt>/" (slash, but no version). This will require a blank version.

Absent Present Any elements whose versions match the <vers> mask, regardless of element name will be eligible.

Present Present Only those elements whose names match the <elt> mask and whose versions match the <vers> mask will be eligible.

The optional <subtype> field allows standard source-element subtypes (ELT, MSM, COB, FTN, etc.) to be used to select elements for the toc listing.

The optional <sgs-name> and <fname> fields determine the SGS label name and file name, respectively. An internal name of "TOCSGS" will be attached. The SGS label will default to "ELT$" if the F option is specified and no <sgs-name> is supplied.

7.2.147.4 Sample Output

*:>TOC,F DA0*ABS-FMGDEV.

 

DA0*ABS-FMGDEV(1). 10/10/91 18:41:25 PAGE: 1

 

SEQ ELEMENT VERSION TYPE DATE TIME SIZE LOCN

1 8 FMGDEV-SCH ABS 06/30/87 09:01:33 96 1792

2 FMGLOD-SCH ABS 11/10/88 12:28:06 96 1888

7.2.148 TOPICS

This macro lists the names of topics which are available as part of the DBE "HELP" feature. More information on a topic may be gotten by entering 'EXPLAIN <topic-name>'.

7.2.148.1 Syntax

TOPICS

7.2.148.2 Discussion

None.

7.2.148.3 Sample Output

>TOPICS

THE FOLLOWING TOPICS MAY BE "EXPLAIN"ED:

"HELP" EXPLAIN THE DBE HELP FACILITY

"TOPICS" THE LIST OF "EXPLAIN" TOPICS

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'TREG' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */TREG

7.2.149 TREG

This macro is used to produce a formatted listing of the TIP-registration information table for a TIP area.

7.2.149.1 Syntax

TREG[,<options>] [<area specification>]

7.2.149.2 Options

P Perform an 'AREA,P' command to reference only the area's ART; do not attempt to physically reference the area.

7.2.149.3 Discussion

This macro will produce a formatted listing of the TIP-registration information (as defined by the FCSS LF function) for the indicated area. This macro should only be used with TIP areas. If no <area-specification> is supplied, the current area will be assumed.

7.2.149.4 Sample Output

| Chapter 7 | 'U$ADT' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */U$ADT

7.2.151 U$ADT

The U$ADT macro is used to print a formatted listing of the Application Description Table (ADT) from core or the Mass-storage copy.

7.2.151.1 Syntax

U$ADT[,<options>] <application-number>

7.2.151.2 Options

none Display ADT entry, Transparent ADT entry, and all alias entries.

 

A Display only alias entries.

 

F Display the ADT mass-storage file rather than the core copy.

7.2.151.3 Discussion

If the application-number is omitted, the entire ADT will be displayed.

7.2.151.4 Sample Output

*:>U$ADT 4

| Chapter 7 | 'U$ALIAS' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */U$ALIAS

7.2.152 U$ALIAS

The U$ALIAS macro is used to display all aliases from the ADT file (see the U$ADT macro) sorted by application and alias name.

7.2.152.1 Syntax

U$ALIAS[,<options>] <application number>

7.2.152.2 Options

F Read from the ADT mass-storage file rather than the core copy.

 

S Create a file of SGS cards containing alias names and application number.

7.2.152.3 Discussion

If application-number is omitted, all applications will be processed.

7.2.152.4 Sample Output

*:>U$ALIAS

7.2.153 U$ALL

7.2.153.1 Syntax

U$ALL[,<options>] 'macro-to-be-called,options-for-macro'

7.2.153.2 Options

E Perform a page eject before executing the called macro.

7.2.153.3 Discussion

None.

| Chapter 7 | 'U$APP' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */U$APP

7.2.156 U$APP

The U$APP macro is used to base a UDS application group based on an alias name or application group number.

7.2.156.1 Syntax

U$APP[,<options>] <alias-name>

7.2.156.2 Options

F Display the ADT mass-storage file rather than the core copy.

 

S Use the currently based Schema as the alias name.

7.2.156.3 Discussion

If alias-name is omitted, the currently based application (if any) will be displayed.

The information from this command is written to a temporary file via the U$APP-LOAD macro. This allows the user to exit DBE, re-enter and have the application information available.

In addition, a temporary file called 'APPSGS' is created containing the application data in SGS card format. See Figure 1-17 for details.

7.2.156.4 Sample Output

*:>U$APP FMGDEV-SCH

DBE IS CONNECTED TO UDS APPLICATION "APPFOR" (#4) BDI: 0402503

WITH ALIAS FMGDEV-SCH

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

7.2.159 U$BSTE

The U$BSTE macro is used to print a formatted listing of the UDS Bank Summary Table Entries (BSTE).

7.2.159.2 Options

none Same as "A" option.

D Show UDS Global D-Bank BSTE.

 

P Show Page Bank BSTEs.

 

S Show Schema Bank BSTEs.

 

T Show Thead Bank BSTEs.

7.2.159.3 Discussion

The 'U$APP' macro must have been previously executed to base a UDS application.

7.2.160 U$DAL

The U$DAL macro is used to display a formatted listing of Files currently down for an application.

7.2.160.1 Syntax

U$DAL

7.2.160.2 Discussion

The 'U$APP' macro must have been previously executed to base a UDS application.

The U$DAL macro does not read the UDS FDT$ file directly to get the File Names. The U$FDT-COPY macro MUST have been previously run to read the UDS FDT$ file and update the DBE FDT$ file.

7.2.160.3 Sample Output

*:>U$DAL

 

DOWNED AREAS FOR FMGTST-SCH

 

FILE-AREA 1512 U

FILE-HIST 1514 U

PEND-AREA 1513 U

 

THERE ARE 3 DOWN ENTRIES FOR SCHEMA FMGTST-SCH

 

DOWNED AREAS FOR HSTPRD-SCH

 

HSTAREA1 2661 F

HSTAREA2 2662 F

HSTAREA3 2663 F

HSTAREA4 2664 F

HSTAREA6 2665 F

 

THERE ARE 5 DOWN ENTRIES FOR SCHEMA HSTPRD-SCH

 

 

TOTALS FOR APP : APPFOR

FILES DOWN : 5

FILES DOWN FOR UPDATE : 2

FILES WITH PAGES DOWN : 0

7.2.160.4 Files Produced

For each area name matched, a 56 word ASCII record is written to temp file DAL.

See the U$FDT-COPY macro for the FDT entry format.

| Chapter 7 | 'U$FDT-COPY' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */U$FDT-COPY

7.2.165 U$FDT-COPY

The U$FDT-COPY macro is used to read the UDS FDT$ file and create a DBE Sector formatted file for use by other macros.

7.2.165.1 Syntax

U$FDT-COPY

7.2.165.2 Discussion

This macro MUST be run after every addition/deleteion/change to the FDT$ file to ensure that macros using the DBE FDT file function correctly.

The 'U$APP' macro must have been previously executed to base a UDS application.

7.2.165.3 Sample Output

*:>U$FDT-COPY

 

EXTRACTED 1529 FDT ENTRIES IN 37 GROUPS FOR UDSSRC

7.2.165.4 Files Produced

The Files defined in macro U$FDT-FILES are updated as follows:

For each valid FDT in the FDT$ file, a 56 word ASCII record is written to the DBEFDT file (starting at record FDTE$START+1) in the format:

 

WORD #

 

1 - 8 Group Name (Schema Name)

9 - 16 Table Name (Area Name)

17 - 24 Version Name (ABS,PRODUCTION,etc.)

25 - 33 Date-Time Stamp

YY/MM/DD HH:MM:SS ############ (12 digit octal YYMMDDHHMMSS)

 

34 TIP Code

35 - 39 spaces

or

34 - 36 Qualifier

37 - 39 File Name

 

40 - 41 Page Size (8 digit octal)

Word 40:Q1 is Darp/sarp flag (1=Darp) and should be set to

an ASCII 0 to obtain the page size.

42 - 43 Max Pages (8 digit octal)

44 Recovery/Checksum

Q1: 1 = Recovered

Q2: 1 = Audited

Q3: 1 = Before Looks

Q4: Checksum Setting

0 = No

1 = Yes (Read and Write)

2 = Write

45

Q1: Lock Strategy

1 = Page

2 = Record

Q2: Domain

1 = User

2 = User-UDS

3 = UDS

H2: Data Format

1 = DMS Data

2 = DMS Index

3 = DMS Pointer

8 = RSM Data

9 = RSM Data and Index

10 = RSM Index

14 = DSDF (SDF Direct)

15 = MSAM (SDF MSAM)

25 = Change File (DMS Change file for TEST mode)

26 = Directory

27 = Absolute (DMS Schema / Subschema file)

28 = UDS Internal File

29 = PSEUDO Absolute

46 - 53 Unused

54 Down Status Flags (binary)

B0 = File is down

B1 = File is down for update

B2 = Pages are down (may be combined with B0 or B1)

55 Start of Down Pages (binary)

56 End of Down Pages

** Note: Words 54-56 are filled in by the U$DAL macro.

** Note: If more than one page range is down, the U$DAL macro will create

one record for each range with words 1-53 duplicated.

For each Group Name, an entry is written (starting at record FDTG$START) in the following format:

 

WORD #

 

1 - 8 Group Name

9 Start of FDT Entries for this Group (REC # in FDTE file)

10 Start of Schema FDT Entry (REC # in FDTE file)

11 Number of Schema entries for this group

12 Number of ABS entries for this group

13 Number of PRODUCTION entries for this group

14 Number of misc entries for this group

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

7.2.166 U$FDT-COPY-ALL

The U$FDT-COPY-ALL macxro is used to call the U$FDT-COPY macro for each UDS application.

7.2.166.1 Syntax

U$FDT-COPY-ALL

7.2.166.2 Discussion

None.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'U$FDT-DUMP' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */U$FDT-DUMP

7.2.167 U$FDT-DUMP

The U$FDT-DUMP macro is used to dump the DBE FDT Tip file.

7.2.167.1 Syntax

U$FDT-DUMP[<,options>] [<table-name>]

7.2.167.2 Options

none Display Group Name, Table Name, Version Name, FDT Date/Time Stamp, File Name.

 

G Display only the Group names and count of FDTs for each.

 

S Display only FDT entries with a version of SCHEMA

7.2.167.3 Discussion

See the discussion under macro "U$FDT-COPY" macro for DBE FDT File creation.

The 'U$APP' macro must have been previously executed to base a UDS application.

If table-name is omitted, all tables in the FDT$ file will be dumped.

7.2.167.4 Sample Output

*:>U$FDT-DUMP TCS

 

TCS AUTH$FILE PROD 90/03/29 14:24:39 120335163047 UDS$$SRC AUTH$FILE

TCS FDT$FILE UDS 82/10/12 09:09:09 021214111111 2350

TCS RDT$FILE UDS 90/03/29 14:24:25 120335163031 UDS$$SRC RDT$FILE

TCS VIEWDEP$FILE PROD 90/03/29 14:24:55 120335173067 UDS$$SRC VIEWDWP$FILE

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'U$FDT-EXT' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */U$FDT-EXT

7.2.168 U$FDT-EXT

The U$FDT-EXT macro is used to create an SDF file containing entries from the DBEFDT copy file for a specied schema.

7.2.168.1 Syntax

U$FDT-EXT[,<options>] <schema-name>

7.2.168.2 Options

none Display FDT entries as they are copied

 

B Do not display entries as they are copied.

7.2.168.3 Discussion

The 'U$FDT-COPY' macro must have been previously executed to update the DBEFDT file.

7.2.168.4 Sample Output

See the U$FDT-DUMP macro for the format of the displayed entries.

7.2.168.5 Files Produced

Each FDT entry matching the specified schema-name will be written to temp file FDTEXT.

See the U$FDT-COPY macro for the format of the FDT entries.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

7.2.169 U$FPTE

The U$FPTE macro is used to print a formatted listing of the File Paging Table Entries (FPTEs) for an in-core FDT.

7.2.169.1 Syntax

U$FPTE[,<options>]

7.2.169.2 Options

none Display only the in-use FPTEs.

 

A Display ALL FPTEs.

 

F Start at the first FPTE block on the chain.

7.2.169.3 Discussion

The 'U$APP' macro must have been previously executed to base a UDS application.

The U$FDT macro must have been previously executed to base an FPTE chain.

| Chapter 7 | 'U$INST-CHECK' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */U$INST-CHECK

7.2.173 U$INST-CHECK

The U$INST-CHECK macro is used to compare schema absolutes to determine if a Process Delete / Process Install is required during schema fallback execution.

7.2.173.1 Syntax

U$INST-CHECK[,<options>]

7.2.173.2 Options

C Compare files DBE*OLD-SCHEMA and DBE*NEW-SCHEMA which must have been created by previous executions of this macro.

 

N Create output file DBE*NEW-SCHEMA.

 

O Create output file DBE*OLD-SCHEMA.

7.2.173.3 Discussion

The following words in each areas ART are written to the file :

 

ART[0]

ART[1]

ART[3]

ART[4]

ART[5]

ART[011]

ART[014]

ART[024]

If all the above fields match between schemas, S6 of the run condition word is set to 0.

If an discrepancies exist, S6 of the run condition word is set to 1.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'U$INSTALL' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */U$INSTALL

7.2.174 U$INSTALL

The U$INSTALL is used to create input to the @DD processor to perform a Process Install of a Schema and all its subschemas.

7.2.174.1 Syntax

U$INSTALL[,<options>]

7.2.174.2 Options

F Read the ADT mass-storage file rather than the core copy.

 

L List the DD syntax as its written.

7.2.174.3 Discussion

Output is written to temporary file 'ADDFILE.' with an @USE name of "ADDFIL'.

7.2.174.4 Sample Output

*:>SCH,T 2340 FMGDEV-SCH

*:>U$INSTALL,L

DBE IS CONNECTED TO UDS APPLICATION "APPFOR" (#4) BDI: 0402503

WITH ALIAS FMGDEV-SCH

PROCESS SCHEMA FMGDEV-SCH INSTALL.

PROCESS SUBSCHEMA DMU-FMGDEV

FOR SCHEMA FMGDEV-SCH INSTALL.

PROCESS SUBSCHEMA FMGDEV-QLP

FOR SCHEMA FMGDEV-SCH INSTALL.

PROCESS SUBSCHEMA FMGDEV-SUB

FOR SCHEMA FMGDEV-SCH INSTALL.

EXIT.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

A Display active and inactive entries.

 

B Only display Block PBSEs.

 

D Display histogram of duplicated PBSEs.

 

P Only display Page PBSEs.

 

T Only display total counts.

7.2.179.3 Discussion

The 'U$THREAD' macro must have been previously executed to select a thread.

*// */U$PROCESS-I

7.2.180 U$PROCESS-I

This macro is used to build "PROCESS STORAGE AREA...INSTALL" syntax for the current schema, associated subschemas and all areas in the schema.

7.2.180.1 Syntax

U$PROCESS[,options]

7.2.180.2 Options

L Display all output lines as they are written to the file.

7.2.180.3 Discussion

The SDF file created will be called "PI." with an @USE name of "PIFILE.".

This macro is most useful after importing schema/subschema/area FDT information to ensure that the schema & subschema FDTs are built before the area FDTs.

7.2.180.4 Sample Output

*:>U$PROCESS-I,L

DBE IS CONNECTED TO UDS APPLICATION "APPSVN" (#7) BDI: 0405533

PROCESS STORAGE-AREA FILMGT-QLP2 VERSION ALL FOR SCHEMA FILMGT-SCH INSTALL. PROCESS STORAGE-AREA FILMGT-SUB VERSION ALL FOR SCHEMA FILMGT-SCH INSTALL. PROCESS STORAGE-AREA LOGICAL-AREA VERSION ALL FOR SCHEMA FILMGT-SCH INSTALL. PROCESS STORAGE-AREA ATT-AREA-2 VERSION ALL FOR SCHEMA FILMGT-SCH INSTALL. EXIT.

| Chapter 7 | 'U$RFL-DUMP' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */U$RFL-DUMP

7.2.182 U$RFL-DUMP

The U$RFL-DUMP macro is used to dump UDS retention files.

7.2.182.1 Syntax

U$RFL-DUMP[,<options>] <rfl-number>,<number-of-recs>,<last-rfl-number>

7.2.182.2 Options

A Dump all retention files from <rfl-number> through <last-rfl-number>.

L Produce long dump of records.

7.2.182.3 Discussion

The 'U$APP' macro must have been previously executed to base a UDS application.

If <rfl-number> is omitted, the first retention file will be dumped.

If <number-of-recs> is omitted, all records in the retention file will be dumped.

7.2.182.4 Sample Output

*:>U$APP 4 *:>U$RFL-DUMP 5

 

RETENTION FILE DUMP FOR APPLICATION APPFOR FILE # 5

PRODUCED ON 10/10/91 AT 15:55:48

 

QUICK LOOK AT SECTOR: 0

 

RECOVERED AFTER LOOK DMS-D AREA:694#FCP-PENDING PAGE:174

BY: *003MT SOS: 91/10/08 10:08:28 (PAGE HEADER: *003LJ 91/10/08 10:07:28)

 

QUICK LOOK AT SECTOR: 68

 

RECOVERED AFTER LOOK DMS-D AREA:703#FCP-TRACKING PAGE:212

BY: *003MT SOS: 91/10/08 10:08:28 (PAGE HEADER: *003LJ 91/10/08 10:07:28)

*** END OF RETENTION FILE ***

2 LOOKS DUMPED FOR RETENTION FILE # 5

7.2.186 U$THREAD

The U$THREAD macro is used to select a thread for use by other system macros to use.

7.2.186.1 Syntax

U$THREAD <thread-number>

7.2.186.2 Discussion

The 'U$APP' macro must have been previously executed to base a UDS application.

If thread-number is omitted, the current thread number will be displayed.

This macro updates the APP$THRDNUM and APP$TSTEADDR system variables.

7.2.186.3 Sample Output

*:>U$APP 3

*:>U$THREAD 4

 

>THREAD # 4 SELECTED FOR APPLICATION UDSSRC

7.2.189.3 Discussion

If the thread-number is omitted, all TSTEs will be displayed. remain 41

| Chapter 7 | 'U$USE-COUNT' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */U$USE-COUNT

7.2.190 U$USE-COUNT

The U$USE-COUNT macro is used to determine if a Schema is currently active in the UDS environment.

7.2.190.1 Syntax

U$USE-COUNT[,<options>] <minutes-to-wait>

7.2.190.2 Options

C Display messages on system console if "M" option is also set.

 

M Display a message for each minute waited.

7.2.190.3 Discussion

The minutes to wait defaults to 30 if not supplied.

If the minutes to wait has been reached, B1 of the run condition word is set to 1.

7.2.190.4 Sample Output

*:>U$USE-COUNT FMGDEV-SCH

DBE IS CONNECTED TO UDS APPLICATION "APPFOR" (#4) BDI: 0402503

WITH ALIAS FMGDEV-SCH

<U$USE-COUNT> SCHEMA FMGDEV-SCH NOT ACTIVE

| Chapter 7 | 'UP-AREAS' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */UP-AREAS

7.2.192 UP-AREAS

This macro will create an SDF file containing a DMU or IRU processor call to up selected areas.

7.2.192.1 Syntax

UP-AREAS[,<options>] [<mask>][,<alias-name>]

7.2.192.2 Options

A Append output to previously created up file.

L List output as it is written to SDF file.

S Up schema file.

X Use "Q" option on IRU call / "X" option on DMU call.

7.2.192.3 Discussion

If <mask> is supplied, only areas matching the <mask> specification will be upped. If <mask> is omitted, all areas in the schema will be upped.

<Alias-name> can be specified to force a specific UDS application group to be used for the IRU/DMU. This is required when upping areas for the SCHEMATA schema.

The SDF file created will be "UP$." with an @USE name of "UFILE".

7.2.192.4 Sample Output

*:>FILMGT-SCH

 

*:>UP-AREAS,LX

@UDS$$SVN*IRU.IRU,EIQUX . . FILE 595#LOGICAL-AREA FILE 596#FILE-AREA FILE 597#IO-AREA FILE 598#FILE-HIST FILE 599#LOGICAL-HIST FILE 2339#ATT-AREA-1 FILE 2348#ATT-AREA-2 ;

ACT APPL APPSVN ; END ; @EOF

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Chapter 7 | 'UPDATE-HIST' Macro |

| MACROS | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

*// */UPDATE-HIST

7.2.193 UPDATE-HIST

The UDDATE-HIST macro is used to produce a histogram of last update dates for all pages in an area.

7.2.193.1 Syntax

UPDATE-HIST[,<options>] <area-mask>

7.2.193.2 Options

A Produce report for all areas matching supplied <area-mask>.

7.2.193.3 Discussion

If the "A" option is not specified, the current area will be reported on.

If the "A" option is specified, a histogram will be produced at the end reporting on all reported areas combined.

7.2.193.4 Sample Output

*:>UPDATE-HIST
