| Appendix B | Level 6R1 |

| Summary Of Changes | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

9.9. Level 6R1 - 19 NOV 82

9.9.1 Processor Changes

9.9.1.1 Hexadecimal Formatting

The WRITE command now supports the FORMAT type "H", which is used to print in hexadecimal format.

9.9.1.2 New Macro DEBUG Mode

The commands "ON TRACE" and "MONITOR" have been rewritten and removed, respectively, to allow for a new DEBUG mode. When DEBUG mode is invoked via the "DEBUG ON" command, the following new commands become available:

BRKPT Stops a macro at any specified line number

GO Continues execution of a macro

MONITOR Displays variables that change value during macro execution

STEP Single-steps through a macro while displaying variable information

TRACE Displays each macro line as it is being executed

TRAP Stops a macro when any specified variable is referenced

9.9.1.3 Training-Mode Areas

When the DBE processor Y-option is on, training-mode areas will be used if they are available.

9.9.1.4 More Specific Subschema Table Errors

If a subschema table is requested and that table does not exist, new errors will describe more exactly why it is not available. The errors are as follows:

Error 145: No subschema has been invoked yet

Errors 11, 133, 139, 154:

No area/record/set/path has been invoked yet

Error 101: The area/record/set is defined in the schema, but not in the subschema

Error 14: The area/record/set/path is not defined for this subschema type (e.g., QLP table in a non-QLP subschema)

9.9.1.5 Security File Rollout

DBE no longer aborts and dumps if the security file has been rolled out. The message "DBE NOT AVAILABLE NOW - TRY LATER" is now displayed and the processor exits gracefully.

9.9.1.6 Processor T-option

The DBE processor T-option, which formerly caused tracing of every line executed, has now been restricted to non-macro input. Should macro tracing be desired, the DEBUG mode command "TRACE" is available.

9.9.1.7 "PRINT" and "OUTPUT" Variable Width

The "PRINT" and "OUTPUT" commands will now display data in either 80- or 132-column format, depending on whether the processor "D" option is set (to specify BATCH/DEMAND mode execution).

9.9.1.8 Single-Schema Version of DBE

The DBE processor may be generated to allow only a single schema to be accessible to certain users.

9.9.1.9 Pointer Areas Handled by "COUNT"

The "COUNT" command will now work with pointer-array pointer areas.

9.9.1.10 Two-dimensional Arrays

Arrays may now be created as two-dimensional. Several commands (e.g., SORT) have been enhanced to handle arrays of this type.

9.9.1.11 Byte Subsets Allowed on "LET" Command

Byte subsets are now permitted on the receiving side of the "LET" command.

9.9.1.12 Call-by-Address Parameters

Calling routines may now specify that array parameters are to be passed as addresses (directly addressible by the subroutine) instead of values. This allows a calling macro to tell a subroutine which array (or array subset) is to be updated, and the subroutine can perform the changes directly.

9.9.1.13 Arrays Created by Macros Deleted by RETURN

Previously, a macro could dimension an array, make that array the current table, and then terminate by either the "RETURN" or "STOP" commands. This would leave the array current, although space for that array had already been deallocated by macro termination. Now, if a macro-created array is still current upon return to interactive mode, the array will be deallocated, and no table will remain current.

9.9.1.14 Array Subsets Allowed on "WRITE" command

The "WRITE" command now supports output from an array subset.

9.9.1.15 "WRITE" Command ASCII Mode

The "A" option has been added to the "WRITE" command to allow output to be sent in ASCII mode. This allows special ASCII screen control sequences and upper/lower case messages to be sent.

9.9.1.16 DID Specification on "HARDCOPY" Command

The "HARDCOPY" command may now specify a printer DID for TIP output to be sent to.

9.9.1.17 "LIST,L" No Longer Destroys Macros

In the past, the "LIST,L" command made no distinction between macros keyed from a terminal and those brought in from a macro file. In an effort to retrieve correction line images, the "LIST,L" command forced the in-core version of the macro requested to be purged, and the longer version was loaded from the macro file. This worked fine for disk-loaded macros, but destroyed macros that had been manually keyed in. The "LIST,L" command now distinguishes between the two types and no longer purges macros keyed from the terminal.

9.9.1.18 Subscripted Variables Allowed on "GET"

The "GET" command now allows subscripted variables to be specified as the destination for file input.

9.9.1.19 Processor No Longer Loops During Exit

Previously, if an error occurred while trying to dynamically close all open files during DBE processor termination, the processor would loop. This problem has been resolved.

9.9.2 System Macro Changes

9.9.2.1 DMSCALC

Now handles binary keys properly. Now handles chaining of records with manual pointers properly.

9.9.2.2 DPATCH

Now allows the new value to be specified on the macro call.

9.9.2.3 LIBRARY

Calling the macro with no parameters now reports the current macro library name.

9.9.2.4 OVERFLOW-ALL

Unavailable areas are now displayed as such, and the reason the area is unavailable is explained.

9.9.2.5 PAGE-USAGE-ALL

Unavailable areas are now displayed as such, and the reason the area is unavailable is explained. Options specified on the PAGE-USAGE-ALL call are now used in the processing of each individual area.

9.9.2.6 PATCH

Allows patching of arrays, as well as tables. Patching variables is still restricted, but now reports the attempt as an error.

9.9.3 New System Macros

9.9.3.1 High-Level Macros

9.9.3.1.1 HELP

Describes the "HELP" feature available.

9.9.3.1.2 SAVE

Writes a copy of a macro to a specified file. No options will produce a macro with the first command starting in column 10, and indentation where needed. The "N" option will produce a macro with the first command starting in column 10, but no indentation will be performed. The "C" option will produce a macro with the first command starting in column 2, and no indentation will be performed. This version takes up the least amount of disk and DBE memory space, but is the least readable.

9.9.3.1.3 TOPICS

Explains the TOPICS feature of DBE help mode.

9.9.3.2 Subroutine Macros

9.9.3.2.1 ACCESS-CONTROL

Called by the "ART" macro, this macro displays the access-control portion of an Area Reference Table in standard table format.

9.9.3.2.2 ART$PRE8R2

Called by the "ART" macro, this macro displays in standard table format that part of an Area Reference Table that was different prior to DMS level 8R2.

9.9.3.2.3 DISC$$T

Part of the "DISCEDIT" package for editing disc files.

9.9.3.2.4 PAUSE

Displays the message "<XMIT> TO CONTINUE" and will either continue or execute a command that has been entered.

9.9.3.2.5 R$FILE

Builds a SORT/MERGE control packet for use by the R$OPN statement.

9.9.3.2.6 YYMMDD

Returns a date in YYMMDD format.

9.9.3.3 Changed Macros

Level 6 of DBE incorporates an easier-to-read standard table format. This format presents a table in three parts: each word of a table is displayed with the 12-digit octal value on the left side, the partial-word segments of that word displayed in the appropriate format in the center, and the description of each partial-word segment on the right. Following is a list of the system macros that have been converted to utilize this new standard table format:

ART

FDT

PH

P0

RDT

RRT

SCRT

SDT

SRT

TREG

9.9.4 New Commands

9.9.4.1 Debug Mode

9.9.4.1.1 BRKPT (B)

Allows a macro to enter DEBUG mode when a specified statement number is encountered.

9.9.4.1.2 DEBUG

Enables and disables "DEBUG" mode.

9.9.4.1.3 MONITOR (M)

Displays the new value of selected variables when these are changed during macro execution.

9.9.4.1.4 STEP (S)

Allows controlled execution of a macro in DEBUG mode.

9.9.4.1.5 TRACE

Displays instructions that are executed by a macro when in DEBUG mode.

9.9.4.1.6 TRAP (T)

Allows a macro to enter DEBUG mode when a specified variable is about to be changed.

9.9.4.1.7 GO

Resumes execution of a stopped macro in DEBUG mode.

9.9.4.2 Table Invoking Commands

9.9.4.3 Sort Control

9.9.4.3.1 R$OPN

Using the packet created by the R$FILE macro, establishes the interface to SORT/MERGE subroutines.

9.9.4.3.2 R$REL

Releases to SORT/MERGE a record that is to be sorted.

9.9.4.3.3 R$SORT

Performs the actual sort once all records have been released.

9.9.4.3.4 R$RET

Returns from SORT/MERGE a record that has been sorted.

9.9.4.3.5 R$QEND

Prematurely terminates the SORT/MERGE interface.

9.9.4.4 Miscellaneous Commands

9.9.4.4.1 XQT

Allows the interpretive execution of a command residing in an array subset.

9.9.5 New System Variables

9.9.5.1 AREAP

Set to one if the pages of the current area cannot be accessed, either due to an "AREA,P" command or an error occurring while reading during an "AREA" command.

9.9.5.2 ART^

The word number within the SCRT where the current ART is found.

9.9.5.3 CONDWD

The run condition word at DBE startup.

9.9.5.4 DID

The Device Identifier specified on the previous "HARDCOPY" command.

9.9.5.5 LAST

The offset of the final word in the current table.

9.9.5.6 POPTS

The DBE processor options that are currently invoked (See the "ON"/"OFF" commands) in master-bit notation.

9.9.5.7 QUAL

The current qualifier in effect, as specified by the "QUAL" command.

9.9.5.8 RRT^

The word number within the SCRT where the current RRT is found.

9.9.5.9 SCHADR

The sector number of the current absolute schema in the schema file.

9.9.5.10 SCHELT

The element name of the current absolute schema as specified on the last "SCHEMA" command.

9.9.5.11 SCHFILE

The file name or number of the current absolute schema as specified on the last "SCHEMA" command.

9.9.5.12 SCHNAME

The name of the current schema as specified on the last "SCHEMA" command.

9.9.5.13 SCHVER

The version name of the current absolute schema as specified on the last "SCHEMA" command.

9.9.5.14 SRT^

The word number within the SCRT where the current SRT is found.

9.9.5.15 TRAIN

Set to 1 if the current area is in training mode (See the DBE processor "Y" option).

9.9.5.16 UCL

Users clearance level.

9.9.6 New Functions

9.9.6.1 COREADR

Returns the in-core absolute address of a subset or character string.

9.9.6.2 FITEM

Returns an array containing the information passed on a "ER FITEM$" request. This information describes the name, size, and other attributes of a selected file.

9.9.7 New Tables

9.9.7.1 CMDBUF

Buffer in which a macro can store a command to be executed upon return to conversational mode.

9.9.7.2 WBUF

The "Write" buffer. EDIT$ buffer used by the DBE "write" command.

9.9.8 New Error Codes

9.9.8.1 Error 33

<33> MONITOR MACRO LIMIT EXCEEDED

9.9.8.2 Error 34

<34> MONITOR VARIABLE LIMIT EXCEEDED

9.9.8.3 Error 46

<46> DEBUG MODE NOT ACTIVE

9.9.8.4 Error 57

<57> NO MACRO IS PRESENTLY SUSPENDED

9.9.8.5 Error 61

<61> * IS AN ILLEGAL STEP COUNT

9.9.8.6 Error 62

<62> ARRAY "*" TOO LARGE - NOT DIMENSIONED

9.9.8.7 Error 63

<63> ARRAY DIMENSION/USAGE INCOMPATABILITY

9.9.8.8 Error 64

<64> TWO-DIMENSION ARRAY USED AS ONE-DIMENSION ARRAY

9.9.8.9 Error 65

<65> PRINT IMAGE IS TOO LONG

9.9.8.10 Error 67

<67> INVALID OR INCOMPLETE SORT/MERGE PACKET

9.9.8.11 Error 74

<74> EOF ENCOUNTERED WHILE READING FROM SORT FILE

9.9.8.12 Error 84

<84> UNRECOVERABLE SORT/MERGE ERROR

9.9.8.13 Error 101

<101> THIS LEG OF THE TIP FILE IS TPFREE'D

9.9.8.14 Error 102

<102> THIS TIP FILE IS NOT DUPLEXED

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Appendix B | Level 7R1 |

| Summary Of Changes | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

9.10. Level 7R1 - 08 NOV 90

9.10.1 Processor Changes

9.10.1.1 CSINTNAME$ Macro Library File Compatibility

If the DBE system macros are kept in the same file as the DBE processor, then CSINTNAME$ may be specified as the name of the macro library file. This will be true even if the processor is COMUS LOCAL-INSTALL'ed (in which case the EXEC @USE's CSINTNALT$ rather than CSINTNAME$ for the processor load file.)

9.10.1.2 UDS Support

To support DMS under the UDS environment, DBE now has the capability to read any Common Bank. This allows macros to be written to go against the various UDS Banks and produce Table Dumps, etc.

9.10.1.3 Processor Abort

Should the DBE processor detect a processor error, it will now abort via the "A$BORT" proc, which does not corrupt any registers, and the DBE-999 dump routines will print the message "DBE INTERNAL ERROR". The address of the A$BORT requestor will now be found in the contin-gency packet.

9.10.1.4 More Specific Subschema Table Errors

If a subschema table is requested and that table does not exist, new errors will describe more exactly why it is not available. The errors are as follows:

Errors 11, 133, 139, 154:

No area/record/set/path has been invoked yet

Error 144: The area/record/set is defined in the schema, but not in the subschema

9.10.1.5 RECOVERR Flag

Internally, the DBE processor may now override the "FATAL" flag for any of the "ERROR" proc errors by setting the RECOVERR flag. This allows more versatility in DBE command handling.

9.10.1.6 ERRPR W-option and C-option

If the W-option is specified on the "ERRPR" command, error information will be written to the write-buffer following any information that already exists there. This allows macros to custom-format error messages. If the C-option is specified, the error information will be written to the console write-buffer for delivery to a system console.

9.10.1.7 DBE-004 Rewrite

The handler for the commands "PRINT", "OUTPUT", "LAST", "FMT", "+/-", and "expression" has been rewritten. This provides more consistent handling of table/array printing. Requests for printing words outside the boundaries of a table/array are now handled more like the standard text editor. An error in displaying the word number in the "EOF:x" message has been corrected.

9.10.1.8 "FEATURE" Command

The "FEATURE" command makes the tables FRT (Feature Reference Table) and GED (Global Encode/Decode Table) directly accessible.

9.10.1.9 Table "#0"

The "AREA", "FEATURE", "PAGE", "PATH", "RECORD", and "SET" commands now allow "#0" to be selected. This has the effect of making no entity of that type current, and clearing all related information. This can be used, for example, if a macro is written to loop through all areas as follows:

MACRO LOOPER

DO FOREVER

AREA +1

<print area information>

END DO

@EOF This macro will process the first area in the schema only if no area has been invoked yet. The user may now enter "AREA #0" prior to execution of this macro to obtain the proper results.

9.10.1.10 Table Resetting

If a table that was current at the start of a command is no longer available at the conclusion of that command, that table will not be accessible to the user. For example, if a PAGE had been current and the user did an "AREA" command, no table will be current at the con- clusion of the "AREA" command. In addition, if a table is current at the beginning of a command and a new version of that table is requested, the current table address will be set to zero at the con- clusion of the command. For example, if the user was positioned at word 100 of a PAGE and then did a "PAGE" command, the table "PAGE" would remain current and the current table address will be set to zero.

9.10.1.11 "AREA" Command N-option

The "N" option has been added to the "AREA" command to inhibit printing of the area name. Previously, the sequence

ON BRIEF

AREA xxx

OFF BRIEF was used to inhibit printing the area name, and any error routines responsible for handling "AREA" command errors needed to reset BRIEF mode.

9.10.1.12 "AREA" Command Always Returns ART

If an "AREA" command selects a valid area, but the command does not complete for some reason (e.g., an empty DARP area causes a failure trying to read page zero), the command is turned into a partial area ("AREA,P") request, and the ART becomes available.

9.10.1.13 Automatic "PAGE" Currency

A "PAGE" command will now make the table "PAGE" current automatically if done interactively and no other table was current. This allows the sequence

AREA ...

PAGE 1

P! to print the entire page, which previously would have caused an error 83 ("NO TABLE IS CURRENT"), since the "PAGE" command caused no table to become current.

9.10.1.14 PAGE Command "R" & "X" Options

The "R" option has been added to the "PAGE" command to allow the current page to be re-read from mass-storage.

The "X" option will allow page selection beyond the normally defined limits of an area. This is helpful, for instance, when the DAE page (page zero) of a DARP area records a high-numbered data page lower than actually exists.

9.10.1.15 SCHEMA Command "L" Option

The "L" option on the "SCHEMA" command will allow a Schema to be loaded from an EXEC-8 file and then automatically reload the file from the correct Tip file if it is a Tip Schema.

9.10.1.16 SCHEMA/SUBSCHEMA Absolute Consistency Check

Elements loaded via the "SCHEMA" and "SUBSCHEMA" commands are now more thoroughly checked to make sure they are the type requested. Previously, the "SCHEMA" command could be requested to load a subschema absolute that would cause the processor to abort.

9.10.1.17 Subschema Handler Rewrite

The subschema table handler has been rewritten, introducing several new tables, and making the table handling more consistent. Many schema and subschema table commands are now directly linked, e.g., if a subschema has been invoked, a schema "AREA" command will make the table "SART" current. New commands such as "SSAREA" allow the selection of schema entities by subschema code. The subschema is now "parsed" to read in only the tables which are current for an area, record or set (similar to SCHEMA command).

9.10.1.18 Alternate File Subschemas

The "SUBSCH" command has been enhanced to allow a filename to be specified. Previously, subschemas were supported only if they resided in the same file as the associated schema. The new command is upward-compatible from DBE level 5, as it will default to the schema filename if none was specified on the "SUBSCH" command. The syntax of the "SUBSCH" command is now identical to that of the "SCHEMA" command, allowing TIP file specification, element versions, and schema name overrides.

9.10.1.19 "PATH" Command Changes

The "D" option has been added to the "PATH" command to completely replace the "NEXTDUP" specification. The "PATH #0" command now completely replaces the "REBASE" specification. These changes make the syntax of the "PATH" command compatible with other table- handling commands.

9.10.1.20 New Output Modes on "TREAD" Command

Data to be printed via the "TREAD" command may now be specified as coming from an array subset, or coming from the standard write-buffer. This allows output lines to be built piece-by-piece before delivery to the terminal user.

9.10.1.21 "WRITE" Command "RETURN" and "STOP" Options

Options "R" and "S" have been added to the "WRITE" command to create the WRITE/RETURN and WRITE/STOP commands. This allows a macro to check for an error, print a message and exit in a single line. Previously, any write-and-exit response to an "IF" command required the "THEN" option on the "IF" command, and an "END IF", in addition to the "WRITE" and exit commands.

9.10.1.22 Site Library File

A second system library file now exists which is intended to contain macros of a site-specific nature (e.g. macros which directly specify DMU/IRU processor files).

9.10.1.23 Second user macro library

Assigning a file with an @USE name of "DBE$PF2" will allow that file to be searched after the standard user library file (DBE$PF) for macros (ALT-LIB macro).

9.10.1.24 I/O to Tip Direct Files.

Files opened as "OPEN TIP" will use FCSS I/O to read/write TIP files using the GET / PUT commands. Files opened in this mode DO NOT require update capablilities to PUT to the file.

9.10.1.25 Allow Hardcopy 0

A copy count of "0" is allowed on the hardcopy command, allowing an alternate print file to be created without being symmed.

9.10.1.26 Corrected Sort/Merge interface

The sort/merge parameter block is now copied to lower memory, correcting a bug which caused scratch files to be ignored.

9.10.1.27 Common Bank Sort routines

A gen parameter exists to select relocatable or common banked sort routines.

9.10.1.28 Re-Dimensioned Arrays

If an array is re-dimensioned to the same size or smaller, the same starting address will be used instead of treating it as a new array and allocating more core.

9.10.1.29 Rewrite Logging

All "REWRITES" are written to the system log with a before and after look of the word being changed.

9.10.1.30 Usage Logging

All "USAGE" commands are written to the system log.

9.10.2 System Macro Changes

9.10.2.1 AREA-DDL

The "A" option now produces an "AREA-DDL" report for each area in a schema. The macro now accepts the same parameters as the "AREA" command.

9.10.2.2 ATTPAGE

Now functions properly. Note that this macro is of no use when using DMS levels beyond 8R2.

9.10.2.3 DATA

When a page offset is entered as the parameter, the user will now be positioned at the start of the record at macro termination (as the "DUMPREC" macro already did).

9.10.2.4 DBK

The parameter entered now has a leading zero placed before it by the macro, forcing DBK's entered to be in octal.

9.10.2.5 DIAGRAM

Correctly handles schemas containing no sets. The vertical bar now defaults to the upper case letter "I", so that printers without the bar can print the diagram. The vertical bar (or any character of the user's choice) may be specified as the parameter on the "DIAGRAM" call.

9.10.2.6 DIRECT

The parameter entered now has a leading zero placed before it by the macro, forcing DBK's entered to be in octal.

9.10.2.7 DMSCALC

Now handles binary keys properly. Now handles chaining of records with manual pointers properly.

9.10.2.8 DPATCH

Now allows the new value to be specified on the macro call.

9.10.2.9 LINK

Corrects errors that occurred when the link number requested was out of range. Pointers in a pointer-array are now correctly handled as DBK's instead of DBP's. Corrects "DECODE" error that occurred if a record specified by a pointer could be found in the database. New "D" option to call "DATA" macro each time a record is located.

9.10.2.10 PATCH

Allows patching of arrays, as well as tables. Patching variables is still restricted, but now reports the attempt as an error.

9.10.2.11 PRT

Added the "P" option which produces paged output (PAUSE macro is called after every 21 output lines).

9.10.2.12 RDT

Correctly displays area within clauses for MIS areas.

9.10.2.13 SETS

Now properly handles schemas which include no sets.

9.10.2.14 TOC

Now displays an error if the file is not in program-file format.

9.10.3 New System Macros

9.10.3.1 High-Level Macros

9.10.3.1.1 ALCALC

Replacement for DMSCALC for use with records with multiple calc keys.

9.10.3.1.2 ALT-LIB

Assigns an alternate user library for use as a third macro file.

9.10.3.1.3 BANKDUMP

Allows dumping of Common Banks.

9.10.3.1.4 BANKSIZE

Displays the starting & ending address for a common bank.

9.10.3.1.5 CALC-REPORT

Provides a report of the number of calc records on each calc chain in an area. A detailed display comparable to that of the "OVERFLOW" macro can be requested, showing exactly which pages have calc chains of a specified length.

9.10.3.1.6 CHECKSUM

Calculates UDS checksum for the current database page.

9.10.3.1.7 CHECKSUM-ONE

Calls "CHECKSUM" macro for each Page in the current Area.

9.10.3.1.8 CHECKSUM-ALL

Calls "CHECKSUM-ONE" macro for each Area in the Schema.

9.10.3.1.9 EDMAC

Calls the @ED processor to edit an element in the current user macro library file.

9.10.3.1.10 FACERR

Decodes a facility Reject/Warning.

9.10.3.1.11 FETCH

Allows "Fetching" of records in the current Area.

9.10.3.1.12 FIELDATA

Displays a chart of fieldata characters with octal conversion.

9.10.3.1.13 FILES

Lists file control information on all open user files.

9.10.3.1.14 FITEM

Displays FITEM$ information for a specified filename in the standard table format.

9.10.3.1.15 FRT

Displays Feature Reference Table information in the standard table format.

9.10.3.1.16 HELP

Describes the "HELP" feature available.

9.10.3.1.17 IDT

Displays Item Description Table information in the standard table format.

9.10.3.1.18 IFETCH

"Fetches" an Index Sequential record (similar to DMSCALC macro).

9.10.3.1.19 ILINK

Links to the next Index Sequential record in an area.

9.10.3.1.20 ILI-TO-ONE

Generates a DMU patch file (via the DPATCH macro) to reset the ILLOGICAL INSERT POINT for a darp area to page 1.

9.10.3.1.21 LIB

Same as LIBRARY macro.

9.10.3.1.22 PATHSTEPS-ALL

Invokes the "PATHSTEPS" macro to display path information for all paths in a subschema.

9.10.3.1.23 PRINT-USE

Attaches an @USE name to an opened alternate print file.

9.10.3.1.24 RE (RESTORE-ENV)

Invokes the "RESTORE-ENV" macro to restore a DBE environment saved during an earlier DBE session.

9.10.3.1.25 REC-DDL

Displays the symbolic (schema-style) record description for a record. Item names cannot be displayed unless a subschema which includes the requested items is currently invoked. If the item name cannot be obtained from a subschema, the item names are printed as "ITEM-<x>", where <x> is the item number in the schema. The "A" option will display information for all records in the schema. The "H" option will display the record header only (no item information is printed. The "B" option will display data concerning the position of the data in the record, i.e., the starting word, starting bit, and item length. The "V" option will display actual item values for a record selected from the database. Variable length records are expanded and the correct item values are displayed. Items containing multiple occurrences display the value of each occurrence displayed as "VALUE(x)=", where "x" is the occurrence number. Values are displayed in the format specified in the schema on an item-by-item basis. The "E" option will display value information for elementary items only.

9.10.3.1.26 SCAN-ALL

Calls the SCAN-ONE macro for each area matching an optional mask.

9.10.3.1.27 SCAN-ONE

Produces reports for an area based on the following options: Record counts - always produced unless "R" optiion set. U - Size-report H - Histogram record counts Q - Page usage / Overflow statistics T - Total page usage histogram P - Prime page usage histogram O - Overflow page usage histogram C - Overflow chaining histogram / detail L - options U,H,Q,T,P,O,C

9.10.3.1.28 SCHEMA-TABLE

Calls the "ART" , "RRT" , "SRT" , "FRT" macros for each of the corresponing reference tables in a Schema.

9.10.3.1.29 SE (SAVE-ENV)

Save the current DBE environment for restoration in a later DBE session. Information about the current schema, subschema, area, and page are saved in a temporary file. Following a later "@DBE", the macro "RE" may be invoked to restore the environment to the point at which the "SE" was performed.

9.10.3.1.30 SET-DDL

Displays the symbolic (schema-style) set description for a set. The "A" option will display information for all sets in the schema.

9.10.3.1.31 SS-AREAS

Like "AREAS" for schema areas, prints area information for selected areas in a subschema.

9.10.3.1.32 SS-RECORDS

Like "RECORDS" for schema records, prints record information for selected records in a subschema.

9.10.3.1.33 SS-SETS

Like "SETS" for schema sets, prints set information for selected sets in a subschema.

9.10.3.1.34 SUBSCHEMAS

Lists all subschemas in the same file as the currently based Schema.

9.10.3.1.35 SYSTEM

Displays the formatted contents of reserved array "SYSTEM".

9.10.3.1.36 TIM

Displays the current date and time.

9.10.3.1.37 TITLE

Displays block letters.

9.10.3.1.38 TOPICS

Explains the TOPICS feature of DBE help mode.

9.10.3.1.39 U$ACT

The U$ACT macro is used to print a formatted listing of the UDS Application Characteristic Table (ACT) table.

9.10.3.1.40 U$ADT

The U$ADT macro is used to print a formatted listing of the Application Description Table (ADT) from core or the Mass-storage copy.

9.10.3.1.41 U$ALIAS

The U$ALIAS macro is used to display all aliases from the ADT file (see the U$ADT macro) sorted by application and alias name.

9.10.3.1.42 U$APP

The U$APP macro is used to base a UDS application group based on an alias name or application group number.

9.10.3.1.43 U$APP-STATUS

The U$APP-STATUS macro displays UDS application status information.

9.10.3.1.44 U$BST

The U$BST macro is used to print a formatted listing of the UDS Bank Summary Table (BST) table.

9.10.3.1.45 U$BSTE

The U$BSTE macro is used to print a formatted listing of the UDS Bank Summary Table Entries (BSTE).

9.10.3.1.46 U$DOWN-LIST

The U$DOWN-LIST macro is used to print a formatted display of the Downed file list for a UDS application.

9.10.3.1.47 U$FDT

The U$FDT macro is used to print a formatted listing of an in core File Description Table (FDT) entry.

9.10.3.1.48 U$FPTE

The U$FPTE macro is used to print a formatted listing of the File Paging Table Entries (FPTEs)for an in-core FDT.

9.10.3.1.49 U$GNL

The U$GNL macro is use to print a formatted listing of the UDS Group Name List Header (GNL) table.

9.10.3.1.50 U$GNLE

The U$GNLE macro is used to print a formatted listing of the UDS Group Name List Entries (GNLEs).

9.10.3.1.51 U$INDEX

The U$INDEX macro is used to print a formatted listing of the UDS Global D-Bank Index Table (DCS Index).

9.10.3.1.52 U$INST-CHECK

The U$INST-CHECK macro is used to compare schema absolutes to determine if a Process Delete / Process Install is required during schema fallback execution.

9.10.3.1.53 U$INSTALL

The U$INSTALL is used to create input to the @DD processor to perform a Process Install of a Schema and all its subschemas.

9.10.3.1.54 U$LCT

The U$LCT macro is used to print a formatted listing of the UDS Logical Data Manager (LDM) table.

9.10.3.1.55 U$TRC

The U$TRC macro is used to print a formatted listing of the UDS Trace (TRC) table.

9.10.3.1.56 U$TST

The U$TST macro is used to print a formatted listing of the UDS Thread Summary Table (TST) header.

9.10.4 U$TSTE

The U$TSTE macro is used to print a formatted listing of the UDS Thread Summary Table Entries (TSTEs).

9.10.5 U$USE-COUNT

The U$USE-COUNT macro is used to determine if a Schema is currently active in the UDS environment.

9.10.5.1 Subroutine Macros

9.10.5.1.1 AREASORT

Returns an array loaded with all area tip codes. The "S" option causes the array to be returned sorted in area name order.

9.10.5.1.2 DDL-SUB

Prints the name of a selected schema entity. The "A" option prints the area name of the current or selected area. The "D" option prints the name of a Data Base Procedure given its code. The "I" option prints the name of a subschema item given its subschema code. The "N" option prints the name of a data base data name (DBDN) given its subschema code. The "R" option prints the record name of the current or selected record. The "S" option prints the set name of the current or selected set.

9.10.5.1.3 DIVIDE

Divides 2 word input by 1 word input, giving 2 word result & 1 word remainder.

9.10.5.1.4 DSL

Shifts 2 word input by n bits, giving two word result.

9.10.5.1.5 EXPAND$REC

Converts an input array of compressed data into an array expanded based on the values of Occurs-Depending-On (ODO) items in a record.

9.10.5.1.6 EXTRACTITEM

Copies the value of an item in a record occurrence into the print buffer. The "C" option puts an asterisk in column 7 of the print buffer, simulating a COBOL comment. The "P" option forces the print buffer to be displayed when the value is complete.

9.10.5.1.7 FINDMAC

Returns the offset in the macro area (MA array) for a given macro.

9.10.5.1.8 GET-INDEX

Returns the record code of the Index Sequential record and the Index area code for the current data area.

9.10.5.1.9 MATCH-ARRAY

Compares two arrays, returning a result of 0 if unequal, 1 if equal.

9.10.5.1.10 OPTBIT2ALPHA

Converts a passed option bit word to ascii characters. The "L" option causes a "," to preceder the characters. The "W" option causes the character string to be written to the write buffer. The "C" option causes the character string to be written to the console buffer.

9.10.5.1.11 SCAN$CHAINS

Called by SCAN-ONE to provide overflow chaining info.

9.10.5.1.12 SCAN$FILE

Called by SCAN-ONE to write out File Management info.

9.10.5.1.13 SCAN$P-USAGE

Called by SCAN-ONE to provide Total/Prime/Overflow page usage info.

9.10.5.1.14 SCAN$PU-OVF

Called by SCAN-ONE to provide page usage / overflow statistics.

9.10.5.1.15 SCAN$RCOUNT

Called by SCAN-ONE to provide record count info.

9.10.5.1.16 SCAN$SIZE

Called by SCAN-ONE to provide size-report info.

9.10.5.1.17 SCAN$TOTREC

Called by SCAN-ALL to provide total record count info.

9.10.5.1.18 SEARCH-SME

Searches the Set Member Entries (SME) for a record and returns a pointer to one selected by either link number or set code. The "C" option selects an SME based on set code number. The "P" option selects an SME based on link (pointer) number. The "O" option searches through the SME's for sets the current record owns. The "A" option searches through the SME's for sets in which the current record is an automatic member. The "M" option searches through the SME's for sets in which the current record is a manual member.

9.10.6 New Commands

9.10.6.1 Non Table Commands

9.10.6.1.1 GOSUB

Transfers control to a specified label in a macro, returning control when an "END SUB" is encountered.

9.10.6.1.2 LOG

Allows System Log entries to be created.

9.10.6.1.3 MACSUB

Allows a macro to be executed as an extension of the current macro (or conversational mode) - all variables are shared.

9.10.6.1.4 SCAN

Obtain Record Counts, Page Usage and Overflow chaining information using efficient Double Buffered I/O.

9.10.6.2 Table Invoking Commands

9.10.6.2.1 FEATURE (FEA)

Allows access to the Feature Reference Table (FRT) and Global Encode / Decode Table (GED).

9.10.6.2.2 SSAREA

Allows the user to make an area current based on its subschema area code.

9.10.6.2.3 SSRECORD (SSREC)

Allows the user to make a record current based on its subschema record code.

9.10.6.2.4 SSSET

Allows the user to make a set current based on its subschema set code.

9.10.7 New System Variables

9.10.7.1 APP$BDI

Application UDS Global D-Bank BDI.

9.10.7.2 APP$NAME

Application Name.

9.10.7.3 APP$NBR

Application Number.

9.10.7.4 APP$QUAL

Application Qualifier.

9.10.7.5 APP$THREADS

Max Threads for a UDS Application.

9.10.7.6 APP$UDS

Set to 1 if the current Application is under UDS control.

9.10.7.7 AREAP

Set to one if the pages of the current area cannot be accessed, either due to an "AREA,P" command or an error occurring while reading during an "AREA" command.

9.10.7.8 DMR$QUAL

Default File Qualifier for the DMS Local Data Manager.

9.10.7.9 DMSDTS

First & Last Page Update Date/Time stamps returned after a SCAN function is executed.

9.10.7.10 FCBBLK

File Control Blocks.

9.10.7.11 FCODE

Feature Code.

9.10.7.12 FSEQ

Feature Sequence Number.

9.10.7.13 IRU$QUAL

Default File Qualifier for the IRU Local Data Manager.

9.10.7.14 LAST

The offset of the final word in the current table.

9.10.7.15 MA

The Macro Area.

9.10.7.16 MSTIME

The current time in milliseconds past midnight.

9.10.7.17 RDM$QUAL

Default File Qualifier for the RDMS Local Data Manager.

9.10.7.18 SFS$QUAL

Default File Qualifier for the SFS Local Data Manager.

9.10.7.19 SSACODE

The subschema code of the current area, as selected by either the "AREA" or "SSAREA" commands.

9.10.7.20 SSADR

Mass-storage address of the currently based Subschema.

9.10.7.21 SSASEQ

The sequence of the current area in the subschema, as selected by either the "AREA" or "SSAREA" commands.

9.10.7.22 SSELT

The element name of the current absolute subschema as specified on the last "SUBSCHEMA" command.

9.10.7.23 SSFILE

The file name or number of the current absolute subschema as specified on the last "SUBSCHEMA" command.

9.10.7.24 SSLEV

DMR Level of the currently based Subschema.

9.10.7.25 SSNAME

The name of the current subschema as specified on the last "SUBSCHEMA" command.

9.10.7.26 SSRCODE

The subschema code of the current record, as selected by either the "RECORD" or "SSRECORD" commands.

9.10.7.27 SSRSEQ

The sequence of the current record in the subschema, as selected by either the "RECORD" or "SSRECORD" commands.

9.10.7.28 SSSCODE

The subschema code of the current set, as selected by either the "SET" or "SSSET" commands.

9.10.7.29 SSSSEQ

The sequence of the current set in the subschema, as selected by either the "SET" or "SSSET" commands.

9.10.7.30 SSVER

The version name of the current absolute subschema as specified on the last "SUBSCHEMA" command.

9.10.7.31 TFPMAX

The value of "TFPMAX" as supplied by a DBE gen parameter or dymnamically retrieved from the operating system.

9.10.8 New Functions

9.10.8.1 BANKREAD

Reads a common bank into an array.

9.10.8.2 BANKSIZE

Returns the start/ending addresses of a common bank.

9.10.8.3 CHECKSUM

Performs UDS Checksum calculation on the current Database Page.

9.10.8.4 EXIST

Checks if an Array/Table exists and is loaded.

9.10.8.5 LF

Performs an FCSS "LF" on a given tip file.

9.10.8.6 MQF$

Performs an ER MQF$ to return application status information.

9.10.9 New Tables

9.10.9.1 DBPDT

Database Procedure Description Table.

9.10.9.2 DCSIDX

UDS Global D-Bank Index.

Item Description Table.

9.10.9.11 INT

Item Name Table. Describes the data-names that exist in each subschema record.

9.10.9.12 NHT

Name Hash Table (QLP Subschema).

9.10.9.13 RFT

Record Feature Table.

9.10.9.14 SART

Subschema Area Reference Table. Comparable to the Schema ART, it describes each area in a subschema.

9.10.9.15 SRDT

Subschema Record Description Table. Comparable to the Schema RDT, it fully describes each record in a subschema.

9.10.9.16 SRRT

Subschema Record Reference Table. Comparable to the Schema RRT, it briefly describes each record in a subschema.

9.10.9.17 SSCD

Subschema Description Table. Identifies all areas, records, and sets included in a subschema.

9.10.9.18 SSDT

Subschema Set Description Table. Comparable to the Schema SDT, it fully describes each set in a subschema.

9.10.9.19 SSRT

Subschema Set Reference Table. Comparable to the Schema SRT, it briefly describes each set in a subschema.

9.10.9.20 UDSVAR

Contains individual UDS variables.

9.10.9.21 USRBUF

General purpose user definable buffer (useful for word 0 based addressing).

9.10.10 New Error Codes

9.11. Level 8R1 - 12 APR 91

9.11.1 Processor Changes

9.11.1.1 RDMS Support

RDMS database areas are supported in a manner similar to DMS database areas. Where possible, macros have been created for RDMS to mirror DMS functionality.

9.11.1.2 RANDENTIAL Calc Routine Support

RANDENTIAL calc placement is supported in the same manner as DMSCALC.

9.11.1.3 CALCASE User Calc Routine Support

The CALCASE user written calc placement routine as implemented at NYSDSS is supported. CALCASE code generation is controlled by a sysgen SGS.

9.11.1.4 ABORT Command

ABORT command will cause DBE to do an "ER EABT$" to abort a batch run.

9.11.1.5 EXEC Area File Frees

The current Exec Area File is now @FREE'd when a new area is assigned to prevent PCT overlow aborts.

9.11.1.6 DMSCALC Fieldata keys

DMSCALC function modified to not translate keys to ascii when fieldata keys passed as a literal for fieldata records.

Snoopy turned off around save & restore of register set to prevent abort.

9.11.1.7 NON-DMS TIP I/O corrected

Non-DMS TIP I/O routine was modified to ensure that DBE is always connected to TIP before performing NON-DMS TIP I/O.

9.11.1.8 REWRITE Handler Modified

The REWRITE handler has been moved to serve as a front end for rewriting of both DMS and RDMS tables.

9.11.1.9 OPEN Command Enhanced

The syntax 'OPEN DBEFDT' will cause the DBE FDT file to be opened for the currently based UDS application.

9.11.1.10 DUMP reformatted

The DBE Dump handler has been reformatted to make DBE dumps more readable.

9.11.1.11 Double Buffered I/O routine change

The Double buffered I/O routine now requires the area page limits to be passed as parameters to allow the routine to work for both DMS and RDMS areas.

9.11.1.12 I/O Error hang corrected

An I/O error from the PAGE or SCAN function caused DBE to hang. This has been corrected by saving/restoring the return address.

9.11.1.13 DBE FDT File Macros Moved

DBE macros relased in level 7R1 in the Site library file have been moved to the standard system macro file due to an enhancement to the OPEN command allowing users without update privileges to update the DBE FDT file.

9.11.2 System Macro Changes

9.11.2.1 AREA-DDL

Fixed Calc Chain printout.

9.11.2.2 DMSCALC

Fixed calc chain location for manual sets.

9.11.2.3 EXPLAIN

Will now display a description of the I/O error encountered if EXPLAIN is called with no parameters and the last error encountered was an I/O error.

9.11.2.4 FITEM

Now handles Cartridge tape properly.

Assign options displayed as alpha characters instead of octal number.

9.11.2.5 PH

No longer attemts to decode Index area Page 2 for an initialized but empty Index area.

9.11.2.6 RDT

Corrected display of lower/upper page boundaries.

9.11.2.7 SAVE-ENV

Will save current application as well as RDMS area and page.

9.11.2.8 U$BSTE

Changed macro to read & display bank summary table entries individually to fix problems encountered when processing where large number of banks are configured.

9.11.2.9 U$FDT

Modified to use R$FDT as a front end to display FDT entries in the FDT$ file.

9.11.2.10 U$RFLE

Now displays max written in TRACKS and max tracks in file if TIP.

Displays thread number for any active RFLE.

'T' option added to display RFLE for a specified thread.

9.11.2.11 U$TST

Displays bank address for TST start.

9.11.2.12 U$TSTE

Displays bank address for TSTE start.

9.11.2.13 U$USE-COUNT

Offset to next entry calculation corrected.

9.11.2.14 WDDUMP

Corrected number of columns of data capable of being displayed.

9.11.3 New System Macros

9.11.3.1 High-Level Macros

9.11.3.1.1 CALCASE

Fetches a record stored using the CALCASE calc routine using a key supplied as a parameter to the macro (similar to DMSCALC macro).

9.11.3.1.2 CALCBOUNDS

Sets the system table CLCBND with lower/upper page limits passed as parameters for use with the RANDENTIAL function.

9.11.3.1.3 RANDENTIAL

Fetches a record stored using the RANDENTIAL calc routine using one or more keys supplied as parameters to the macro (similar to DMSCALC macro).

9.11.3.1.4 RAPT

Prints a formatted listing of an RDMS Allocation Page supplied as a parameter or the current Allocation Page if none supplied.

9.11.3.1.5 RAPTS

Produces a report of information contained in all Allocation Pages for the current RDMS area.

9.11.3.1.6 RFCP

Prints a formatted listing of the RDMS File Control Page for the current RDMS area.

9.11.3.1.7 RPH

Prints a formatted listing of the RDMS Page header for a page supplied as a parameter or the current page if none supplied.

9.11.3.1.8 RTREG

Prints a formatted listing of the RDMS TREG table.

9.11.3.1.9 R$ALLRECS

ALLRECS macro for RDMS page.

9.11.3.1.10 R$ALLSLOTS

ALLSLOTS macro for RDMS page.

9.11.3.1.11 R$BTREE

Displays pages in an RDMS BTREE from the root index page to the data pages.

9.11.3.1.12 R$DATA

DATA macro for RDMS page/record.

9.11.3.1.13 R$DUMPREC

DUMPREC macro for RDMS page/record.

9.11.3.1.14 R$NEXTREC

NEXTREC macro for RDMS page/record.

9.11.3.1.15 R$PGDUMP

PGDUMP macro for RDMS page.

9.11.3.1.16 R$RECSLOT

RECSLOT macro for RDMS page/record.

9.11.3.1.17 R$SCAN

The R$SCAN macro uses the RSCAN function to produce reports based on the following options:

 

R Record Counts

T Total Page Usage

D Data Page Usage

I Index Page Usage

L All of the above

9.11.3.1.18 R$SCAN-ALL

Calls R$SCAN for each RDMS area in an RDMS Schema/Group.

9.11.3.1.19 R$SLOTS

SLOTS macro for RDMS page.

9.11.3.1.20 U$RFL-LIST

Lists all TIP Retention file sizes along with their tip codes in decimal and octal for a UDS application.

9.11.3.1.21 U$RFL-LIST-A

Calls the U$RFL-LIST for each configured UDS application.

9.11.3.2 Subroutine Macros

9.11.3.2.1 R$$ANAME

Writes the current RDMS area name to the write buffer in the format:

 

QUAL*FILE for exec areas

TIP CODE (FCSS FILENAME) for TIP areas

If the "W" option is specified, the write buffer will be printed.

9.11.3.2.2 R$$AREAS

Writes all RDMS areas associated with a RDMS Schema name (passed as a parameter), masked by File name and Qualifier.

RDMS area names are obtained from the DBE FDT file.

9.11.3.2.3 R$$STATUS

This macro determines if an RDMS Area, Page, and Record are current.

9.11.3.2.4 R$$TABLE-LD

This macsub macro loads the two dimensional table DITEMS with byte offsets and field sizes for the current RDMS record.

9.11.4 New Commands

9.11.4.1 Non Table Commands

9.11.4.1.1 ABORT

Causes DBE to close and release all files and do an "ER EABT$" to abort a batch run.

9.11.4.1.2 RSCAN

Scans an RDMS area using the double buffered I/O routine, returning record counts, record sizes, and page usage information.

9.11.4.2 Table Invoking Commands

9.11.4.2.1 RAP

Bases an RDMS Allocation page table. If no parameter is specified, the current RAP will be displayed. If a parameter is passed, that RAP will be based.

9.11.4.2.2 RAREA

Bases an RDMS area and loads the RP1 and RFCP tables. If no parameter is passed, the current RDMS area is displayed.

 

For TIP files, the syntax is: RAREA ####

 

For EXEC files, the syntax is: RAREA QUAL*FILE

9.11.4.2.3 RPAGE

Bases an RDMS database page and loads the RRSLOT table. If no parameter is specified, the current RDMS page number will be displayed.

 

R option - Reread the current page from mass-storage.

X option - Base a page higher than the highest allocated.

RDMS Allocation Page.

RDMS Page.

The first 10 words of RPAGE.

9.11.6.8 RTREG

TREG information for current RDMS area if TIP.

9.11.7 New Functions

9.11.7.1 CALCASE

Returns page and chain for a passed calc key using the user written CALCASE calc database procedure.

9.11.7.2 RANDENTIAL

Returns page and chain for passed calc key(s) using the RANDENTIAL calc routine.

9.12. Level 8R2 - 14 JUN 91

9.12.1 Processor Changes

9.12.1.1 Error Changed when loading low RDMS pages

When loading an RDMS page lower than the first data page, the error "Page Header Inconsistency Error" has been changed to return the "Invalid Page Request" error.

9.12.1.2 RLSTPG variable contains wrong number

The cell read from the FITEM$ call has been changed to correctly return the highest page physically written.

9.12.1.3 P0 Rewrite error fixed

Attempts to rewrite the P0 table resulted in an E$117 error. This was due to an overwrite of the rewrite validation list (P0 is first entry).

9.12.1.4 P0 Rewrite returns Page Header Inconsistency error

Page header checking is now separate for P0 and other database pages.

9.12.1.5 RSCAN Function not returning correct results

The RSCAN function scanned pages up to the last page written to instead of the last page allocated. Pages in the unallocated portions lower than the last page written were reported on. Page usage percentage information was incorrect in the high unused space ranges.

The above RSCAN problems have all been corrected in this release.

9.12.1.6 SCAN

'L' option added to fill array # 4 (Overflow/Prime Page #) array with half-word entries instead of full-word entries.

9.12.2 System Macro Changes

9.12.2.1 PRT

No longer prints Maximum line message if the maximum line limit is not exceeded.

9.12.2.2 R$DUMPREC

Buffer pointer now updated correctly at macro termination.

9.12.2.3 R$NEXTREC

If current record is last on page, get next logical page and dump first record.

9.12.2.4 R$PGDUMP

Error corrected when dumping page with no unused space.

'U' option now required to dump unused space.

Deleted records now dumped in ASCII and octal with 'D' option.

9.12.2.5 R$SCAN

Now displays area sizing information if 'S' or 'L' option specified.

Displays number of FCP pages in TOTAL page histogram.

9.12.2.6 RFCP

Now displays BTREE root pages.

9.12.2.7 SCAN-ONE

Problem scanning very large areas corrected by change to SCAN function.

9.12.2.8 U$FDT-COPY

Expanded to capture additional FDT information.

Macro execution time reduced by walking logical pages instead of pre-scanning area with R$BTREE macro.

9.12.2.9 U$LOAD

QAD , TMP , TCS , DFT , ACW , DMPERR table loading added.

9.12.3 New System Macros

9.12.3.1 High-Level Macros

9.12.3.1.1 R$COUNT

Produces record counts by Btree.

9.12.3.1.2 R$FETCH

"Fetches" an RDMS record given index keys.

9.12.3.1.3 U$DFT

Dumps Dedicated File Table for a UDS application.

9.12.3.1.4 U$DFTE

Dumps Dedicated File Table Entries for a UDS application.

9.12.3.1.5 U$FDT-EXT

Creates an extract file of all FDT copy file entries for a given schema.

9.12.3.1.6 U$LOOK-RPT

Displays Quick-Look , After-Looks and Before-Look settings for a schema by interrogating the FDT copy file.

9.12.3.1.7 U$QAD

Dumps the Queuing and Deadlock table for a UDS application.

9.12.3.2 Subroutine Macros

9.12.3.2.1 R$$FIRSTPAGE

Returns the first Index or Data page for a specified BTREE in an RDMS area.

9.12.4 New System Variables

9.12.4.1 RLSTPA

Last RDMS page allocated in an RDMS area.

9.13. Level 8R2A - 28 JUN 91

9.13.1 Processor Changes

9.13.1.1 On G / Off G supported

Turning the "G" option on and off dynamically is now supported to allow] dynamic suppression of the DBE signoff line. Request" error.

every 500 pages. This prevents the "Max Log Entries Written" error.

9.13.2.2 U$TSTE

Current thread is displayed if thread number not passed as parameter.

"A" option added to allow U$TST to call U$TSTE and display all threads.

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

9.14. Level 8R3 - 15 NOV 91

9.14.1 Processor Changes

9.14.1.1 ATTSIZE Command

The ATTSIZE command was implemented to size the ATTBUF system table to a default value specified in the DBE gen stream.

9.14.1.2 KEYIN$ Handler

An ER KEYIN$ handler has been added to provide statistics while DBE is executing. The handler is activated via a "*<runid>" console keyin.

The KEYIN$ handler is enabled / disabled via a DBE sysgen parameter.

9.14.1.3 Logging Rewritten

DBE logging has been rewritten to allow logging either via "ER LOG$" , "ER SYSLOG$" or no logging via a DBE sysgen parameter. If logging is via "ER SYSLOG$" the log entry number is specified via the DBE sysgen.

Logging of "PUT" commands to DMS files or Sector Formatted Exec files has been added.

9.14.1.4 RDMS Checksum Calculation Fixed

The RDMS checksum calculation routine has been fixed to work on RDMS pages as well as the file control page and allocation pages.

9.14.1.5 REALTIME capability added

DBE now has the capability of running at realtime status. This is controlled via the "ON F" / "OFF F" commands.

REALTIME capability is enabled via a DBE sysgen parameter which also controls the realtime level.

9.14.1.6 REWIND Command

The REWIND command has been implemented to position tape reels back to load point instead of using the "POSITION 1" syntax.

9.14.1.7 @SYM Banner Supported on HARDCOPY Command

The HARDCOPY command now allows the @SYM banner id to be specified as the third field.

9.14.1.8 USAGE Command Enhanced

The USAGE command will now display the first character of each valid command as the usage prompt.

Entering "?" as the command will cause the usage commands and thier syntax to be printed.

Initializing a table will cause the user to answer an "Are You Sure" message.

9.14.2 System Macro Changes

9.14.2.1 DMSCALC

The DMSCALC macro will now automatically call the CALCASE macro if the record location mode is CALCASE instead of DMSCALC.

9.14.2.2 PAUSE

Entering a control card or "@EOF" as a response to the PAUSE macro caused the macro to error. This has been corrected.

9.14.2.3 RPH

The RPH macro has been changed to display the checksum value as word 05 instead of word 04.

9.14.2.4 SCAN-ONE

The 98LLOAD record produced by the SCAN-ONE macro has been changed to match the layout documented in the DBE User's Guide.

The number of prime pages is now obtained from P0 for darp areas to cure <51> errors in Index Sequential data areas.

Overlow pages on the free page chain are now treated as unallocated instead of 100% empty for histogram purposes.

Number of free chain pages is passed to SCAN$SIZE macro.

9.14.2.5 SCAN$SIZE

If the number of free chain pages passed from the SCAN-ONE macro is non-zero, the number will be used in the display of free chain pages instead of having the SCAN$SIZE macro walk the free chain again.

9.14.2.6 TOC

The "F" option has been added to the TOC macro to create a file in the format of the SGS statement "*ADD SGS FILE./ELT$".

9.14.2.7 U$ACT

The display of the application number in the U$ACT macro has been changed to correctly display the number of configured page banks and application number as half word entries.

9.14.2.8 U$ADT

The space reserved for a read of the ADT file was expanded to prevent array boundary violations when reading large ADT files / banks.

9.14.2.9 U$ALIAS

The "S" option was added to the U$ALIAS macro to create a file in SGS format containing alias names and thier corresponding application names.

The space reserved for a read of the ADT file was expanded to prevent array boundary violations when reading large ADT files / banks.

9.14.2.10 U$APP

The start address of the DCSD Index was hard coded in the U$APP macro. The macro has been changed to get the address from the current configuration in the system file.

9.14.2.11 U$READ-ADT

The start address of the common banked ADT entries was hard coded in the U$READ-ADT macro. The macro has been changed to dynamically determine the start of the ADT entries within the common bank.

9.14.2.12 U$TSTE

Changed display format of IR Sequence # and Step #.

9.14.3 New System Macros

9.14.3.1 AREA-ALL

Allows calling of a specified macro for each area in the current schema matching an optional area name mask.

9.14.3.2 ATT

Produces formatted listing / dumps of IRU audit trail tapes/disk files with search and record type selection support.

9.14.3.3 ATT-DUMP

Produces a formatted dump of the audit record made current by the ATT macro.

9.14.3.4 BRKPT$

Performs an "@BRKPT PRINT$/..." or "@BRKPT PRINT$" via csf call.

9.14.3.5 LOGBUF

Produces a formatted dump of the log packet and log buffer(s).

9.14.3.6 O-CHAIN

Displays overlflow pages chained to the current prime or overlow page.

9.14.3.7 PATCH-FREE-O

Creates DMU page patch commands to patch the page headers on the free page chain to point to page 0 instead of the original prime page.

9.14.3.8 R$CHECKSUM

Displays / Corrects checksums for an RDMS page, file control page or allocation page.

9.14.3.9 R$CHECKSUM-ONE

Calls R$HECKSUM macro for all or a range of pages in an RDMS area.

9.14.3.10 U$RFL-DUMP

Produces formatted dumps of UDS retention files.

9.14.4 Subrouine Macros

9.14.4.1 LDSL

Performs a "left double shift logical" on a two word array.

9.14.4.2 R$UPH

Treats the USRBUF system table as the RPH table to produce a formatted dump of the page header identical to the RPH macro.

9.14.4.3 SCHEMA-LOAD

Loads a schema passed as a parameter via acsf @ADD.

9.14.4.4 TDATE1

Returns DMS date/time stamp as YY MM DD HH MM SS.

9.14.4.5 TDATE2

Returns IRU audit date/time stamp as YY MM DD HH MM SS.

9.14.4.6 TDATE3

Returns 2 word DTIME$ as YY MM DD HH MM SS.

9.14.4.7 U-ART

Treats the USRBUF system table as the ART table to produce a formatted dump of the Area Reference Table identical to the ART macro.

9.14.4.8 UPH

Treats the USRBUF system table as the PH table to produce a formatted dump of the page header identical to the PH macro.

9.14.5 New System Variables

9.14.5.1 LOGBUF

The "ER LOG$" / "ER SYSLOG$" packet and log entry buffer.

9.14.5.2 LOGTYPE

Type of logging configured for DBE (FIELDATA, ASCII, NONE).

9.14.5.3 SYMID

Currently selected @SYM banner id as specified by the HARDCOPY command.

9.14.6 New Tables

9.14.6.1 ATTBUF

Audit Trail buffer, used by ATT related system macros.

This table is sized at 1 word until resized by the ATTSIZE command.

9.14.6.2 ATTCTL

Used by ATT system macros to determine ATTBUFF offset for the current audit record as well as trcaking audit trail media type and sector offsets for disk audit trails.

9.14.6.3 KEYBUF

Buffer used for a macro to pass information to the KEYIN$ handler.

9.14.7 New Error Codes

9.14.7.1 Error 180

<180> USER ACCOUNT DOES NOT ALLOW REALTIME STATUS

9.14.8 Sysgen Changes

9.14.8.1 ATT

ATT BUFFER DEFAULT SIZE IS <words> WORDS

9.14.8.2 KEYIN$

KEYIN$ HANDLER IS ENABLED

-or- KEYIN$ HANDLER IS DISABLED

9.14.8.3 LOGGING

LOGGING IS ENABLED VIA LOG$

-or- LOGGING IS ENABLED VIA SYSLOG$ ENTRY TYPE 200001

-or- LOGGING IS DISABLED

| Appendix B | Level 8R4 |

| Summary Of Changes | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

9.15. Level 8R4 - 03 SEP 92

9.15.1 Processor Changes

9.15.1.1 EXEC 43R4 Change

When attempting to run realtime under EXEC 43R4, DBE would get an IGDM error. This has been fixed by correctly loading the realtime level value instead of attempting to access protected memory.

9.15.1.2 AREA Command

Fixed code to clear current page when new area is based.

9.15.1.3 DECODE Command Enhanced / "Q" Processor Option

The DECODE command would error if it encountered an invalid area code in the pointer passed to it. The "Q" processor option was added to allow decode to return a value of zeros instead of erroring.

9.15.1.4 DOUBLE BUFFERED I/O Configuration Change

The size of the buffers used by the double buffered I/O routine (called by SCAN and RSCAN functions) are now configurable and can be specified at DBE SYSGEN time.

9.15.1.5 ERROR HANDLING Fixed

When the error handling routine checked to see if a SCAN was in progress, the register containing the return address was overlayed causing an IGDM error. This has been corrected by saving/restoring the register around the code.

9.15.1.6 FEATURE Command Implemented

Implemented FEATURE command which was documented but never coded.

9.15.1.7 LET Command Fix

Fixed code which caused E$31 errors following SCANs which encountered errors.

9.15.1.8 RSCAN Command Changes

RSCAN now correctly determines whether start/stop pages passed to it are valid.

All arrays passed to the RSCAN function are now monitored.

9.15.1.9 SCAN Command

Changed E$77 error handling to set a bit in ERRSTS table instead.

Added code to detect corrupted page offsets in record slots and to report the condition instead of causing an IGDM error.

Added code to detect record "bit-out" condition, invalid area code or page # in record set pointers.

Cleaned up/standardized error reporting.

9.15.2 System Macro Changes

9.15.2.1 ATT

ATT macro fixed to test queue item status before referencing undefined "qdate" variable.

Calculation of highest track fixed.

Code added to prevent binary find from entering an infinite loop.

9.15.2.2 FRT

FRT macro rewritten to use FRT/DBPDT system tables.

9.15.2.3 LINK

LINK macro changed to recognize an owner record type being encountered and to re-calculate the pointer offset for the set being walked.

9.15.2.4 REC-COUNT

REC-COUNT macro changed to call SCAN$COUNT subroutine macro to display record counts/sizes.

9.15.2.5 SCAN-ONE

SCAN-ONE macro fixed to call SCAN$SIZE macro only once.

Error handling cleaned up. If an error is detected, macro SCAN$ERRMSG will be attempted. This macro can be user written and should reside in the DBE Site Library File.

Average I/O rates were truncated if rates were very large. Macro now uses half words instead of quarter words to hold I/O rate information.

Dropped # of pages on free page chain from I/O calculations.

9.15.2.6 SIZE-REPORT

SIZE-REPORT enhanced to display total tracks used/available for all areas reported on.

9.15.2.7 U$GNLE

Added code to detect zero value in BDI field, indicating BDI of UDS global DBANK is to be used.

Fixed looping problem when TCS GNLE not found.

9.15.3 New System Macros

9.15.3.1 GED

Produces a formatted dump of the Global Encode Table.

9.15.3.2 RFT

Selects the correct FEATURE for the current record and calls the FRT macro.

9.15.3.3 STOC

Call the TOC macro for the current schema file.

9.15.4 Sysgen Changes

9.15.4.1 DOUBLE

DOUBLE BUFFERED IO SIZE IS <tracks> TRACKS

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Appendix B | Level 8R5 |

| Summary Of Changes | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

9.16. Level 8R5 - 09 OCT 92

9.16.1 Processor Changes

9.16.1.1 ABORT Command fixed

DBE would get an IGDM error when the ABORT command was executed. This has been fixed by first clearing the contingency handler.

9.16.1.2 SCAN Command Errors Enhanced

The SCAN command error display has been enhanced to display the area name being scanned when the first error is detected and after all errors for the area have been displayed.

9.16.1.3 ER PCTWT$ Changed

The ER PCTWT$ code has been rewritten to allow the ER number to be specified at DBE SYSGEN time. This prevents a problem whereby DBE could not be genned when a new level of EXEC dropped the equate for this ER.

9.16.2 System Macro Changes

9.16.2.1 SCAN-ONE

Changed dimension size of overflow array to correctly handle DARP areas which have pages on the free page chain.

9.16.2.2 U$APP

Error trap introduced to detect errors encountered when the UDS application group is down.

9.16.3 Sysgen Changes

9.16.3.1 PCT

PCT WRITE IS ENABLED WITH ER <ER-#>

-or- PCT WRITE IS DISABLED

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

| Summary Of Changes | |

:-------------------------------:--------------------------------:

9.17. Level 8R6 - 30 APR 93

9.17.1 Processor Changes

9.17.1.1 HISTOGRAM Command Enhanced

The HISTOGRAM command was enhanced to provide a cumulative percentage column when the "C" option is specified on the command call.

9.17.2 System Macro Changes

9.17.2.1 ATT$$22

Subroutine macro changed to make SFS page number displayed 1 relative.

9.17.2.2 ATT$$RTYPE

Macro changed to use user variable instead of system variable when displaying type of system log entry being processed.

9.17.2.3 ATT

"DUMP" parameter added to pass options from ATT to ATT-DUMP macro.

IO error 5 from read of very small mass-storage Audit Trails has been fixed.

Mass-Storage block size is now obtained from audit block header.

9.17.2.4 ATT-DUMP

Compacted After Looks will now be correctly broken out by the ATT-DUMP macro.

9.17.2.5 PGSLOT

The PGSLOT macro has been changed to correctly handle overflow pages whose prime pages have calc chains.

9.17.2.6 SCAN$SIZE

Reduced overflow pages in use by number of pages on Free Page Chain.

9.17.2.7 SCAN-ONE

Extra page ejects when executing "SCAN-ONE,R" have been eliminated.

9.17.2.8 SIZE-REPORT

Report headings lined up.

"Q" option added to allow walking/counting of Free Page Chain to be skipped.

9.17.2.9 U$ACT

U$ACT macro enhanced to support UDS 5R1. If UDS level is less than 5R1, the U$ACT-4R1 macro will be called.

9.17.2.10 U$BST

U$BST macro enhanced to support UDS 5R1. If UDS level is less than 5R1, the U$BST-4R1 macro will be called.

9.17.2.11 U$FDT

U$FDT macro enhanced to support UDS 5R1. If UDS level is less than 5R1, the U$FDT-4R1 macro will be called.

9.17.2.12 U$FPTE

U$FPTE macro enhanced to support UDS 5R1. If UDS level is less than 5R1, the U$FPTE-4R1 macro will be called.

9.17.2.13 U$GNLE

U$GNLE macro enhanced to support UDS 5R1. If UDS level is less than 5R1, the U$GNLE-4R1 macro will be called.

9.17.2.14 U$INDEX

U$INDEX macro enhanced to support UDS 5R1. If UDS level is less than 5R1, the U$INDEX-4R1 macro will be called.

9.17.2.15 U$LSS

U$LSS macro enhanced to support UDS 5R1. If UDS level is less than 5R1, the U$LSS-4R1 macro will be called.

9.17.2.16 U$RFL

U$RFL macro enhanced to support UDS 5R1. If UDS level is less than 5R1, the U$RFL-4R1 macro will be called.

9.17.2.17 U$TET

U$TET macro enhanced to support UDS 5R1. If UDS level is less than 5R1, the U$TET-4R1 macro will be called.

9.17.2.18 U$TSTE

U$TSTE macro enhanced to support UDS 5R1. If UDS level is less than 5R1, the U$TSTE-4R1 macro will be called.

9.17.3 New System Macros

9.17.3.1 AREA-PCT

Produces a report of Area Names/Codes/Sizes sortable by file size.

9.17.3.2 CALCSLOT

Similar to RECSLOT macro, performs a DUMPREC for the record pointed to by a specified calc chain header.

9.17.3.3 CALCLOTS

Dumps Calc Chain Header slots at the bottom of a prime page.

9.17.3.4 U$ACT-4R1

U$ACT macro for UDS levels 4R1 and lower (called by U$ACT macro).

9.17.3.5 U$BST-4R1

U$BST macro for UDS levels 4R1 and lower (called by U$BST macro).

U$FDT macro for UDS levels 4R1 and lower (called by U$FDT macro).

U$GNLE macro for UDS levels 4R1 and lower (called by U$GNLE macro).

9.18. Level 8R7 - 01 JUN 93

9.18.1.1 REWRITE Command Enhanced

9.19. Level 8R8 - 17 JUN 93

9.19.1 Processor Changes

9.19.1.1 IGDM When SCANning mixed EXEC/TIP Schemas Fixed

The IGDM error encountered when scanning an EXEC database area using a schema which resides in a TIP file has been corrected.
